### content/gittin/69.txt
<a id="src-00140"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/69.txt`

Gittin 69 - Talmud remedies
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj92xgdmkvHTw4Zcfla5IdaWiY8llmuuOJRnNLa7gG_9ZdE-ZS2EMAIW6-4dq0GEPyNzyqxAVzFGfUQc_zDg7OQLvoBolETStDQR_lVMpj4RBWvc4F0s62O6QPnym5CdOplFVgXYW3Gud2x/s1600-h/gittin69.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5247451066178710946" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj92xgdmkvHTw4Zcfla5IdaWiY8llmuuOJRnNLa7gG_9ZdE-ZS2EMAIW6-4dq0GEPyNzyqxAVzFGfUQc_zDg7OQLvoBolETStDQR_lVMpj4RBWvc4F0s62O6QPnym5CdOplFVgXYW3Gud2x/s320/gittin69.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>Many remedies are recorded in the Talmud. One can not use them nowadays because we are not certain of the exact meaning of the words and because the nature of people and medicines has changed. Here is one such remedy.<br />
<br />
For cataracts – bring a scorpion that is spotted with seven colors because of its age, dry it out in the shade, grind it, and make a powder consisting of two parts antimony and one part ground scorpion. Apply three doses to one eye and three doses to another. One must beware not to apply more, or the eyes may burst.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Alchemist by William Fettes Douglas&nbsp;</div>

---

### content/gittin/7.txt
<a id="src-00141"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/7.txt`

Gittin 7 – To fight the bad or not to fight
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiV-2cssP-FaGpIAuJzvS3DNR3qQbhdUQ_oYZkx-GT-MTg0lGBrQPgdxZQvKbcALst7CEqnx5gJt3VRlVkipLldgMrCCFQDFo-qhN-B7TGmPaFlX6mJAyMhQyfFuZMkW3Ba2hlk73zP88Jn/s1600/Wedding+Dance+by+Pieter+Brueghel+the+Younger.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="222" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiV-2cssP-FaGpIAuJzvS3DNR3qQbhdUQ_oYZkx-GT-MTg0lGBrQPgdxZQvKbcALst7CEqnx5gJt3VRlVkipLldgMrCCFQDFo-qhN-B7TGmPaFlX6mJAyMhQyfFuZMkW3Ba2hlk73zP88Jn/s320/Wedding+Dance+by+Pieter+Brueghel+the+Younger.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
One should never be too assertive with the members of his household; if he is, they will lie to him out of fear and lead him to multiple sins. For example, Rabbi Chanina ben Gamliel used to put fear into his servants, and they fed him a prohibited thing. What happened? A part of a properly slaughtered animal was lost, and they substituted it with another cut from a live animal. 
<br />
<br />
But is it possible that a righteous Rabbi Chanina would eat anything not kosher? God watches even over the animals of the righteous, like in the story where a donkey would not eat food from which tithe was not separated; how much more so over the righteous themselves? – True, they wanted to feed him a prohibited item, but something prevented this.
<br />
<br />
Mar Ukva sent a question to Rabbi Elazar, "There are bad people who hurt me, and I can give them away to the government, should I?" Rabbi Elazar took out a piece of parchment, made lines for writing, and wrote, "<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt2639.htm">Let me not do wrong with my mouth with an evil person is in front of me</a>." Mar Ukva replied, "But they are torturing me!" Rabbi Elazar then wrote, "<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt2637.htm">Be silent unto God, and the enemies will disappear.</a>" Rabbi Elazar's words took effect right away, and the enemies of Mar Ukva were led away in chains.
<br />
<br />
The Talmud then discusses why, according to Mar Ukva, a meal can be accompanied by joyous music only if it is a meal connected to a mitzvah, as well as other signs of diminished joy, decreed after the destruction of the Temple. 
<br />
<br />
Art: Wedding Dance by Pieter Brueghel the Younger

---

### content/gittin/70.txt
<a id="src-00142"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/70.txt`

Gittin 70 - Healthy living
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIze5NSH8i9XFdnt_pYH8RBeEgzNCOFIQ7Rd45jq32kl4LoDoRqPptsCEzM-itT0rbDkgVSPY-KM8_VqZexd-RIy_FIOKc8LG2zJtKVEBVIWTvMxTtQtjaRq0_lw9INz8-87zOThwKk6F5/s1600-h/gittin70.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5247856313964924802" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIze5NSH8i9XFdnt_pYH8RBeEgzNCOFIQ7Rd45jq32kl4LoDoRqPptsCEzM-itT0rbDkgVSPY-KM8_VqZexd-RIy_FIOKc8LG2zJtKVEBVIWTvMxTtQtjaRq0_lw9INz8-87zOThwKk6F5/s320/gittin70.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>Healthy living: eat 1/3 of the stomach's capacity, drink 1/3, and leave 1/3 of the stomach's capacity unfilled. If you get angry after a meal, you will be filled to capacity but not become ill.<br />
<br />
One who is impotent should bring 3 vessels of 3 reviit (~3 ounces) of saffron that grew in a field fertilized with sheep manure, grind them up, boil them in wine, and drink. Rabbi Yochanan said, “It is exactly this which made me like a teenager again.”<br />
<br />
Three things drain a person's strength: anxiety, travel, and regret of sin.<br />
<br />
<div>
Art:&nbsp;Still Life With Cheese Fruit Olive Bread By Floris Van Dyck Repro</div>

---

### content/gittin/71.txt
<a id="src-00143"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/71.txt`

Gittin 71 - A deaf-mute
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgceNOviOuhQoAUrTuH0bXvXxj17IjM667i7umuNnlab443HvGewGKpKrpQq0GMMH5eIN2o72qIyNQyaWoNZR9lvpjFZMbybe6OF26EF0JD_lUgrsuSLu5LQ3rLlx2g7xRjFYJ74UrypbkI/s1600-h/Clef10_Steen_OudeVrijerJongeMeid_1665.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5248340507593388466" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgceNOviOuhQoAUrTuH0bXvXxj17IjM667i7umuNnlab443HvGewGKpKrpQq0GMMH5eIN2o72qIyNQyaWoNZR9lvpjFZMbybe6OF26EF0JD_lUgrsuSLu5LQ3rLlx2g7xRjFYJ74UrypbkI/s320/Clef10_Steen_OudeVrijerJongeMeid_1665.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If one became mute and they asked him, "Shall we write a get for your wife?" and he nodded his head, they should test him six times with questions requiring "yes" or "no" in random order. If he answers all questions correctly, they may write and give a get.<br />
<br />
A person born deaf-mute is presumed to lack clear understanding and can not contract a biblically binding marriage. Rabbinical enactments validated his marriage and divorce. Therefore, if his brother marries a woman and dies, and the wife falls to him in a levirate marriage, he lacks the legal power to divorce.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Old Suitor - Young Girl by Jan Steen</div>

---

### content/gittin/72.txt
<a id="src-00144"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/72.txt`

Gittin 72 - Conditional Divorce
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhruRAvI2f4IYI2YwbDqrYjX5sfYo6dHoRHc852xRlEbiG4hA5oqWNKBvS8Gh8V7GwP-v902GNSNhxpEu9GPUHV8D-zSyYfqcEik_MhFt08eQnOIH0ZpggpaZ-eyln0gcxVgEYcLuupusSL/s1600-h/carolus-duran_001.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5248496048515940258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhruRAvI2f4IYI2YwbDqrYjX5sfYo6dHoRHc852xRlEbiG4hA5oqWNKBvS8Gh8V7GwP-v902GNSNhxpEu9GPUHV8D-zSyYfqcEik_MhFt08eQnOIH0ZpggpaZ-eyln0gcxVgEYcLuupusSL/s320/carolus-duran_001.JPG" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If a husband told his wife, “This is your Get if I die,” or, “This is your Get if I die from this illness,” or “This is your Get after my death,” he has not said anything. In all three cases, the Get is void because the husband stipulated  that it would take effect after his death, and this is impossible.<br />
<br />
If he said, “This is your Get from today if I die from this illness,” - it is a valid Get. It takes effect retroactively, but care must be taken not to invalidate the Get by living together.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;<span style="background-color: white; color: #050505; font-family: Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; white-space-collapse: preserve;">The Convalescent by Carolus-Duran</span></div>

---

### content/gittin/73.txt
<a id="src-00145"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/73.txt`

Gittin 73 - Results of Conditional Divorce
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjKRH1WV1HU_tHEPNf6jXGuEGxIPHJhQc9vimAvaJf6QIsGcsHl9_R6lenl7A7m8wIp8Bfo_a3R1yszcmZ_R4xLOxnaaSg_gM-XrHILekpgvqzEB8DaVxmIKc4gz9LahTFX0RoJ5twj8PN/s1600-h/Modigliani+Bride+and+Groom.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5249006835417369106" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjKRH1WV1HU_tHEPNf6jXGuEGxIPHJhQc9vimAvaJf6QIsGcsHl9_R6lenl7A7m8wIp8Bfo_a3R1yszcmZ_R4xLOxnaaSg_gM-XrHILekpgvqzEB8DaVxmIKc4gz9LahTFX0RoJ5twj8PN/s320/Modigliani+Bride+and+Groom.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">The Get of a seriously ill person has the same law as his gift; if he recovers, it is assumed that he changed his mind. The possession of the gift returns to him, and the Get should be void. However, the Get is decreed to take effect to avoid people thinking that the Get can work after the husband’s death. Such a mistake could lead to serious consequences.<br />
<br />
After receiving a conditional Get, the wife should not be alone with her husband unless it is in the presence of witnesses – even witnesses not normally qualifying to give testimony.</span><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Bride and Groom by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Modigliani&nbsp;</span></div>

---

### content/gittin/74.txt
<a id="src-00146"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/74.txt`

Gittin 74 - Divorce on Condition of Payment
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEizJAiVYGup7F54qaZnESSfxYDD-k3gLrk5GX2sZZYUCmK2Tlm4h2R-nf4_spPdwuR7fg5_t5ycv_X7DBe8CdxYF6cxRS8ZAOoLHTYFs22F1fZJqgEES-LeupItf_MS5g95Cfr5kgEvuQ6h/s1600-h/Kauffman+Isidor+-+A+Business+Transaction.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5249277586347818098" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEizJAiVYGup7F54qaZnESSfxYDD-k3gLrk5GX2sZZYUCmK2Tlm4h2R-nf4_spPdwuR7fg5_t5ycv_X7DBe8CdxYF6cxRS8ZAOoLHTYFs22F1fZJqgEES-LeupItf_MS5g95Cfr5kgEvuQ6h/s320/Kauffman+Isidor+-+A+Business+Transaction.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If a man tells his wife, "This is your Get on condition that you give me 200 zuz coins (~$10,000)," then she is divorced, and the Get takes effect retroactively to the time of giving the Get at the moment when she gives the money. Therefore, if the Get is meanwhile lost or destroyed, it still works.<br />
<br />
If he said, "On condition that you give me the money within 30 days," - then if she gave him the money within 30 days, she is divorced, but if not, she is not divorced.<br />
<br />
If he says, "On condition that you give me a certain garment," and the garment is lost - she is not divorced. Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel says that she can pay money for the garment, as it once happened in the city of Tzidon, but this is one of <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/09/daf-in-100-words-gittin-74-divorce-for.html">the</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/02/bava-batra-174-lender-and-guarantor.html">three</a> cases where the law does not follow him.</span><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">A Business Transaction by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Isidor&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Kauffman</span></div>

---

### content/gittin/75.txt
<a id="src-00147"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/75.txt`

Gittin 75 - Contracts Based on Unfulfilled Conditions
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEibsp7P5N0tmW4Gm_bswZwEGaBYlqSxSsPNpYwBt4npYDvMfPr_Gtd28ixhk30JrW1lPS-5YxvaO-bQUGeKAbW6vNAFQGj7ByqU3TBeI9EEZSrYbk9F3lJ9-6S1yF7weX4RlBZmS9AN2L_8/s1600-h/gittin75.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5249686763751449938" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEibsp7P5N0tmW4Gm_bswZwEGaBYlqSxSsPNpYwBt4npYDvMfPr_Gtd28ixhk30JrW1lPS-5YxvaO-bQUGeKAbW6vNAFQGj7ByqU3TBeI9EEZSrYbk9F3lJ9-6S1yF7weX4RlBZmS9AN2L_8/s320/gittin75.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>A man said to his sharecropper, "Sharecroppers usually water the field three times a year and take one-fourth of the produce as payment for their work. However, you will water four times a year and take one-third of the crop." The sharecropper accepted the proposal. Eventually, the rain came and made it unnecessary to water the crops for the fourth time.<br />
<br />
One side: since the sharecropper did not actually irrigate a fourth time, only one-quarter of the produce is due him. Another: since irrigating the fourth time was unnecessary, the sharecropper takes one-third. The second point of view is preferred.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Landscape with Conversing Peasants by&nbsp;Pieter de Molyn</div>

---

### content/gittin/76.txt
<a id="src-00148"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/76.txt`

Gittin 76 - Divorce for Services
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQskLc3p-J_hrMIaYf2hrTE198ChjEEv1RaTzMSXAnvqdIMw2Hbo006fgBUq7v1CsEbwNmvcLbIJj_LGTHknjAZjUQ5fRhe2_YiUfzx6orAnSp5g6qRmKrnugIyKn66K9EprW70hrnxaCr/s1600-h/philippe-de-champaigne_cardinal-richelieu-on-his-deathbed.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5250154140848354002" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQskLc3p-J_hrMIaYf2hrTE198ChjEEv1RaTzMSXAnvqdIMw2Hbo006fgBUq7v1CsEbwNmvcLbIJj_LGTHknjAZjUQ5fRhe2_YiUfzx6orAnSp5g6qRmKrnugIyKn66K9EprW70hrnxaCr/s200/philippe-de-champaigne_cardinal-richelieu-on-his-deathbed.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If a husband told his wife, “This is your Get on condition that your take care of my father,” and the father died, - it is a valid Get. The condition was based on need, and the need was fulfilled.<br />
<br />
If a man told his wife, “This is your Get on condition that you nurse my son for two years,” and the son died, the <span>Get is void</span>. The husband wanted to harass her and failed. <span>Other</span><span>s say</span> that the husband wanted to profit and that the <span>Get is valid</span>. Practically, we rule stringently, but they should have been more specific!<div><br /></div><div>Art: Cardinal Richelieu on his Deathbed by Philippe de Champaigne</div>

---

### content/gittin/77.txt
<a id="src-00149"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/77.txt`

Gittin 77 - He Throws Her the Get
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRRWLNQlz3qlc5N-_35pxTAie7gb3ToryRUEftIApgJ3ccd7D8NEfVqBumRgiNbCLtCXxtNm87FMpnkVn0EwREMrdDNccw4gQQ1CyGFxzV_C6QgyaKvDM533A3LnC2lrwSVnPAj6KsBno3/s1600-h/Vermeer+Elinga.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5250395774646554722" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRRWLNQlz3qlc5N-_35pxTAie7gb3ToryRUEftIApgJ3ccd7D8NEfVqBumRgiNbCLtCXxtNm87FMpnkVn0EwREMrdDNccw4gQQ1CyGFxzV_C6QgyaKvDM533A3LnC2lrwSVnPAj6KsBno3/s320/Vermeer+Elinga.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If someone throws a Get to his wife while she is inside her house or inside her courtyard, she is divorced because her property has acquired the Get for her. If he threw the Get while she was inside his house, even if the Get is with her in the same bed, - she is not divorced because the Get has not been placed in her domain.<br />
<br />
If he threw the Get into her lap or into her sewing basket hanging from her, she would be divorced.<br />
<br />
Later authorities prohibited divorcing a wife without her consent.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Interior with Painter, Woman Reading, and Maid Sweeping - Pieter Janssens</div>

---

### content/gittin/78.txt
<a id="src-00150"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/78.txt`

Gittin 78 - Tricks to Give a Get
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-9XhPZXULTO1k-yIu_QA1xD_Mwp0gnrLU0z-DgTBDu16MdveSjVg72D5EUWt3VhsZqtLrv6n8layO64U30UN_m1JU-hJj4oLPjQSHFXUfge17AyDCK_zRaAfk23A-SXzQChfI8U8tYkNP/s1600-h/Domenico+Fetti+-+Sleeping+Girl.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5250922516958225890" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi-9XhPZXULTO1k-yIu_QA1xD_Mwp0gnrLU0z-DgTBDu16MdveSjVg72D5EUWt3VhsZqtLrv6n8layO64U30UN_m1JU-hJj4oLPjQSHFXUfge17AyDCK_zRaAfk23A-SXzQChfI8U8tYkNP/s200/Domenico+Fetti+-+Sleeping+Girl.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If a man handed a Get to his wife and said, “Please receive this note of indebtedness,” or she found a document next to him, read it, and it was a Get – it is not a valid Get until he says to her, “Here is your Get.”<br />
<br />
If he placed it in her hand while she was sleeping, and she awakes, and it is her  Get, - it is not a valid Get.<br />
<br />
If she stood in the street and he threw the Get to her, she would be divorced if it landed close to her. Otherwise, she is not divorced.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Sleeping Girl by Domenico Fetti</div>

---

### content/gittin/79.txt
<a id="src-00151"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/79.txt`

Gittin 79 - Get is Thrown from the Roof
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4eXT73vTe1yuQeC2IM7UUGvN62tfqNx_ucqYwNAEUnQtN4RG4v6jW0ZkSeCWPNFpqihg399mX-RC4ekOol0M2FaaS3-3nfKgey91rkilPpM4MmykLglzQ7iDLzOi95UlJFmBvbJ1JxXMh1cndd29G4AmjJ4vXkhJZDwHuoVnCG98bkH2cSW9gxXTQdkBX/s800/Anton_Gunther_Gheringh_or_Jacob_Balthasar_Peeters_-_View_through_an_Architectural_Setting,_Courtyard_at_Rubens'_House.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="615" data-original-width="800" height="246" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4eXT73vTe1yuQeC2IM7UUGvN62tfqNx_ucqYwNAEUnQtN4RG4v6jW0ZkSeCWPNFpqihg399mX-RC4ekOol0M2FaaS3-3nfKgey91rkilPpM4MmykLglzQ7iDLzOi95UlJFmBvbJ1JxXMh1cndd29G4AmjJ4vXkhJZDwHuoVnCG98bkH2cSW9gxXTQdkBX/s320/Anton_Gunther_Gheringh_or_Jacob_Balthasar_Peeters_-_View_through_an_Architectural_Setting,_Courtyard_at_Rubens'_House.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>If she was standing on top of a roof that belonged to her and he threw the Get from the courtyard that belonged to him - once it reached the airspace of the roof, she would be divorced.<br />
<br />
If he was on his roof above and she was in her courtyard below, and he threw the Get to her, once it leaves the domain of the roof – even if it is erased or burnt before it lands in the courtyard – she is divorced.<br />
<br />
After the Get is written, the husband and wife can not be alone together.<div><br /></div><div>Art: View through an Architectural Setting, Courtyard at Rubens' House by Anton Gunther Gheringh or Jacob Balthasar Peeters</div>

---

### content/gittin/8.txt
<a id="src-00152"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/8.txt`

Gittin 8 – What is the difference between a ship and a flower pot?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh8VOITfLMgIlBfqMNIYHAkkCOZw_KjDc12lRL7iSE9rX8Y1_8gNyNBx0ThrdVIYZrgjWPZQfgRUlfbHr0BKq5RvJXVbYeGT9cvVLeznYvIWRpLs0b1Av1eXt7fQMyN_3FlCAUNWUcDFnON/s1600/Ships+Close+Inshore+at+Low+Tide+by+Willem+van+de%252C+the+Younger+Velde.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="282" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh8VOITfLMgIlBfqMNIYHAkkCOZw_KjDc12lRL7iSE9rX8Y1_8gNyNBx0ThrdVIYZrgjWPZQfgRUlfbHr0BKq5RvJXVbYeGT9cvVLeznYvIWRpLs0b1Av1eXt7fQMyN_3FlCAUNWUcDFnON/s320/Ships+Close+Inshore+at+Low+Tide+by+Willem+van+de%252C+the+Younger+Velde.jpg" width="320" /></a><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/12/gittin-2-messenger-of-divorce.html">We saw</a> that a messenger bringing a divorce document (Get) from outside of Israel must confirm that he saw it being written and signed. The Talmud also discusses which neighboring cities and areas are still considered the Land of Israel for this purpose and which are not. Would writing a Get on a ship close to Israel be regarded the same as on land? 
<br />
<br />
Finally, is a ship the same as a flower pot? We mean the laws of tithes. Anything that grows on a ship does not directly draw sustenance from the Land of Israel, and anything that grows in a hanging pot does not do this either, so at first glance, they should be the same. But perhaps this is not so: a ship constantly moves and thus cannot be considered connected to the ground, but a stable pot can. Or the opposite is true: the air divides between the pot and the earth, so the pot does not draw sustenance from the earth and is not liable to tithes, but a ship is in the water, which can be considered as a continuation of the water bed, and so maybe it is liable to tithes.
<br />
<br />
Art: Ships Close Inshore at Low Tide by Willem van de, the Younger Velde

---

### content/gittin/80.txt
<a id="src-00153"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/80.txt`

Gittin 80 - Errors in Get
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7Xfp_Myz_qApKV_V_9ZmAjstUHSyJwYw0z6BuT5r8BR5fGTzWOs9P5wkmaMCHUp1Pk1-T3YdSfKd79t0R6tZgL2mHUbkdYaWhGzBTN6b5JWlhIc0zurwsMHBpfrKEcGmwXAR2oz3KKJcLyYyiDim4oho-2fyTbuOMRp2Ih144bRkt9tEeyX5DkHqSZ9QO/s1122/Bathsheba_Receiving_David's_Letter_by_Jan_Steen.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1122" data-original-width="863" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7Xfp_Myz_qApKV_V_9ZmAjstUHSyJwYw0z6BuT5r8BR5fGTzWOs9P5wkmaMCHUp1Pk1-T3YdSfKd79t0R6tZgL2mHUbkdYaWhGzBTN6b5JWlhIc0zurwsMHBpfrKEcGmwXAR2oz3KKJcLyYyiDim4oho-2fyTbuOMRp2Ih144bRkt9tEeyX5DkHqSZ9QO/s320/Bathsheba_Receiving_David's_Letter_by_Jan_Steen.jpg" width="246" /></a></div>If one deviated from the rules of a Get, such as being in Babylon, dating it according to the calendar of Rome or Greece, or even dating it from the construction or destruction of the Temple, or incorrectly naming the city of writing, the Get is invalid.<br />
<br />
According to Rabbi Meir, the woman must leave her new husband if she re-married but can not return to her previous husband. She also loses her Ketubah payment from both and many other benefits.<br />
<br />
However, the prevailing ruling is that she does need another Get but is not penalized as above.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Bathsheba Receiving David's Letter by Jan Steen</div>

---

### content/gittin/81.txt
<a id="src-00154"></a>

Gittin 81 - Change of Mind about the Get
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjk86RIIphksjZHB9cOZD-4r5xDXlsEZlf5PIjI2yN16r0Sx9r7-0KVvXUWpprsaVibBHw6Ss0lGzz7PSNpDS1W9Qyj5gPcrpybYT72qXqv5DTfsOpt63tBakaIY4cCjzxcGO_LFLEVhFpE/s1600-h/Isra%C3%ABls-A_Jewish_Wedding-1903.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5252414254862993298" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjk86RIIphksjZHB9cOZD-4r5xDXlsEZlf5PIjI2yN16r0Sx9r7-0KVvXUWpprsaVibBHw6Ss0lGzz7PSNpDS1W9Qyj5gPcrpybYT72qXqv5DTfsOpt63tBakaIY4cCjzxcGO_LFLEVhFpE/s200/Isra%C3%ABls-A_Jewish_Wedding-1903.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If one wrote a Get for his wife and then changed his mind before delivering the Get, Beit Shammai says she is somewhat like a divorcee and can not marry a Kohen later.<br />
<br />
However, Beit Hillel says that even if he gave her a Get conditionally and the condition was never met, she can still marry a Kohen if her husband dies.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Jewish Wedding by Joseph Israels</div>

### content/gittin/82.txt
<a id="src-00155"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/82.txt`

Gittin 82 - Get is Complete Severance
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipHvc-v3Mv81ULJFkzQxCpRzBcM1pyNFOfhOtPXLxL_dVM-Fn2Tsy1ieJQ_sD2gH5X_8l4wxPWWgHHawSGu3i4HnaHFyJ-tmJUzuCvVTmzhcaMzM_SXZ1h7UCidsBHDZvIlTA2UpoudHfS/s1600-h/A-Seated-Woman-In-An-Interior-Gazing-Out-Of-The-Window.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5252418298624651586" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipHvc-v3Mv81ULJFkzQxCpRzBcM1pyNFOfhOtPXLxL_dVM-Fn2Tsy1ieJQ_sD2gH5X_8l4wxPWWgHHawSGu3i4HnaHFyJ-tmJUzuCvVTmzhcaMzM_SXZ1h7UCidsBHDZvIlTA2UpoudHfS/s320/A-Seated-Woman-In-An-Interior-Gazing-Out-Of-The-Window.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>To be effective, a Get must completely sever the marital relationship between the husband and the wife.<br />
<br />
If one divorces his wife and says to her, "You are hereby permitted to any man but so-and-so," she is not divorced. What should he do? He should take the Get from  her, give it to her again, and say, "You are hereby permitted to any man."<br />
<br />
But if he wrote this restriction into the Get itself, although he later erased it, the Get is invalid since it never was a "document of severance."<div><br /></div><div><div>Art: A Seated Woman in an Interior Gazing out of the Window by Thomas Wyck</div></div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/gittin/83.txt
<a id="src-00156"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/83.txt`

Gittin 83 - No Strings Attached to the Get!
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSnShpTR3fgBNY5mJkfxa-ScdIAz1nAJHLecJvkHldg8FU3rUqQy1NKIsUQUhTmH_sddvhe3eKfAAAxUKPAtsvkLZLwv0U2UKwX8VTK9y7_T5YUfyunonyuDvEzgfvrX_VCLGTYE43vBiX/s1600-h/rembrandt.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5252662598193882786" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSnShpTR3fgBNY5mJkfxa-ScdIAz1nAJHLecJvkHldg8FU3rUqQy1NKIsUQUhTmH_sddvhe3eKfAAAxUKPAtsvkLZLwv0U2UKwX8VTK9y7_T5YUfyunonyuDvEzgfvrX_VCLGTYE43vBiX/s320/rembrandt.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>Rabbi Eliezer validated a Get with a condition "You are permitted to marry any man but so-and-so." Rabbi Eliezer's learning was supreme, but many Rabbis reunited to disprove his teaching after his death. However, all but one of their rebuttals had potential flaws.<br />
<br />
The indisputable proof came from Rabbi Elazar ben Azaria. He deduced the requirement of complete severance from the term that the Torah used, "Kritut," instead of a possible shorter word, "Karet." According to Rabbi Elazar Ben Azaria, this teaches that temporary conditions in the Get are valid but not permanent ones.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Portrait of an Old Man by Rembrandt</div>

---

### content/gittin/84.txt
<a id="src-00157"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/84.txt`

Gittin 84 - Giving Wives as Gifts
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOKy1QDjKKED-7x2SSyAXY_fRQwK1xwIvTb4AJPXFARybGXfnDhkW3Spny_k-06Ut0VaOosd1BjqbGuREI6bdg3r-NpRRNfMeHLKJ9u6VohxewLVmE8d8BhCBL1lL_n2wPHoapRb72OL0V/s1600-h/Vittorio+Matteo+Corcos+-+An+elegant+Woman+at+St_+Malo.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5253507392943987906" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOKy1QDjKKED-7x2SSyAXY_fRQwK1xwIvTb4AJPXFARybGXfnDhkW3Spny_k-06Ut0VaOosd1BjqbGuREI6bdg3r-NpRRNfMeHLKJ9u6VohxewLVmE8d8BhCBL1lL_n2wPHoapRb72OL0V/s320/Vittorio+Matteo+Corcos+-+An+elegant+Woman+at+St_+Malo.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If a man gives his wife a Get on condition that she marries so-and-so, she should not marry so-and-so because it looks like giving wives as gifts. If she does marry, she need not divorce. She should not marry others because this may invalidate the Get.<br />
<br />
"On condition that you have relations with so-and-so" is valid because she can bribe him to marry her for a time. "On condition that you have relations with my father, or your father" is invalid because she can not bribe the father, so it is to vex her, and the Get is valid.<br /><br /><div>Art: An Elegant Woman at St. Malo by Vittorio Matteo Corcos&nbsp;</div>

---

### content/gittin/85.txt
<a id="src-00158"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/85.txt`

Gittin 85 - Get with Unusual Conditions
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj1E69w8j9GIkXgRi7nqtBAGFdWq37NFRcpwaEjsSXlBOhfB-3vGtrEcAhheXLMB4K_hQ39aWWB1KbNXM-YIdC52PJ4wibYM8ai7PabfuXEMCvMQGLxD2LO9Cjye1phPN9Mi666IoNjYd6x/s1600-h/eleonora_von_toledo.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5253535130597149426" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj1E69w8j9GIkXgRi7nqtBAGFdWq37NFRcpwaEjsSXlBOhfB-3vGtrEcAhheXLMB4K_hQ39aWWB1KbNXM-YIdC52PJ4wibYM8ai7PabfuXEMCvMQGLxD2LO9Cjye1phPN9Mi666IoNjYd6x/s320/eleonora_von_toledo.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If one gives his wife a Get and says, "You are hereby permitted to any man except to my father or your father," or “to a slave or an idolater,” the divorce is valid since her marriage to any of these men would not be binding.<br />
<br />
But what if the husband makes a condition that she can not marry a particular minor? At present, the minor can not marry, but eventually, he will become an adult. By comparison with a minor girl who can divorce, because eventually she will marry as an adult, the Get above is declared not complete separation, thus void.<br />
<br />
<div>
Art:&nbsp;Eleanor of Toledo. Portrait by Agnolo Bronzino.</div>

---

### content/gittin/86.txt
<a id="src-00159"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/86.txt`

Gittin 86 - Three Gittin are Invalid
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh-Uun1NHkjaVMYoPC3fccw3FZ8kX8jQuyVf5bDco_0kDZTYmh7RbkNnzBFOaWnfViogajKuyWKJHK0U1T1GudqRf9678GUuf__OatL3okH9qiyw3S975bDw1vNr8rgOAZ3qR4kEQILoxJQ/s1600-h/Peace-With-Honour-Queen-Victoria-With-Benjamin-Disraeli--Following-The-Signing-Of-The-Berlin-Treaty-In-1878.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5253826178432957762" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh-Uun1NHkjaVMYoPC3fccw3FZ8kX8jQuyVf5bDco_0kDZTYmh7RbkNnzBFOaWnfViogajKuyWKJHK0U1T1GudqRf9678GUuf__OatL3okH9qiyw3S975bDw1vNr8rgOAZ3qR4kEQILoxJQ/s320/Peace-With-Honour-Queen-Victoria-With-Benjamin-Disraeli--Following-The-Signing-Of-The-Berlin-Treaty-In-1878.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>Three types of Get documents are invalid, but if she married on their basis anyway, the child she has from the second marriage is legitimate: a Get that the husband wrote in his own handwriting but there are no witnesses signed on it; a Get that has no date recorded on it; a Get that has only one witness signed on it.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Elazar says, “Even though there are no witnesses signed on the Get, but he gave it to her in the presence of witnesses, it is valid, for witnesses sign on the Get only for the benefit of society.”<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Peace with Honour - Queen Victoria (1819-1901) with Benjamin Disraeli (1804-81) following the signing of the Berlin Treaty in 1878 by&nbsp;THEODORE BLAKE WIRGMAN</div>

### content/gittin/87.txt

Gittin 87 - Group Divorce
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyT-AT0vwGH_C2SIs9p88iUByAUdUuxriQqe00NLYZh1tkIqGejuj-rK57_DgNb4H2WZAxyXWRxDMnV8hDibMrBqTFzpzBIQGncM9k6wNphPNxSfApM39sI9s0_2WpaMFBH1DRPSEaALMY/s1600-h/Th%C3%A9odore_Chass%C3%A9riau.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5254104941060020082" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyT-AT0vwGH_C2SIs9p88iUByAUdUuxriQqe00NLYZh1tkIqGejuj-rK57_DgNb4H2WZAxyXWRxDMnV8hDibMrBqTFzpzBIQGncM9k6wNphPNxSfApM39sI9s0_2WpaMFBH1DRPSEaALMY/s320/Th%C3%A9odore_Chass%C3%A9riau.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If two men sent two identical Get documents to their wives through an agent (the names of the husbands and their wives being identical), and the Get documents were confused by the agent, he must give both Get documents to both women.<br />
<br />
If five men wrote a common text in the Get, namely, "I, so-and-so, am divorcing my wife, so-and-so, etc.," the Get is valid for all five couples, and it should be given to every one of the women named in it to effect her divorce.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Two sisters by Theodore Chasseriau</div>

### content/gittin/88.txt
<a id="src-00161"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/88.txt`

Gittin 88 - Divorce Procured by Force
<div class="separator"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUzBOg9qVCmoNag6E6y8oaL03NFFQnPkY0JN7XPVUVk05UXNVFrTQ9nPJ50XSqDqmwX4cboGV12758aBgJtpjsRpsrVH8fAxr0IJBWKibtC_j-3b-4lsSJwH35OB1_CPJD16YOFmzAkFwl/s1600-h/fighting.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5254536823821081490" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUzBOg9qVCmoNag6E6y8oaL03NFFQnPkY0JN7XPVUVk05UXNVFrTQ9nPJ50XSqDqmwX4cboGV12758aBgJtpjsRpsrVH8fAxr0IJBWKibtC_j-3b-4lsSJwH35OB1_CPJD16YOFmzAkFwl/s320/fighting.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a></div>The term "quickly" of the Master of the World means 852 years because of the phrase "you will be aged (venoshantem=852 by gematria), and you will be removed, quickly, from the Land."<br />
<br />
Concerning a Get procured by force, the Get is valid if the coercion was applied by the Jewish court and the husband acquiesced. But if the pressure was used by a court of idolaters, the Get is invalid. However, even in a court of idolaters, they may beat the husband and tell him, "Do what the Jewish court tells you to do!" the Get is valid.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Peasants Fighting by Adriaen Brouwer</div>

### content/gittin/89.txt

**Source file:** `content/gittin/89.txt`

Gittin 89 - Rumors of Marriage
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgkxcZlhJ7A6u4cNKLBlVYwXOkVr_HqUO8NHwKzFK0HUhlsAIuKYZQ8KSnpm-Rwa5EkjwXVfTTTH41OZm445TnDPgTZkYaw_X2urivg091MqxPmwWr7Tcs_NDw3_VxszszQGznJZp7Qzc3q/s1600-h/The-Secret-L.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5255379207324716306" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgkxcZlhJ7A6u4cNKLBlVYwXOkVr_HqUO8NHwKzFK0HUhlsAIuKYZQ8KSnpm-Rwa5EkjwXVfTTTH41OZm445TnDPgTZkYaw_X2urivg091MqxPmwWr7Tcs_NDw3_VxszszQGznJZp7Qzc3q/s320/The-Secret-L.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a><div>If a woman was rumored in town to be betrothed, she is treated as though she were betrothed; that is, she may not marry anyone except the man to whom she is rumored to be betrothed unless he gives her a Get.<br />
<br />
A rumor of marriage is recognized not as mere gossip. Still, when they say, "We heard the rumor from so-and-so, and they heard it from so-and-so," the court continues to investigate until they find two qualified witnesses who saw the betrothal feast and heard people say, "So-and-so was betrothed today."<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Secret by&nbsp;William-Adolphe Bouguereau</div></div>

### content/gittin/9.txt
<a id="src-00163"></a>

**Source file:** `content/gittin/9.txt`

Gittin 9 – Letter of freedom
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEijdatHY1uePlLdmR8AFY2sltHbrsXqiRZfc9RROqJfWxkgztQPFsu-LZ4Viu9oMc4XWN8Nj5MOe8bRYrRmr2pS_po6UpRwjI9TSSN7ol_wCzl3d1qnm0Wnx7uUxT_1AhnBVy1o-T2c7cjA/s1600/The+Hour+of+Emancipation+by+William+Tolman+Carlton.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="256" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEijdatHY1uePlLdmR8AFY2sltHbrsXqiRZfc9RROqJfWxkgztQPFsu-LZ4Viu9oMc4XWN8Nj5MOe8bRYrRmr2pS_po6UpRwjI9TSSN7ol_wCzl3d1qnm0Wnx7uUxT_1AhnBVy1o-T2c7cjA/s320/The+Hour+of+Emancipation+by+William+Tolman+Carlton.jpg" width="320" /></a>A divorce document (Get) is essentially a letter of freedom for the woman, who can now marry anyone she wants. In the same way, a Get can be given to a slave, and it will be a letter of his emancipation, reading "You are free" or "You belong to yourself."
<br />
<br />
The similarity goes further: a woman can bring her own Get to court, and they will use it to effect a divorce, as long as she can tell them it was written and signed before her. So too, can do the slave. 
<br />
<br />
However, if in the Get, the master says to the slave, "You and all my possessions are yours," - he indeed goes free because it is similar to a Get of a woman, but the second part, "all my possessions are yours," does not take effect because, for any monetary transaction, one needs two witnesses. There are two clauses in this Get, and they work differently.
<br />
<br />
What happens if the Get says, "You acquire all my possessions." Since "all my possessions" includes the slave, he acquires himself and becomes free, and in the same step, acquires all the possessions as well. At least, this is what Abaye opined. 
<br />
<br />
Rava disagreed. Since the slave did not have two witnesses, he did not acquire the possessions. And since he did not acquire the possessions, he did not acquire himself and is thus still a slave. Rava later changed his mind but still divided the single statement "You acquire all my possessions" into two. This is called severability, but here it is applied to one sentence! They continued to argue about this principle.
<br />
<br />
Art: The Hour of Emancipation by William Tolman Carlton

---

### content/gittin/90.txt

Gittin 90 (Conclusion) - Reasons for Divorce
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgcwAG6z5CnvySBcm6gF0dJLHcSRgJ3xDrIfDqW63094haaFv7iNtUGpJGt8VxzJoPGVtGBaonQ2J5oFLAyKIYhdNT72a5wGrZxQsZPwYv51m6nGBDr51ZO92gpN8qn2WvDyMBBkwqxrQuk/s1600-h/renoir.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5255385617794138594" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgcwAG6z5CnvySBcm6gF0dJLHcSRgJ3xDrIfDqW63094haaFv7iNtUGpJGt8VxzJoPGVtGBaonQ2J5oFLAyKIYhdNT72a5wGrZxQsZPwYv51m6nGBDr51ZO92gpN8qn2WvDyMBBkwqxrQuk/s320/renoir.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Beit Shammai say, “A man may not divorce his wife unless he found in her an act of adultery.” Proof: “Because he found in her an adulterous matter.”<br />
<br />
But Beit Hillel says, “Even if she burned his dish.” Proof: “Adulterous or any other matter.”<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiva says, “Even if he found another more attractive than her.” Proof: “And it comes to pass that she does not find favor in his eyes.<br />
<br />
Despised by God is anyone who sends away his wife without a compelling reason.<br />
<br />
Whenever anyone divorces his first wife, even the <a href="http://bible.cc/malachi/2-13.htmhttp://bible.cc/malachi/2-13.htm">Temple Altar sheds tears on his account</a>.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Alfred Sisley with His Wife by Renoir<br /></span><div><br /></div></div>

---

### content/horayot/10.txt
<a id="src-00165"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/10.txt`

Horayot 10 – The King and the Commoner
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_Kb-j4k2fCrIqcMIkpnANX3aH5Uuq_2hGNFoR7rVYHZ7EV57rm6u7aUEnSP8MKczgJgJ4owsXFDarSbeLW4pkDTKW-Fz7ghRNvuRZLlqK2etjeP2R12569HLQnibidqtmbct3MnV8n40/s1600/Emil+Carlsen+-+Moonlilt+Seascape.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="287" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_Kb-j4k2fCrIqcMIkpnANX3aH5Uuq_2hGNFoR7rVYHZ7EV57rm6u7aUEnSP8MKczgJgJ4owsXFDarSbeLW4pkDTKW-Fz7ghRNvuRZLlqK2etjeP2R12569HLQnibidqtmbct3MnV8n40/s320/Emil+Carlsen+-+Moonlilt+Seascape.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an anointed priest has sinned and then left his position, and similarly, if a leader has sinned and then left his position of greatness, they still bring the sacrifices corresponding to their previous level: the priest brings a bull and the leader – a he-goat.<br />
<br />
The High Priest is removed from his position if he develops a physical blemish that makes his service invalid. A leader is removed if he develops a sickness of tzaraat – spiritual leprosy – or if he is deposed.<br />
<br />
Who is that leader that the Torah describes as “Prince, or Nasi,” to whom the above laws are applicable? That is the king, as the Torah describes him, “one who has no superior except God.”<br />
<br />
The king is a servant of the people, as we see from the following story. Rabban Gamliel and Rabbi Yehoshua were traveling together on a ship, Rabban Gamliel had bread, and Rabbi Yehoshua had bread and flour. When Rabban Gamliel ran out of bread, he was sustained by Rabbi Yehoshua's flour. Said he to Rabbi Yehoshua, “Why were you so provident?” Rabbi Yehoshua replied that there is a star that misleads sailors, and it shows once in 70 years. “If you are so smart,” - said Rabban Gamliel - “Why do you have to travel on business?” Rabbi Yehoshua replied, “Before you help me, help your two students, Rabbi Elazar and Rabbi Yochanan, who know how to count every drop in the sea, but don't have bread. Rabban Gamliel wanted to appoint them heads of  Yeshiva, but they did not want to. So he told them, “Don't think that I am making you rulers, rather, I am making you servants.”<br />
<br />
Art: Emil Carlsen - Moonlilt Seascape</span>

---

### content/horayot/11.txt
<a id="src-00166"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/11.txt`

Horayot 11 – How is Anointed High Priest Different
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjFZhRVXFPQKsVoUzjW16yjvizxseZJXUccAeIz5RfxoTofslg_x7f61kOMSd9Q94VUsVJCq1gVhRo2nhToD92gys2mrTARFQF9FAdZxkQ91ja2_K8UqRAYMFSYqAiBNT3isT7lpPEgAdY/s1600/James+Jacques+Joseph+Tissot+-+A+Widow.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjFZhRVXFPQKsVoUzjW16yjvizxseZJXUccAeIz5RfxoTofslg_x7f61kOMSd9Q94VUsVJCq1gVhRo2nhToD92gys2mrTARFQF9FAdZxkQ91ja2_K8UqRAYMFSYqAiBNT3isT7lpPEgAdY/s320/James+Jacques+Joseph+Tissot+-+A+Widow.JPG" width="222" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">An anointed High Priest is installed into his office by being anointed with the special oil prepared by Moses, and by donning four extra vestments in addition to the four garments of the regular priest. After the anointing oil was concealed, only the installation by donning the extra vestments remained. <br />
<br />
The difference between an anointed High Priest and one who was installed with additional garments is that only the anointed Priest brings a special bull sacrifice if he sins or the court errs.<br />
<br />
If a High Priest becomes ritually impure or otherwise temporarily unfit for service, another High Priest is appointed in his stead. When the first one returns, he is called The Serving High Priest, and the temporary substitute gets the name of High Priest Who Passed out of Service. The Serving High Priest is higher in that he brings the bull of Yom Kippur and his daily flour offering. They are equally commanded to marry a virgin and cannot marry a widow. Both cannot observe mourning, and accidental murderers return from their exile on the death of both.<br />
<br />
Art: James Jacques Joseph Tissot - A Widow</span>

---

### content/horayot/12.txt
<a id="src-00167"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/12.txt`

Horayot 12 – Good Omens
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhdKgSe2qe6XHaJOPxqihh5F_hxuATm1TWaSK2R-VIpi5RDlfW1rjW6OiCXTFhq22KYVzr9bt3gC-olmsgiPmPvLIswVH_11xxinS2u8HC84OjuBP9g8RH8auuHIhkQldx76gbeOryn3BU/s1600/Ferdinand+Loyen+Du+Puigaudeau+-+Chinese+Shadows%252C+the+Rabbit.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhdKgSe2qe6XHaJOPxqihh5F_hxuATm1TWaSK2R-VIpi5RDlfW1rjW6OiCXTFhq22KYVzr9bt3gC-olmsgiPmPvLIswVH_11xxinS2u8HC84OjuBP9g8RH8auuHIhkQldx76gbeOryn3BU/s320/Ferdinand+Loyen+Du+Puigaudeau+-+Chinese+Shadows%252C+the+Rabbit.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Anointing a king at a spring is a good omen for his kingdom to last. On the subject of good omens, if one wants to know if he will live out the year or not, he should kindle a lamp during the ten days between Rosh HaShana and Yom Kippur, in a house where no wind blows. If the light continues to burn for as long as there is oil in the lamp, we know that he will live out the year.<br />
<br />
If one wants to undertake a business venture and wants to know if it will be successful or not, let him raise a rooster for the sake of that business venture and let him see: if the rooster grows plump and fine, it is  a good omen that he will be successful.<br />
<br />
If one wants to go out on the road and wants to know if he will return home safely or not, let him stand in a dark house. If he sees a shadow of his shadow, know that he will return home successfully.<br />
<br />
And it is not a wise thing for one to do, for if the omen is negative, he may become distressed, and his luck might indeed take a turn for the worst. For this reason, the omens are formulated to consider only the good outcome.<br />
<br />
Art: Ferdinand Loyen Du Puigaudeau - Chinese Shadows, the Rabbit</span>

---

### content/horayot/13.txt
<a id="src-00168"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/13.txt`

Horayot 13 – Order of Precedence
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhNu50eprKD_t8FbwHVTe-8GxnWFiHk-WSuHUPjYkkVOcumwP3qxKAbZVROlEoLKckfux3aDsEW_MLGFTgTxIJXnzT1xDUI3i0PFHzlLtvi57Q4RL4T6FOqtBVxlZ_KimLxVxS0Jv2-Aw0/s1600/Jean-L%25C3%25A9on+G%25C3%25A9r%25C3%25B4me+-+Old+Clothing+Merchant+in+Cairo.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="253" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhNu50eprKD_t8FbwHVTe-8GxnWFiHk-WSuHUPjYkkVOcumwP3qxKAbZVROlEoLKckfux3aDsEW_MLGFTgTxIJXnzT1xDUI3i0PFHzlLtvi57Q4RL4T6FOqtBVxlZ_KimLxVxS0Jv2-Aw0/s320/Jean-L%25C3%25A9on+G%25C3%25A9r%25C3%25B4me+-+Old+Clothing+Merchant+in+Cairo.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When a High Priest needs to observe mourning, he tears his garment from the bottom, and not from the top, like regular priests and laypeople do. He brings sacrifices even on the first day of mourning, just does not eat them, while regular priests do not bring sacrifices.<br />
<br />
When one has any two mitzvot that he can perform, he should first do the one that is more frequent, and this is derived from the order of sacrifices in the Temple. If one mitzvah is more sacred than the other, it has to be done first. If the High Priest's bull and the assembly's bull, brought for a court's error, are both standing to be sacrificed, the High Priest's bull goes first – not based on the above rules, but because it is called “first” by the Torah. <br />
<br />
If a man and a woman both need food or clothing, the woman takes precedence, because the man can go begging door to door. When both are held captive, the woman is ransomed first.<br />
<br />
Art: Jean-Léon Gérôme - Old Clothing Merchant in Cairo</span>

---

### content/horayot/14.txt
<a id="src-00169"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/14.txt`

Horayot 14 - Retaining One's Learning
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhHBwbt0e5a6Js-rZyYlF70V71hX2L0Cq60kQW12L79cAkE-nM7_RfVxHjnRrrTgUIZSJIB-PCCJAXlw8qKA7dz2SDttK2H6sVwQZpVUkYGDvxzQvXksUGiVYFdhyKQYRUyzeTeS6PASC8/s1600/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Venetian+Wineshop.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="254" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhHBwbt0e5a6Js-rZyYlF70V71hX2L0Cq60kQW12L79cAkE-nM7_RfVxHjnRrrTgUIZSJIB-PCCJAXlw8qKA7dz2SDttK2H6sVwQZpVUkYGDvxzQvXksUGiVYFdhyKQYRUyzeTeS6PASC8/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+Venetian+Wineshop.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When it comes to redeeming people from captivity, there is a specified order, who is redeemed first, but it only applies to regular people, however, a Sage always takes precedence, and an illegitimately born Sage precedes an unlearned High Priest.<br />
<br />
Five things are conducive to retaining one's learning: eating wheat bread, eating lightly cooked eggs, regular consumption of olive oil, regular enjoyment of wine and aromatics spices, and drinking water left over from producing a dough.<br />
<br />
Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel instituted that the Prince (he occupied this position) should be given more honor than the President of Court (Rabbi Nathan) and than the leading Sage (Rabbi Meir). They wanted to overthrow him, and plotted to suddenly ask him to expound Ukzin, the hardest tractate of Mishna. A friend, however, warned him, so he studied all night and was able to expound on the next day. However, Rabban Gamliel forbade Rabbi Meir and Rabbi Nathan to enter the study hall, and they had to write their answers in a piece of paper and throw them inside. The Sages petitioned for them, and they were readmitted, but when their teachings are quoted, they are not mentioned by name, but as "others say."<br />
<br />
Art: John Singer Sargent - Venetian Wineshop<br />
<br />
End of Horayot<br />
</span>

---

### content/horayot/2.txt
<a id="src-00170"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/2.txt`

Horayot 2 – Court Makes a Mistake
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhuqLp8U5A1a_2PIDTh2On16SLrNAFbts1-XHNPEjMppcs3i88yejumwwGbnhvyte8juWuN83G51JC9zqix-xwUPSxvNNa7UZY7kLA1XlzQuzikA3CAQJ8zWyRzGgwIy7EO_GxJL8WY8iY/s1600/Thomas+Satterwhite+Noble+-+The+Price+of+Blood.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="256" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhuqLp8U5A1a_2PIDTh2On16SLrNAFbts1-XHNPEjMppcs3i88yejumwwGbnhvyte8juWuN83G51JC9zqix-xwUPSxvNNa7UZY7kLA1XlzQuzikA3CAQJ8zWyRzGgwIy7EO_GxJL8WY8iY/s320/Thomas+Satterwhite+Noble+-+The+Price+of+Blood.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the court ruled to transgress one of the commandments written in the Torah - for example, they decided that a certain type of blood is allowed to be eaten, and an individual did it, relying on their words – he is free from liability. Whether he ate the blood together with them at a meal, or after observing them, or even if they just ruled it permitted, but did not do it themselves, since he relied on their words, it is not his fault.<br />
<br />
However, if he was one of the Sages of the court, or even one of the students who was worthy to be on the court, and he knew that they erred, but he nevertheless followed their ruling, he is liable to bring a sin offering. If he knew that they erred, then why did he do it? Because he mistakenly thought that the mitzvah to follow the words of the Sages applies even in this case.<br />
<br />
Art: Thomas Satterwhite Noble - The Price of Blood</span>

---

### content/horayot/3.txt
<a id="src-00171"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/3.txt`

Horayot 3 – Only Jews in Israel Count for Majority
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiY8k-lqnMXHXw2RpnkzLPxRf2YttfbDN8CjVFOEebCCPs_znPgWe4XZllmZ-7kUY0fs6vywR465S_9BsyKC7bpQ8rj61SH-L1xDvGkbDyNlFH96olIEdRr9Vjn92vmkrPgOfhr_8yhktg/s1600/Ignacy+Aleksander+Gierymski+-+Feast+of+Trumpets.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="237" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiY8k-lqnMXHXw2RpnkzLPxRf2YttfbDN8CjVFOEebCCPs_znPgWe4XZllmZ-7kUY0fs6vywR465S_9BsyKC7bpQ8rj61SH-L1xDvGkbDyNlFH96olIEdRr9Vjn92vmkrPgOfhr_8yhktg/s320/Ignacy+Aleksander+Gierymski+-+Feast+of+Trumpets.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The previous rule that one is not liable if he followed the erroneous decision of the court is the minority opinion; the prevailing opinion is that one IS liable in such case. However, if the majority of Jews acted on a court's error – who ruled, for example, that a certain action is not idol worship when in reality it is – then each individual is not liable, and instead the court brings the sacrifice for the mistake they had made. The majority in this case is determined only among the Jews living in Israel.<br />
<br />
What if the court mistakenly ruled that a certain prohibited fat (destined for the Altar) is permitted, and then a minority of Israel acted upon that, then the court retracted their mistake, and afterwards again mistakenly ruled that this fat was allowed, and now a different minority acted upon it – do they combine into a majority? This and other similar inquiries remain unresolved.<br />
<br />
Ignacy Aleksander Gierymski - Feast of Trumpets (Slichot)</span>

---

### content/horayot/4.txt
<a id="src-00172"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/4.txt`

Horayot 4 – After Court Retracted
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjM46jrrFJ7WVqdT_Ot6CwBxWBD0NgTshHp9JmBcnsxC4fDlFMWR9PdGtxrS6wsdW0hQaOdBSKDzOHW5fI7LQkrxuJYb2ls3LMDuWMM51rYfhfz3gy73vb4OJjaa_9UywprfPDeZetTXWI/s1600/Pierre-Auguste+Renoir+-+Man+Carrying+a+Boy.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjM46jrrFJ7WVqdT_Ot6CwBxWBD0NgTshHp9JmBcnsxC4fDlFMWR9PdGtxrS6wsdW0hQaOdBSKDzOHW5fI7LQkrxuJYb2ls3LMDuWMM51rYfhfz3gy73vb4OJjaa_9UywprfPDeZetTXWI/s320/Pierre-Auguste+Renoir+-+Man+Carrying+a+Boy.jpg" width="177" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the court ruled incorrectly and permitted something that the Torah has prohibited under the pain of excision – being cut off from the people - and the majority of Jews did it, then when the judges realize their mistake, they need to bring a bull sacrifice, to atone for the “sin of forgetfulness.”<br />
<br />
What happens if an individual did it  because he has not heard that the court has retracted? Rabbi Shimon always exempts him. Rabbi Elazar says that his error is in doubt, and therefore he must bring a special guilt-offering.  This applies when he stayed at home and could check on the court opinion before doing the act. If he went overseas, he is completely exempt.<br />
<br />
The court needs to forget only part of the law, but not the complete law. For example, if they ruled that there is no Shabbat in the Torah, they are exempt from the bull offering, but if they said, “There is Shabbat in the Torah, but one is allowed to carry things from one's house into the street,” - then they are liable to a communal-error bull offering.<br />
<br />
Art: Pierre-Auguste Renoir - Man Carrying a Boy</span>

---

### content/horayot/5.txt
<a id="src-00173"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/5.txt`

Horayot 5 – Who Brings the Bull for the “Sin of Forgetfulness”
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgh5ZkzuoKC0pWHzeKQdWpgX26L27zmvYIW7qfSNPdtcig_QeKB9cleGhu4UigTMH8vZWctLHBpcnM-SOyhy76Pt3ItykOPbskq_q6NF6ltyqhkHgE9dgjmxB0szyExey97F60KFzZsz-A/s1600/Paulus+Potter+-+Young+Bull+1647.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="221" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgh5ZkzuoKC0pWHzeKQdWpgX26L27zmvYIW7qfSNPdtcig_QeKB9cleGhu4UigTMH8vZWctLHBpcnM-SOyhy76Pt3ItykOPbskq_q6NF6ltyqhkHgE9dgjmxB0szyExey97F60KFzZsz-A/s320/Paulus+Potter+-+Young+Bull+1647.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one of the court members realized that they have erred and dissented, or if the most distinguished member of the court was not present, or if one of the judges was disqualified for the court, such as a convert or an elder who is unfit to father children – they don't bring a bull offering. If the court ruled incorrectly on purpose, and not by mistake, then each individual who transgressed brings his own sin offering, an ewe or a she-goat.<br />
<br />
How many bulls are brought? There are multiple opinions about it: some say that the court brings the offering, and some – that the congregation of people does it. Furthermore, each tribe is called a congregation, so there are opinions that each tribe brings an offering, some tribes bring it, and even that all tribes bring it if one tribe sinned. Some opinions require the court of a single tribe to bring an offering, but the Sages say that liability exists only for the error of the Great Sanhedrin of seventy one, which was located on the Temple Mount, in the Chamber of Hewn Stones.<br />
<br />
Art: Paulus Potter - Young Bull 1647</span>

---

### content/horayot/6.txt
<a id="src-00174"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/6.txt`

Horayot 6 – The Sacrifices of the Babylonian Exiles
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_bK_y-Dr2A0T52CzUKWF52Ml8k_N0b_-2kNXa4mSFq47AbFBxl79C3t625Wy3dgF8_3UHYaa5O6AR5-LJSBls7ol6wF5pc9T57ETIOKrKDbM0NiQwZ1VaJJywf07maa4bJpvTZJBAhZ0/s1600/Jan+Victors-+Jacob+Seeking+Forgiveness+of+Esau.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="277" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_bK_y-Dr2A0T52CzUKWF52Ml8k_N0b_-2kNXa4mSFq47AbFBxl79C3t625Wy3dgF8_3UHYaa5O6AR5-LJSBls7ol6wF5pc9T57ETIOKrKDbM0NiQwZ1VaJJywf07maa4bJpvTZJBAhZ0/s320/Jan+Victors-+Jacob+Seeking+Forgiveness+of+Esau.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When, led by Ezra, the Jews returned from Babylon to Jerusalem, they “<a href="http://bible.cc/ezra/8-35.htm">brought offerings to the God of Israel, twelve bulls... twelve goats...all as burnt offerings to God.</a>” <br />
<br />
Incidentally, they were not all “burnt offerings,” rather, the goats were sin-offerings. If so, why are they called this? - because the goats were sin-offerings for idol worship, but like the burnt offering, they were not eaten by the priest.<br />
<br />
According to Rabbi Yehudah, who says that if some of the tribes sinned, every tribe brings a goat, we understand twelve goats. According to Rabbi Shimon, who says that tribes do not “drag” each other into asking for forgiveness, eleven tribes sinned and brought eleven offerings, and the twelfth was brought by the court. But according to Rabbi Meir, who says that only the court brings the offering, why were twelve offerings required? Rabbi Meir answers that the court sinned, changed its mind, sinned again, changed its mind again, and so on, twelve times. <br />
<br />
If, after the mistake of the court, one of the Jews dies, they still bring an offering – since the congregation never dies – but if one of the judges dies, they do not bring an offering.<br />
<br />
Art: Jan Victors- Jacob Seeking Forgiveness of Esau</span>

---

### content/horayot/7.txt
<a id="src-00175"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/7.txt`

Horayot 7 – Mistake of the High Priest
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhZSxZSevRxnlJ-xqDcBY9S7wy1BUNZBWT-t4rhM5vUJbTOjbsfJA_TRjmalUgLFxxvqsP8sD2A-Oy6V1184xloywqHosoSP6Gf7Od1xLlbH9muLDy8sPwdl9cyONk1iBvIyWCmRjWpmSg/s1600/John+Byam+Liston+Shaw+And+Who+Knoweth+Whether+He+Shall+Be+A+Wise+Man+Or+A+Fool.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhZSxZSevRxnlJ-xqDcBY9S7wy1BUNZBWT-t4rhM5vUJbTOjbsfJA_TRjmalUgLFxxvqsP8sD2A-Oy6V1184xloywqHosoSP6Gf7Od1xLlbH9muLDy8sPwdl9cyONk1iBvIyWCmRjWpmSg/s320/John+Byam+Liston+Shaw+And+Who+Knoweth+Whether+He+Shall+Be+A+Wise+Man+Or+A+Fool.jpg" width="193" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the High Priest, anointed for service with Temple oil, is himself a Sage and ruled that something normally forbidden on the pain of excision is allowed, and then, without realizing his mistake, performed the act, he brings a special sacrifice, the “Anointed Kohen's bull.” If he knowingly ruled incorrectly or knowingly performed the forbidden act, he does not bring this sacrifice. His law is thus similar to the court's ruling that it makes for the community.<br />
<br />
If he ruled incorrectly together with the court and performed the act together with the congregation, he does not bring his special sacrifice but is atoned for by the communal “sacrifice of forgetfulness” bull. Just as the court is only liable if it negates a part of a commandment, but not the whole commandment, so too the High Priest.<br />
<br />
Art: John Byam Liston Shaw - And Who Knoweth Whether He Shall Be A Wise Man Or A Fool</span>

---

### content/horayot/8.txt
<a id="src-00176"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/8.txt`

Horayot 8 – How Serious Does the Error  Have to Be?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilVXgI-lOa4q5km2RNJ0VFqid__JfG53fD57H605LyQlYkVu1U2cWruVVVpIqSZw-H6MZYHJSpQrI_FHuSBIPL0zmNTkCIgN0HtwojB3BWiqxsptil6LI799y8bkSj7jnG3r-o4JprEBo/s1600/Pierre+Auguste+Renoir+-+Two+Sisters+II.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilVXgI-lOa4q5km2RNJ0VFqid__JfG53fD57H605LyQlYkVu1U2cWruVVVpIqSZw-H6MZYHJSpQrI_FHuSBIPL0zmNTkCIgN0HtwojB3BWiqxsptil6LI799y8bkSj7jnG3r-o4JprEBo/s320/Pierre+Auguste+Renoir+-+Two+Sisters+II.jpg" width="270" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The court brings the “sin of forgetfulness” sacrifice only if the action they had permitted requires a sin offering if done unintentionally and leads to excision if done willfully. This is known by comparison to the law of one's wife's sister, which the Torah spells out. In both places the same word “because of her” is used and thus their laws are the same. This rule is also true for an anointed priest, about whom the Torah says “for the people to be ashamed of him” - which means that he has the same law as the people. This rule is also true for a leader of the nation.<br />
<br />
The court does not bring a bull sacrifice if they rule incorrectly about a purity aspect of the Temple service, since an individual brings a different sin offering for that. Rather, it should be an error leading to a regular sin-offering, for example, the positive commandment of husband and wife to abstain before the day of expected menses, and a negative commandment not to have relations with the wife who has not been to the mikvah.<br />
<br />
Art: Pierre Auguste Renoir - Two Sisters II</span>

---

### content/horayot/9.txt
<a id="src-00177"></a>

**Source file:** `content/horayot/9.txt`

Horayot 9 – Who Brings What Sacrifice
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5TmcsvongZWeWbF92X8h_ZjfFafQvlWFkm3dWj2QZ5_V5gJWB7EuDvj3peR9OB5nlWvlIbDN5OTFD0DAri9gShpwez3dKqqxrH0Ewqqs7Q6dEbZZ26pgYXKsr-2XaMM6MftrFEGTXdlc/s1600/Stefano+Bruzzi+-+Mountain+Goats.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="259" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5TmcsvongZWeWbF92X8h_ZjfFafQvlWFkm3dWj2QZ5_V5gJWB7EuDvj3peR9OB5nlWvlIbDN5OTFD0DAri9gShpwez3dKqqxrH0Ewqqs7Q6dEbZZ26pgYXKsr-2XaMM6MftrFEGTXdlc/s320/Stefano+Bruzzi+-+Mountain+Goats.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">For any commandment in the Torah, for the violation of which one is liable to excision if done on purpose, and to a sin-offering, if done by mistake, the actual sacrifice is different. An individual brings a she-lamb or a she-goat as his sin-offering, also called an “offering for a mistake.” The leader of the nation brings a he-goat, the anointed High Priest and the court bring a bull.<br />
<br />
If the transgression was that of idol worship, an individual, the leader, and the anointed priest bring a she-goat, whereas the court brings a bull and a he-goat. The bull as completely burned on the Altar, and the goat is a sin-offering, which is partially eaten by the priests.<br />
<br />
If one violated a commandment, resulting in a guilt-offering, and furthermore if he is in doubt about this,  both an and a leader of the community bring a “doubtful guilt-offering,” but the anointed priest and the court are exempt. Regarding a definite guilt-offering, an individual, the leader, and the priest are liable, but the court is exempt.<br />
<br />
Art: Stefano Bruzzi - Mountain Goats</span>

---

### content/keritot/10.txt
<a id="src-00178"></a>

**Source file:** `content/keritot/10.txt`

Keritot 10 – Offering Which Depends On Financial Status
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjoB-BYysuOCRuIZ3llxZi0suc1oHJNFsEbU-wAU9Vb9rRANLRY0ITvHooXalyBJczaTH_WpTJ6NyIHuDbWO0qdsRVTEbqxMa3kvU4YdiPsm5WxeT_VSCy0QF1SiwcRQcJontbOWmPtBdVj/s1600/Fritz+Paulsen+-+The+Birthday+Present.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjoB-BYysuOCRuIZ3llxZi0suc1oHJNFsEbU-wAU9Vb9rRANLRY0ITvHooXalyBJczaTH_WpTJ6NyIHuDbWO0qdsRVTEbqxMa3kvU4YdiPsm5WxeT_VSCy0QF1SiwcRQcJontbOWmPtBdVj/s320/Fritz+Paulsen+-+The+Birthday+Present.jpg" width="263" /></a>Some mistakes mentioned in the Torah require a sacrifice whose value depends on the financial status of the one who brings it. For example, if a litigant in money matters asked a witness to testify, and the witness refused, the litigant then asked him to swear that he knows nothing, and he swore (falsely), the witness needs to bring a sacrifice. This variable cost sacrifice is an animal in the case of sufficient means, a bird offering if he is poor, and a flour offering, if he is indigent. 
<br />
<br />
The same type of sacrifice is brought by one who inadvertently entered the Temple while being spritually impure, or one who ate the meat of sacrifices in this state.
<br />
<br />
A woman who gave birth brings a male lamb if she has the means, and a pair of birds if she is poor. A spiritual leper (metzora) brings three animals (sin, guilt, and burned offerings) if he has the means, and one animal and two birds if he is poor.
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Fritz Paulsen - The Birthday Present

---

### content/keritot/11.txt
<a id="src-00179"></a>

**Source file:** `content/keritot/11.txt`

Keritot 11 – The Differences Between A Slavewoman And Other Women
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiX8a4VgkS2UwcOJ3-i5fDgADw9DeheZzFTresAfBZSZyR0_QGVi-dIXwvH83beDysCWA933lS2VwsO2IqypY3dt1qFY9p8mLXuX5wCJtgCE5pev9YBjg5Z3v-XVPV-fFCfcN1yPNln5lIe/s1600/Gustave+Courbet+-+Peasant+Woman+Sleeping.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiX8a4VgkS2UwcOJ3-i5fDgADw9DeheZzFTresAfBZSZyR0_QGVi-dIXwvH83beDysCWA933lS2VwsO2IqypY3dt1qFY9p8mLXuX5wCJtgCE5pev9YBjg5Z3v-XVPV-fFCfcN1yPNln5lIe/s320/Gustave+Courbet+-+Peasant+Woman+Sleeping.jpg" width="267" /></a>The laws of a slavewoman designated for another differ in many ways from the laws of other forbidden women. For example, for mistaken relations with all other women one brings a sin-offering, but for a slavewoman he brings a guilt-offering. Incidentally, sin-offering is always a female sheep, and guilt-offering is a male ram. 
<br />
<br />
Usually, both transgressing parties have equal liability, for example, both bring a sacrifice. In the case of relations with a slavewoman, the man is liable for a sacrifice, whether he acted intentionally or by mistake; she, on the other hand, is only liable if she was warned not to do it and nevertheless immediately proceeded with the act, in which case she is liable to lashes. Usually, one is liable for each and every act of cohabitation, but with the slavewoman he brings one sacrifice for all acts. Normally, one is liable whether he performs the “beginning of cohabitation” (genital contact, and some say, insertion of the corona), or the “complete act” (full penetration), but in the case of a slavewoman one is only liable for the complete act. Normally, if one of the partners was sleeping, only the awake one is liable, but in the case of a slavewoman, if one of the partners was sleeping, none is liable.
<br />
<br />
Art: Gustave Courbet - Peasant Woman Sleeping

---

### content/keritot/12.txt
<a id="src-00180"></a>

**Source file:** `content/keritot/12.txt`

Keritot 12 – Witnesses Tell Him That He Inadvertently Ate Forbidden Fat
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhB4pB9SwypTLuHA-xV6G580Zx39EkICaPd4fvfdHDek9CBAGD5BH5WJj4PA96HjDaClZ5__2GlkXF0jSEVR6DodAz_kEyIzPoC-evN4yhOY0HMwskJVy1H-pIhMt8v651mFgoLUa0otHo2/s1600/By+Hermann+Kern+-+The+Peasant's+Meal.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhB4pB9SwypTLuHA-xV6G580Zx39EkICaPd4fvfdHDek9CBAGD5BH5WJj4PA96HjDaClZ5__2GlkXF0jSEVR6DodAz_kEyIzPoC-evN4yhOY0HMwskJVy1H-pIhMt8v651mFgoLUa0otHo2/s320/By+Hermann+Kern+-+The+Peasant's+Meal.jpg" width="209" /></a>If one witness tells somebody, “You ate forbidden fat,” and the man remains silent, he has to bring a sin-offering. However, if he denies it, he is not liable. If two witnesses tell a man that he ate forbidden fat, and he denies it, then Rabbi Meir holds him liable, but the Sages exempt him.
<br />
<br />
(There are two sorts of animal fat, permitted, called “shuman,” and forbidden, called “chelev”. If one eats forbidden fat by mistake, he needs to bring a sin-offering, and if he eats it knowingly, he is liable to be cut off from his spiritual source.)
<br />
<br />
What is the source for these laws and what is the logic of the argument? The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=4#P2816">If his sin becomes known to him</a>.” This means that he himself became aware of his act. Alternatively, others told him, but he was silent, thus confirming that he accepted the fact and became aware of it. Thus, if he denies one witness, he is believed.
<br />
<br />
When two witnesses tell him that he ate the wrong fat, we have an established fact. Rabbi Meir then reasons that if witnesses can testify about a capital crime and have a man executed, then certainly they can obligate him to bring a sacrifice. The Sages, however, say that he has a way out: he can claim that he ate the fat on purpose, and be free from a sacrifice obligation. This claim, of course, does not work to escape capital punishment.
<br />
<br />
Art: Hermann Kern - The Peasant's Meal

---

### content/keritot/13.txt
<a id="src-00181"></a>

**Source file:** `content/keritot/13.txt`

Keritot 13 – How Fast One Must Eat
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjzUVxPbrWPKcAFwOxpIsQuPIRLu2CLD58MiM3knEiBNLnFQKiXz0uI-crIQAAHwBO59fvqjT1FRne-9sR4uE5FoXLVDneLi9HIZObK-3Gn3IjanwZWC23ugcf-KHqDflSAe-VHg12nnH3-/s1600/+Hendrick+Terbrugghen+-+The+Merry+Drinker.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjzUVxPbrWPKcAFwOxpIsQuPIRLu2CLD58MiM3knEiBNLnFQKiXz0uI-crIQAAHwBO59fvqjT1FRne-9sR4uE5FoXLVDneLi9HIZObK-3Gn3IjanwZWC23ugcf-KHqDflSAe-VHg12nnH3-/s320/+Hendrick+Terbrugghen+-+The+Merry+Drinker.jpg" width="252" /></a>If one eats very slowly, this is not considered eating at all. Thus, if he ate half an olive volume of a prohibited substance, and then another half, but took longer than a certain time period, he is not liable. How slow is slow?
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Meir says that we estimate how long it would take a person to eat the food if it had be crumbled into pieces as small as parched grain, and then eaten one by one. However, the Sages say that this time is measured by how long it would take a person to eat half a loaf of bread, four egg-volumes, and some say, three egg-volumes. The bread for measurement is made of wheat, which is eaten faster than barley, and in practice this time limit is between three to nine minutes. There is also an opinion that one can eat  as slow as he wants, as long as he does not pause for the time it takes a normal person to eat half a loaf.
<br />
<br />
Consequently, if a Kohen drank a quarter of a “log” of wine (about 30 milliliters), during the time that it takes to eat a half a loaf of bread, he is forbidden to enter the Temple to perform service. After the Torah prohibits Kohanim from serving in the Temple while drunk, it continues to say that he needs to “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=10#P2984">Distinguish between the sacred and profaned, permitted and forbidden, and teach the sons of Israel</a>.” By extension, one is not a allowed to render decisions on the matter of law while drunk. However, one is allowed to teach the Talmud.
<br />
<br />
Art: Hendrick Terbrugghen - The Merry Drinker

---

### content/keritot/14.txt
<a id="src-00182"></a>

**Source file:** `content/keritot/14.txt`

Keritot 14 – One Meal, Five Transgressions
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi5lg8OK3BZanE5lKcS_x80prKMujPAStvxl14N3DcCWtCcTtu5QEDGGyQOIeC_Q8vEDH4LrCKyjN9Mvdzo5aGDfuqSSxUVRlAAo1jT4GyPqqLdvXjqJe-2IWCFzNkubwfMMFKrraMNY1pR/s1600/Thomas+Gainsborough+-+Portrait+of+the+Artist's+Daughters.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi5lg8OK3BZanE5lKcS_x80prKMujPAStvxl14N3DcCWtCcTtu5QEDGGyQOIeC_Q8vEDH4LrCKyjN9Mvdzo5aGDfuqSSxUVRlAAo1jT4GyPqqLdvXjqJe-2IWCFzNkubwfMMFKrraMNY1pR/s320/Thomas+Gainsborough+-+Portrait+of+the+Artist's+Daughters.jpg" width="267" /></a>One can eat a piece of food and be liable for four sin-offerings and a guilt-offering: if he was ritually impure and ate prohibited fat, which was left over from sacrifices, on Yom Kippur. Rabbi Meir says that if it was Shabbat and he carried food in this mouth, he is liable for a fifth sin-offering, but the Sages respond that it doesn't come it, since it is a different group of prohibitions.
<br />
<br />
What is the count? He (1) ate sacrificial meat in the state of ritual impurity, (2) ate prohibited fat, (3) ate leftover sacrifices, (4) ate on Yom Kippur. Additionally, since the fat was from a consecrated animal, he used consecrated property and needs to bring a guilt-offering.
<br />
<br />
One can do a single act of cohabitation and be liable for six sin-offerings: if he cohabits with his daughter, who is his sister, his brother's wife, his father's brother's wife, a married woman, and was not in a mikva. How is that possible? He had an incestuous relationship with his mother, from which a daughter was born. The daughter married his (paternal) brother. After her husband died, this daughter married his father's brother. He then had committed incest with her, without her going to the mikva.
<br />
<br />
Art: Thomas Gainsborough - Portrait of the Artist's Daughters

---

### content/keritot/15.txt
<a id="src-00183"></a>

**Source file:** `content/keritot/15.txt`

Keritot 15 – Questions That Rabbi Akiva Asked
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiGU1lBsG0zd1FF966JkXNq6HfDR03bITZwh-PGe_uAYH_-NlkWObFoFtHTT7vj1YHyyWJEmlRM9F4CnVusH9r7Z44nuqIWaYcK6yYH5SrTSEfPTTSrPaxFFFSvNeOZjdw_p0wjdYJqIqvZ/s1600/Sofonisba+Anguissola+-+Two+Sisters+and+a+Brother+of+the+Artist.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="253" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiGU1lBsG0zd1FF966JkXNq6HfDR03bITZwh-PGe_uAYH_-NlkWObFoFtHTT7vj1YHyyWJEmlRM9F4CnVusH9r7Z44nuqIWaYcK6yYH5SrTSEfPTTSrPaxFFFSvNeOZjdw_p0wjdYJqIqvZ/s320/Sofonisba+Anguissola+-+Two+Sisters+and+a+Brother+of+the+Artist.jpg" width="320" /></a>Rabban Gamliel and Rabbi Yehoshua went to the meat market of Ema'um, to buy an animal for the wedding feast of Rabban Gamliel's son. Rabbi Akiva met them there and involved them in a discussion. He asked, “If a man inadvertently cohabits with his sister, who is also his father's sister and his mother's sister, what is the law?
