### content/ketubot/84.txt
<a id="src-00299"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/84.txt`

Ketubot 84 – The wife, the creditor and the children
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0gQXiFEP51lg6VEbAoJV09fiUNbzFZMPAj07zp5D_YMSCC_tElXGEIPkBfwQs6WWGjMtj0XINv1leb-UFB87khrL6vID-DI-WhnbiETIghfH1TGD7RNDmTp2dKREVq_Z_VFd2zt82Kvz_/s1600/Group+portrait+of+a+gentleman+and+his+wife,+and+their+four+children+by+Gerbrand+Ban.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="245" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj0gQXiFEP51lg6VEbAoJV09fiUNbzFZMPAj07zp5D_YMSCC_tElXGEIPkBfwQs6WWGjMtj0XINv1leb-UFB87khrL6vID-DI-WhnbiETIghfH1TGD7RNDmTp2dKREVq_Z_VFd2zt82Kvz_/s1600/Group+portrait+of+a+gentleman+and+his+wife,+and+their+four+children+by+Gerbrand+Ban.jpg" width="320" /></a>When someone dies, his wife wants the Ketubah, his creditors – monies owed to them, and his children want the entire inheritance without paying his debts to anyone.
<br />
<br />
However, his wife can only take the land since this is what she relied on when getting married, and so too his creditors. The children automatically get all movables and all precious objects.
<br />
<br />
What happens to his things that are deposited with somebody, such as at a bank in a safe deposit box? Since the children have not yet taken possession of them, the court should give them to the underdog, the wife, or the creditor – this is the opinion of Rabbi Tarfon. Rabbi Akiva argues: you cannot base judgment on the feeling of mercy; the objects are given to the children or other inheritors to whom they rightfully belong. Even if the wife or creditor seizes the valuables, the court takes them away from her.
<br />
<br />
Today, when people don't own the land as commonly as they used to, the question is moot since the wife gets her Ketubah paid from all valuables the husband has left. Also, everybody agrees that there is a moral obligation on the children to pay their father's debts; it's just that they cannot be forced to do so.
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Group portrait of a gentleman and his wife and their four children by Gerbrand Ban

---

### content/ketubot/85.txt
<a id="src-00300"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/85.txt`

Ketubot 85 – Taking the law into one's own hands
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhf4LpSJ2fn8LYX44jTWZig0cpky5dVkdHlIBf3vZChucSPuDlbNR1R6pYOIE_yeWfq77n-tK8RuOAm2M814VDk-IVsHK9RMafYUX7-ov5cQl3B1YsodihJvtCnZYhuWJTid0LP26KdhiFZ/s1600/Towing+the+Boat+by+Winslow+Homer.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="182" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhf4LpSJ2fn8LYX44jTWZig0cpky5dVkdHlIBf3vZChucSPuDlbNR1R6pYOIE_yeWfq77n-tK8RuOAm2M814VDk-IVsHK9RMafYUX7-ov5cQl3B1YsodihJvtCnZYhuWJTid0LP26KdhiFZ/s1600/Towing+the+Boat+by+Winslow+Homer.jpg" width="320" /></a>We mentioned that <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/04/ketubot-84-wife-creditor-and-children.html">when a man dies, his creditors, who usually have a little claim against the man's heirs, can somewhat take the law into their own hands and seize the </a>deceased's property. Here is a story.
<br />
<br />
A man died, and his creditor, Yeimar, sent an agent to seize the man's boat. The agent did so, and as he was towing the boat, he was met by Rav Pappa and Rav Huna. They told the agent, "You are just an agent, not a creditor, so you have no right to seize anything since you deprive other creditors!" Then they seized the boat themselves because they, too, loaned money to the deceased. 
<br />
<br />
So now Rav Pappa rowed the boat while Rav Huna pulled it with the rope, each claiming that he thus acquired the boat. In this way, they came to Rava to (in the language of the Bard) "try whose right, of thine or mine, is most in this boat." 
<br />
<br />
Rava told them, "White geese, you strip clothes off people!" That was a compliment: white because they were old and gray, and geese because it is a sign of wisdom in a dream.  Rava continued, "The law is like Rabbi Akiva, who only allows you to seize the property while the debtor is alive, not after his death!"
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Towing the Boat by Winslow Homer<br />
<br />

---

### content/ketubot/86.txt
<a id="src-00301"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/86.txt`

Ketubot 86 – Trust
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh8vPDuWmc6bnvYk-oWVxk8np_gFiKLwiZGmba4qni3MuwWjEXWDarBdbqrBnXo3MTpUWzgTUiRbC8eU49j2OBTmN7BE56tg2_o9koAHNNZMO02wKMDd5B2vBFE04SSNxSXAMDB4IiDOcT6/s1600/Young+Italian+Woman+from+Papigno+with+Her+Spindle+by+Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh8vPDuWmc6bnvYk-oWVxk8np_gFiKLwiZGmba4qni3MuwWjEXWDarBdbqrBnXo3MTpUWzgTUiRbC8eU49j2OBTmN7BE56tg2_o9koAHNNZMO02wKMDd5B2vBFE04SSNxSXAMDB4IiDOcT6/s1600/Young+Italian+Woman+from+Papigno+with+Her+Spindle+by+Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot.jpg" width="196" /></a>An oath is a serious thing, and nobody can impose an oath on a person at will, not even a court. There must be a reason, such as a case where one admits to part of the claim and says, "It is true that I owe you money but less than what you say." Then the oath is in order.<br />
<br />
However, if the husband appointed his wife a storekeeper or overseer for his business, he can ask for an oath at any time without a definite claim. This applies to any business partner of whom one may have a suspicion of embezzlement.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Eliezer says that the husband can impose an oath in any case because it is unavoidable that the wife is an overseer over her spindle and dough. But the Sages say, "One cannot live with a snake in the same basket." If the husband suspects her so much, the wife may not be able to live with him.<br />
<br />
Art: <br />
Young Italian Woman from Papigno with Her Spindle by Jean-Baptiste-Camille Corot

---

### content/ketubot/87.txt
<a id="src-00302"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/87.txt`

Ketubot 87 – Repairing trust
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjo6Letx1aOBP-wZz5iMPoYCrgtelpslESO5mu_VOU-fLgsmDCGGDi8m6c9rm-Y6NBnlZywLCgQqndvXyiEM5jQV5FaGaBLHsxz7uC3NYi-HSVK2oskvAbfnA0t_IKxwg19CYaBRfqJGe1l/s1600/The+Orphan+By+Walter+Langley.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="239" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjo6Letx1aOBP-wZz5iMPoYCrgtelpslESO5mu_VOU-fLgsmDCGGDi8m6c9rm-Y6NBnlZywLCgQqndvXyiEM5jQV5FaGaBLHsxz7uC3NYi-HSVK2oskvAbfnA0t_IKxwg19CYaBRfqJGe1l/s1600/The+Orphan+By+Walter+Langley.jpg" width="320" /></a><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/04/trust.html">Earlier, we learned</a> that a husband may sometimes impose an oath on his wife that she did not embezzle any of his property. We also mentioned that the possibility of this oath may lead to mistrust between the husband and the wife.
<br />
<br />
To prevent this, the husband may write for her a document stating that he "Will have no right to impose an oath or vow on her," and he then waives this right, although he can still impose the oath on her successor. He may give up the right to impose an oath on others.
<br />
<br />
The purpose of this oath was often to verify that the wife has not yet collected her Ketubah and that she is coming with a valid claim on the total amount. However, there was a strong incentive for the widow to take this oath, even if she had already collected some or all of the payment. She rationalized that she was entitled to extra compensation because of the care she would have to give to the orphans. The courts stopped accepting this oath, and widows had no way of collecting the Ketubah.  To rectify that, the Sages gave the orphans the right to ask her to pronounce a vow (such as "The use of my husband's property is prohibited to me if I embezzled"), and then she gets the Ketubah.<br />
<br />
The standard case where an oath would be present is where the husband claims that he paid his wife the Ketubah, and she says she received only a partial payment. The oath is in order because the one who pays usually remembers his payment well, but the one who receives it is not as careful about the details. The oath makes him better go through his recollections.
<br />
<br />
Art: The Orphan By Walter Langley

---

### content/ketubot/88.txt
<a id="src-00303"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/88.txt`

Ketubot 88 – Further arguments between the widow and the orphans
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjqBJXbS_smKKlHshmRUQrq9mZfuqVRXChkmPc5U-W8BcWcyZMxPj2YTJp_KxrE54lkdTmFdQGUk_pnV487tJEkArPPvgj5LNZsyORs0HQf3-BKDbcHlApOcSHn018vbZm29-mYkDe_O6Rw/s1600/The+Children+by+Henri-Jules-Jean+Geoffroy.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjqBJXbS_smKKlHshmRUQrq9mZfuqVRXChkmPc5U-W8BcWcyZMxPj2YTJp_KxrE54lkdTmFdQGUk_pnV487tJEkArPPvgj5LNZsyORs0HQf3-BKDbcHlApOcSHn018vbZm29-mYkDe_O6Rw/s1600/The+Children+by+Henri-Jules-Jean+Geoffroy.jpg" width="320" /></a><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/05/ketubot-87-repairing-trust.html">We learned earlier</a> that when the widow comes to court to collect her Ketubah, she must take an oath that her husband, while alive, did not already pay the Ketubah to her. Incidentally, such oaths apply to orphans as well. 
<br />
<br />
For example, say that the children of one family, after their father died, claim that the father of the other family (who also died) borrowed money from their father. The borrower's children say,"  "Our father told us that he indeed borrowed, but repaid" – the borrower's children must take an oath. This applies when their father says ""I paid"" for then the existence of the loan document does not prove anything. 
<br />
<br />
However, if their father said,"  "I never borrowed"" then it works against him."  "I never borrowed" means that he, of course, never repaid. Since the loan is uncontested and documented, no oath helps, and the orphans need to pay the debt. Furthermore, this is only when the children are adults, but minors are more protected from the claims of others.<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;The Children by Henri-Jules-Jean Geoffroy

---

### content/ketubot/89.txt
<a id="src-00304"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/89.txt`

Ketubot 89 – How to collect divorce settlement
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjt2sIZIDGVmBXZqdK99xHEbYogwWupuydyQzMQ_kvlJR0tpjgL5_kGtKIsYdh-47iayamto6Waq2aQEsFdY7jmvBbHZY8Ha-zucqy4-q_gZu8IrVrs10ByLqsXHZsxYPM0HQb6NugUx1hW/s1600/A+group+portrait+of+a+husband,+wife+and+their+child+by++Francis+Alleyne.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="262" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjt2sIZIDGVmBXZqdK99xHEbYogwWupuydyQzMQ_kvlJR0tpjgL5_kGtKIsYdh-47iayamto6Waq2aQEsFdY7jmvBbHZY8Ha-zucqy4-q_gZu8IrVrs10ByLqsXHZsxYPM0HQb6NugUx1hW/s320/A+group+portrait+of+a+husband,+wife+and+their+child+by++Francis+Alleyne.jpg" width="320" /></a>Imagine that a woman comes to court and presents a Get with which her husband divorced her. Then she wants him to pay the amount of the Ketubah. However, she does not have the Ketubah document, claiming it was lost. Normally, she should not be able to collect: anybody who wants to collect payment should present a loan document (in this case, it is the Ketubah). If it is lost, his money is lost.
<br />
<br />
However, since the Ketubah is the enactment of the court, it has the same power as though the document was actually present, so she can collect the money. Her former husband's claim that he paid the Ketubah is not believed. They should have torn the Get, given him her Ketubah or the payment receipt if he paid.
<br />
<br />
Consider the next case: the woman comes with the Ketubah but not with a Get. She wants the payment, but the husband claims that based on the rule above, she already collected her payment with her Get, claiming that the Ketubah was lost, and now she has put away the Get and produced the Ketubah. As for his receipt, he says he lost it. In this case, the husband wins because she does not have a Get and indeed could be collecting the money twice. 
<br />
<br />
Rabban Gamliel adds that in the “time of danger,” people were afraid to keep their Get or Ketubah because the idolaters were persecuting the Jews for the performance of commandments. From this time on, a woman can collect her payment even without the Get because she may have destroyed it right after divorce. 
<br />
<br />
Art: A group portrait of a husband, wife, and their child by  Francis Alleyne

---

### content/ketubot/9.txt
<a id="src-00305"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/9.txt`

Ketubot 9 – Claims of "not a virgin"
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihsQUhEUwVb3p3TuvmFewCT0dFCqhtOACZXweXa-a5dL11APEASqEK3XIyt8J2rrnHywMGtwBjRGORf4fThIWkkjyACMVMX05GDo8EI9ASYLxrLlFgJZUxjUFCe7mzANSTEbo5Lp-aeP4Q/s1600/The+Hesitant+Betrothed+by+Auguste+Toulmouche.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihsQUhEUwVb3p3TuvmFewCT0dFCqhtOACZXweXa-a5dL11APEASqEK3XIyt8J2rrnHywMGtwBjRGORf4fThIWkkjyACMVMX05GDo8EI9ASYLxrLlFgJZUxjUFCe7mzANSTEbo5Lp-aeP4Q/s1600/The+Hesitant+Betrothed+by+Auguste+Toulmouche.jpg" width="265" /></a>If the husband claims "I found an open opening" - that is, he felt that his wife was not a virgin, then he may not be believed as far as the girl is concerned, but he is believed to impose a restriction on himself, and he now cannot live with her.  This is the opinion of Rabbi Elazar. Others say he would not be believed even for himself since his feelings are subjective. 
<br />
<br />
But according to Rabbi Elazar, even if we believe the husband's feelings, what evidence is there that she was unfaithful to him while being engaged? Perhaps this happened before engagement, and even if not, maybe she is from a family where women do not have significant hymen? – Rabbi Elazar's rules apply only in the case where one betrothed a girl when she was younger than three and married her when she grew up.
<br />
<br />
Shmuel says that the husband is believed to the point that her Ketubah (marriage obligation paid in case of divorce) is void, and he does not have to pay it. But why would he be believed? Perhaps he is just trying to get out of his obligation? – Shmuel will reply that one would not trouble himself to make a wedding feast, only to lose her the next day. 
<br />
<br />
Art: The Hesitant Betrothed by Auguste Toulmouche

---

### content/ketubot/90.txt
<a id="src-00306"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/90.txt`

Ketubot 90 – Serial marriages and divorces
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgAIAGi8Sin_5xCzlIxoTBNUr2qJoWHnjEVtiAwlNVRl4VxEkrpTPSg8XdXMYqJsMejV4lsg2mGYCRM-3mDDVMELIok4dsbd9kyc_NKSOdDuuQ3kfnH4as1SuLcvRARRLSQH-nGP-TAtr3B/s1600/Husband+and+Wife+by+Lorenzo+Lotto.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="261" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgAIAGi8Sin_5xCzlIxoTBNUr2qJoWHnjEVtiAwlNVRl4VxEkrpTPSg8XdXMYqJsMejV4lsg2mGYCRM-3mDDVMELIok4dsbd9kyc_NKSOdDuuQ3kfnH4as1SuLcvRARRLSQH-nGP-TAtr3B/s320/Husband+and+Wife+by+Lorenzo+Lotto.jpg" width="320" /></a>If a woman comes to court with two Get and two Ketubah documents, we assume that things were just as she describes: her husband married her, divorced, then re-married, and wrote a new Ketubah. She collects two payments. 
<br />
<br />
However, if she produces two Ketubah documents but only one Get, we assume they are from one marriage, but he simply wrote another Ketubah for her. She collects only one. Finally, if she has two Get documents from him but only one Ketubah, he must have married (and divorced) her again, but anybody who re-marries his wife relies on the original Ketubah, so she again collects only one payment.
<br />
<br />
If one was married to two wives and died, and did not leave enough to pay both, then the Ketubah of the first way has priority over the Ketubah of the second. If the wives died before collecting their Ketubah payments, then the heirs of the first wife have priority over the heirs of the second one.
<br />
<br />
Art: Husband and Wife by Lorenzo Lotto

---

### content/ketubot/91.txt
<a id="src-00307"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/91.txt`

Ketubot 91 – Two groups of children from two wives want the inheritance
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZX0ayiVgkfhNi-rjf-SNjv7oSpKgWYuDzd39M2NgH1GFDYJ8g8bnDUqy0trgZaivTCo-_PiHhucdvq7UyidGQJhpDjylznqd7Mni8FexZ6VAWvDmXNEeweHxBnWoent8Uksk810yIzZoS/s1600/The+Three+Fishers+Wives+by+Mrs+Henry+Harewood+Robinson.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZX0ayiVgkfhNi-rjf-SNjv7oSpKgWYuDzd39M2NgH1GFDYJ8g8bnDUqy0trgZaivTCo-_PiHhucdvq7UyidGQJhpDjylznqd7Mni8FexZ6VAWvDmXNEeweHxBnWoent8Uksk810yIzZoS/s320/The+Three+Fishers+Wives+by+Mrs+Henry+Harewood+Robinson.jpg" width="252" /></a>When people were allowed to have more than one wife, fathers were reluctant to give large dowries to their daughters. They were apprehensive that when their daughter and her husband died, the inheritance would go to the children of the other wife. Therefore, the Sages established a rule that when the children claim the inheritance, they can ask for their late mother's Ketubah first. Then they would divide the remaining estate equally with the other wives' children. This is called "Ketubah of the (male) children."
<br />
<br />
Now imagine that it did happen: someone was married to two wives, they both died, then he died, and now the children all want the inheritance. This is where the above rule would kick in.
<br />
<br />
However, if there is not enough money to pay both the Ketubah of the first and the second wife, then there will be no leftover inheritance to divide: everything will be paid out as a Ketubah payment. Then the law of the inheritance from the Torah will be abrogated completely!  - at least in this case. The Sages did not want this outcome, so they limited their rule to only cases where there was enough money to pay both Ketubahs and some. If there is not enough, then the rule above is not used; instead, everyone divides equally, which is the Torah law. Even if one group of the children wants to add money to the inheritance so that there is enough for the Ketubah and gain by getting their mother's larger Ketubah, they are not listened to.
<br />
<br />
Art: The Three Fishers Wives by Mrs. Henry Harewood Robinson

---

### content/ketubot/92.txt
<a id="src-00308"></a>

**Source file:** `content/ketubot/92.txt`

Ketubot 92 – Mind twisting problems 
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTAyn1XHhCFyr7UUr3bZhXwcCN90EAcbSN093q4ECsiVXcItf4qXEX0ErTW1Oo53OJbwpaCe9saqi80jxodta-3ImhVvSRb6afqGgQlMsJJUJpv1SGrCuWDtBDPqAj1XU5bwrBhRsxAIFN/s1600/A+thinking+girl+by+Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTAyn1XHhCFyr7UUr3bZhXwcCN90EAcbSN093q4ECsiVXcItf4qXEX0ErTW1Oo53OJbwpaCe9saqi80jxodta-3ImhVvSRb6afqGgQlMsJJUJpv1SGrCuWDtBDPqAj1XU5bwrBhRsxAIFN/s320/A+thinking+girl+by+Jean-Baptiste-Camille+Corot.jpg" width="255" /></a>The Talmud first discusses a problem where our&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/05/ketubot-91-two-groups-of-children-from.html">previous ruling</a> is used for comparison and then continues with a series of difficulties helpful in training the mind.<br />
<br />
Let us say that debtor D owes $1,000 to his creditor C. Meanwhile, he owns two houses and sells them to buyer B, each for $500.
<br />
<br />
Now C wants his money, and D cannot pay, so C repossesses the first of the houses because real estate always guarantees the loan. B loses one of the houses he bought. Still, he wants to keep the second one, so he comes with $1,000 cash to C and proposes the following: if C wants to consider the first house, the one he just repossessed, as worth $1,000, then all is well; but if not, then this $1,000 should cover both houses, and C gets his money but loses the repossessed house.
<br />
<br />
Rami bar Chama wanted to say that this is precisely our previous rule: there, the orphans could not<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2015/05/ketubot-91-two-groups-of-children-from.html">&nbsp;artificially inflate the worth of their mother's Ketubah</a>, &nbsp;so here too, the argument of considering the $500 house worth $1,000 does not stand. Without this, the second part of the proposal does not stand either, and the creditor can collect the second house. However, Rava reversed him: in the case of orphans, their suggestion would hurt the other group of children, but in our case, the creditor would always get his $1,000 loan back.
<br />
<br />The following cases are abbreviated with mnemonics ("thousand" - that is our case, "hundred," "mitzvah of Ketubah"...). Such abbreviations, or "signs," contain clues to the mystical meaning of the subjects discussed.
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;A thinking girl by Jean-Baptiste-Camille Corot

### content/kiddushin/10.txt
<a id="src-00316"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/10.txt`

Kiddushin 10 –  Betrothal by relations
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUQp2Okzdn_Xt7Nrw3ZO49G-rKzWQ_kXvL_NzrJeh5QfgkVYwNAOKhKd0WAMkOcBiyK0FMcy0WDb3xFY6kTqMIi779WcKT97z5W8AP2FhWbTczTPZs_HGY56OGKSSd5tSvBRnAZ9rjM9Rv/s1600/Wedding+at+the+Photographer%2527s+by+Pascal+Adolphe+Jean+Dagnan-Bouveret.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="226" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUQp2Okzdn_Xt7Nrw3ZO49G-rKzWQ_kXvL_NzrJeh5QfgkVYwNAOKhKd0WAMkOcBiyK0FMcy0WDb3xFY6kTqMIi779WcKT97z5W8AP2FhWbTczTPZs_HGY56OGKSSd5tSvBRnAZ9rjM9Rv/s320/Wedding+at+the+Photographer%2527s+by+Pascal+Adolphe+Jean+Dagnan-Bouveret.jpg" width="320" /></a>A woman can be betrothed by having relations with her, and there are two different ways to derive this, one from the words, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=22#P5487">Woman who cohabited with her husband</a>," and another – from  "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=24">If a man marries a woman or possesses her</a>."<br />
<br />
Is there a practical difference between these theoretical derivations? – Imagine that ten men cohabited anally with a betrothed girl who is a virgin. According to the first way of learning, she is still a virgin after each act since only the husband makes her a non-virgin with anal cohabitation; therefore, each man is to be punished by stoning, specified for violating a betrothed virgin. According to the second approach, though, she is a non-virgin after the first act, and the next nine men are subject to a lighter punishment of strangulation. 
<br />
<br />
Exactly what stage of cohabitation accomplishes kiddushin? Typically, for infidelity and prohibited relations, the first stage of relations, member touching (discussed in <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/11/yevamot-56-what-is-legally-considered.html">another place</a>), is considered the act. However, for kiddushin, it is different. Since the man intends complete penetration, he achieves kiddushin only when this is done. Practical difference? – Can he inherit his wife or bury her if he is a Kohen.
<br />
<br />
Since there are two stages in marriage, betrothal (dedication) and chuppah (bringing the bride into the husband's domain), a question may be asked: if one does betrothal through cohabitation, does it accomplish the second stage of marriage – that is, is the second cohabitation or a chuppah still needed? After multiple arguments back and forth, it is concluded that cohabitation only accomplished betrothal, but a chuppah is still required.
<br />
<br />
Art: Wedding at the Photographer's by Pascal Adolphe Jean Dagnan-Bouveret

---

### content/kiddushin/11.txt
<a id="src-00317"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/11.txt`

Kiddushin 11 - How Much Money is Needed for Kiddushin?
<div><br /></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEimG7oolot7zs8pwVnR7XDDYdQ7dPIRW278slsrPyIz09bNxMFnlCaOuvugp3Uja4xXTIW-FqRodxnH2toDV4uY79yMUGgyoGmgaBubKSPhbpihxu0kVk-35WO0nD1FJr-uiX8OfnXgtxlRTixiV38a1p72fmYDeqDL53sKpXlERwWS_P8f3Qeic-o77iHh/s1024/Godfried%20Schalken%20or%20Schalcken%20-%20A%20Candlelight%20Scene%20A%20Man%20Offering%20a%20Gold%20Chain%20and%20Coins%20to%20-%20(MeisterDrucke-223020).jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="835" data-original-width="1024" height="261" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEimG7oolot7zs8pwVnR7XDDYdQ7dPIRW278slsrPyIz09bNxMFnlCaOuvugp3Uja4xXTIW-FqRodxnH2toDV4uY79yMUGgyoGmgaBubKSPhbpihxu0kVk-35WO0nD1FJr-uiX8OfnXgtxlRTixiV38a1p72fmYDeqDL53sKpXlERwWS_P8f3Qeic-o77iHh/s320/Godfried%20Schalken%20or%20Schalcken%20-%20A%20Candlelight%20Scene%20A%20Man%20Offering%20a%20Gold%20Chain%20and%20Coins%20to%20-%20(MeisterDrucke-223020).jpg" width="320" /></a></div><div>Beit Shammai required a minimum of a dinar for Kiddushin, a coin with silver content equivalent to 96 barley grains. What is their reason?</div><div>
<br />
Self-esteem? - No, because then some would require more.<br />
<br />
Is it because when Torah mentions Kesef (money), it means a silver coin? This withstands questioning.<br />
<br />
<br />Or is it because we compare a bride to a Jewish maidservant, who is redeemed by diminishing the price for years served, so she must start with a dinar? This also withstands questioning.<br />
<br />
The law follows Beit Hillel, who requires only a minimal coin (prutah, about 5 cents).<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A Candlelight Scene: A Man Offering a Gold Chain and Coins to a Girl Seated on a Bed</div></div>

### content/kiddushin/12.txt
<a id="src-00318"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/12.txt`

Kiddushin 12 - Betrothal with Correct Value
<div><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUqXTKQQcRxwfrRfUqo0gK1EN0amz-sHj4F0SBjtM-BWBgFL6yf0PXvbSct2nEYDIHAFOR73wtbZpqEiCnPGDLGq9elruBS3Ptrg7UHEs9QQgkilZYJ0JXHxrlydbGngBwMF55wYzHVoy47zxoS-WctGSGmzY5ICddPuv0Lm93bct0a4JBJyq9npQiM6gW/s781/wedding%20present.png" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em; text-align: center;"><img border="0" data-original-height="626" data-original-width="781" height="256" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUqXTKQQcRxwfrRfUqo0gK1EN0amz-sHj4F0SBjtM-BWBgFL6yf0PXvbSct2nEYDIHAFOR73wtbZpqEiCnPGDLGq9elruBS3Ptrg7UHEs9QQgkilZYJ0JXHxrlydbGngBwMF55wYzHVoy47zxoS-WctGSGmzY5ICddPuv0Lm93bct0a4JBJyq9npQiM6gW/s320/wedding%20present.png" width="320" /></a></div><div>According to Beit Hillel, the minimum amount needed for Kiddushin is a small coin called a prutah. This does not mean the smallest coin in circulation. Instead, it is the value of one-half of a barleycorn of silver, estimated anew each generation.</div><div>
<br />
If a man betrothed a woman by handing her a date with a value of less than a prutah, there is still a possibility that, in some places, this date is worth more than a prutah. Therefore, he should repeat the Kiddushin with a definite value or give her a Get.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Wedding Presents by James Wells Champney</div></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/13.txt
<a id="src-00319"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/13.txt`

Kiddushin 13 - Questionable Goods
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiqrYBwMLMt0yRSgwpxPVuNS4ORjiR30I9F8Hb1zbwYevpea2uvJdawrxG9_MPhUeCHxYwcl1RJDYfY8QrxuU4HBm2RlEm_6hzlEtkzdhUXKzXZrNlKdoG_vdBkOaCQMX1UNaHpsQDbrOMQ/s1600-h/Francis+Campbell+Boileau+Cadell.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5260195840228470322" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiqrYBwMLMt0yRSgwpxPVuNS4ORjiR30I9F8Hb1zbwYevpea2uvJdawrxG9_MPhUeCHxYwcl1RJDYfY8QrxuU4HBm2RlEm_6hzlEtkzdhUXKzXZrNlKdoG_vdBkOaCQMX1UNaHpsQDbrOMQ/s320/Francis+Campbell+Boileau+Cadell.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 246px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">A man betrothed a woman with a mat of myrtle twigs. After she accepted it, those present said to him, "But the mat is not worth a prutah!" He replied, "Let her become betrothed with the four coins wrapped inside." The woman retained the money. Is she betrothed?<br />
<br />
Since her silence occurred after the money had been given, it is meaningless, and she is not betrothed.<br />
<br />
If a man betrothed a woman with goods he grabbed or stole from her, this betrothal is valid, provided they had previously agreed to marry one another.</span><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Black Hat by&nbsp;Francis Campbell Boileau Cadell</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/14.txt
<a id="src-00320"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/14.txt`

Kiddushin 14 - Why The Death of the Husband Sets the Wife Free
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhzYhg1MMwORtOwTiVQxVRO0_2nG6a5Q9_UKsKbTxvldGxckMOC4bz8eYD_hLJge-LDLwzZgq1UlIhdcYEGDV6h9yasK9ngiBl-Sh7-JTUOKXLP9iqrEKqIB2UVqvehX2Ws_DwpNFqxA7Rr/s1600-h/Armand-Carrel-1800-36-On-His-Deathbed,-1836+-+Copy.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5260202743287344994" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhzYhg1MMwORtOwTiVQxVRO0_2nG6a5Q9_UKsKbTxvldGxckMOC4bz8eYD_hLJge-LDLwzZgq1UlIhdcYEGDV6h9yasK9ngiBl-Sh7-JTUOKXLP9iqrEKqIB2UVqvehX2Ws_DwpNFqxA7Rr/s320/Armand-Carrel-1800-36-On-His-Deathbed,-1836+-+Copy.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 254px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>A married woman acquires herself back through the death of her husband. Why?<div><br /></div><div>Maybe the husband caused the prohibition, and he also removed it? No, because she is still forbidden to marry his son from the previous marriage or his father.</div><div><br /></div><div>Or maybe a widow is forbidden to marry the High Priest, so she must be allowed to marry everyone else? No, perhaps she would still be transgressing a positive commandment.</div><div><br /></div><div>Maybe when Jewish soldiers went to war, "And whichever man betrothed a wife and did not yet take her, let him return, lest he dies in battle and another man takes her" - is valid proof!</div><div><br /><div>Art: Armand Carrel On His Deathbed by Ary Scheffer</div>
</div>

### content/kiddushin/15.txt

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/15.txt`

Kiddushin 15 - Hebrew Servant Can Marry a Non-Jewish Slave-Woman
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgQT6kLlTpZ6_S7UuH9FeGHa0pdnPoPxMCezm1ohPI1-NIDw3ICxM5ngKWQ-Go0A3-hDHgnSeTkmGH7oNeoytG8BU5XxRhx8tVFUso026nXDqUac1S7SG69Z9hw17cm8-uTQtEd87IiWUne/s1600-h/sweerts.jpg"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5260574881629700914" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgQT6kLlTpZ6_S7UuH9FeGHa0pdnPoPxMCezm1ohPI1-NIDw3ICxM5ngKWQ-Go0A3-hDHgnSeTkmGH7oNeoytG8BU5XxRhx8tVFUso026nXDqUac1S7SG69Z9hw17cm8-uTQtEd87IiWUne/s320/sweerts.jpg" style="cursor: hand; float: left; height: 245px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a>There are four categories of Hebrew servants discussed in the Torah:<br />
<br />
<br />
1. A man who steals and can not repay, who is sold by the courts to pay the one he robbed;<br />
2. A girl under the age of twelve who is sold by her father;<br />
3. A man who sells himself because of his poverty;<br />
4. A Jew who sells himself to a gentile.<br /><br /><div>
A servant sold by the court can be given a Canaanite slave woman to have children.<br /><br />Even today, there is a way for a mamzer (illegitimate) to have kosher children from a Canaanite slave woman.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Seated Man with a Youth &amp; a Servant in an Interior by Michael Sweerts</div></div>

### content/kiddushin/16.txt
<a id="src-00322"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/16.txt`

Kiddushin 16 - How Hebrew Servant Regains His Freedom
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjBETeJ5-sqy1rl9Jo4sizvK76rv5bGRuvmOlajYUn1jt4TWwexKGIIIlmhODrPJpTwkuJNImgKTp3R6_hnMkpb3W6tDmGI3hZ2FSEpB8hmt1dtB6P2v17bWLgvssvV2EKjnuySGTDLD-Vu/s1600-h/kiddushin16.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5260824994180960354" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjBETeJ5-sqy1rl9Jo4sizvK76rv5bGRuvmOlajYUn1jt4TWwexKGIIIlmhODrPJpTwkuJNImgKTp3R6_hnMkpb3W6tDmGI3hZ2FSEpB8hmt1dtB6P2v17bWLgvssvV2EKjnuySGTDLD-Vu/s320/kiddushin16.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 138px;" /></a>A Hebrew servant sold by the courts can gain his freedom back in one of four ways:<br />
<ul>
<li>completion of six years of service;</li>
<li>the onset of the Jubilee year;</li>
<li>paying his purchase price back to his master minus the cash equivalent of the years already served;</li>
<li>death of his master.</li>
</ul>
In addition to a Hebrew servant's ways, a Hebrew maidservant sold by her father goes free when she reaches twelve years of age and has “signs of physical maturity” (two pubic hairs).<br />
<br />
When a Hebrew servant or maidservant goes free, they receive severance gifts.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;The Farewell By Eugene De Blaas</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/17.txt
<a id="src-00323"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/17.txt`

Kiddushin 17 - Severance Gifts of Hebrew Servants
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYJGSUX7AQFvrR-VeDXCMwO7vsRKWOjM2rAxR3wcOio8PIgk27PiWjnLzKVY58bspaDHoQ9NBXifEB1jyFzcqS_Wswu1G9jhfgjzRGnfE0hAwv_Yk37FDWmfxOqvdwvSMke6rZWbVVwn9b/s1600-h/Jules+Breton+-+Harvesters.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5261329049292699826" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYJGSUX7AQFvrR-VeDXCMwO7vsRKWOjM2rAxR3wcOio8PIgk27PiWjnLzKVY58bspaDHoQ9NBXifEB1jyFzcqS_Wswu1G9jhfgjzRGnfE0hAwv_Yk37FDWmfxOqvdwvSMke6rZWbVVwn9b/s320/Jules+Breton+-+Harvesters.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 253px;" /></a>If a Hebrew servant had been ill for up to three years of his six-year term, he is not obligated to make up.<br />
<br />
What is the worth of severance gifts that a master must give to his departing servant? Three kinds of goods: sheep and goats, grain, and wine, for the total worth of thirty selah (equal to the penalty for goring a Canaanite slave), approximately $6,000.<br />
<br />
A Hebrew servant serves his term under the master's son but not his daughter or any other inheritor. A Hebrew maidservant is free if her master dies and does not serve anybody.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Harvesters by Jules Breton&nbsp;</div>

### content/kiddushin/18.txt
<a id="src-00324"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/18.txt`

Kiddushin 18 - Master or his Son to Marry Hebrew Maidservant
A Hebrew convert is like a newborn child and does not inherit his father, except by rabbinical ordinance. He has to tell his brothers, "Take these idols, and I will take the produce," before the idols come into his possession.<br />
<br />
A father can sell his daughter into servitude only once. Her master or master's son is expected to <a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgIYhphy6G3DsveX5HQgx4ya0c0ZGMI1e3H2Y0YTCEVJTu3PtP8xxSONngLo1yyqRkFF_y9_ywKvlRxJo3ADKa_NuVFAgdd8roMnkbiyF8X8CNlINYhoF7SL_-OdNRbJXyWmNyqhdRNaOQW/s1600-h/A+Fisherman+Goodbye.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5261682232736805330" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgIYhphy6G3DsveX5HQgx4ya0c0ZGMI1e3H2Y0YTCEVJTu3PtP8xxSONngLo1yyqRkFF_y9_ywKvlRxJo3ADKa_NuVFAgdd8roMnkbiyF8X8CNlINYhoF7SL_-OdNRbJXyWmNyqhdRNaOQW/s320/A+Fisherman+Goodbye.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 254px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>marry her and provide for her, with no additional Kiddushin money required.<br />
<br />
A Hebrew servant is sold for his theft if he can not repay, but only if what he owes exceeds the value of the six years of his servitude.<div><br /></div><div><div>Art: The Fisherman's Goodbye by Philip Lodewijk</div></div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/19.txt
<a id="src-00325"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/19.txt`

Kiddushin 19 - Designation of a Hebrew Maidservant as a Wife
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEih60ux6KU9Go0Jz_KxQ3F8Mw-EKlN7rbwc_TkfVQZisyoaBTWpm5qdsmDATPrv7tZgbzUXX-xZ0cu7b8eFnw3IPi7mXBo9TVfZcJtX2A30_WxyUHbqaydMpkudPEk02qnd4POOIOUM5VPB/s1600-h/Delort+Charles+Edouard+Edmon.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5261946056259882178" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEih60ux6KU9Go0Jz_KxQ3F8Mw-EKlN7rbwc_TkfVQZisyoaBTWpm5qdsmDATPrv7tZgbzUXX-xZ0cu7b8eFnw3IPi7mXBo9TVfZcJtX2A30_WxyUHbqaydMpkudPEk02qnd4POOIOUM5VPB/s320/Delort+Charles+Edouard+Edmon.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 193px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>A man who has bought a Hebrew maidservant can designate her as his wife, without the need for Kiddushin money, but with her knowledge. Can he do this for his son, who is a minor? Does the phrase "or to his son” mean that the son can be any age or must be like his father, an adult?<br />
<br />
Answer: While a nine-year-old CAN acquire a wife in a levirate marriage if his brother dies by having marital relations with her, the designation of a maidservant as a wife is not possible until the son is an adult.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Proposal by Charles Edouard Delort</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/2.txt
<a id="src-00326"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/2.txt`

Kiddushin 2 - Three ways to acquire a woman
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLikOYDa_ayweiBwf_j84d_ak7QnVvXQGpwjUQMYOmpB4dsoWtew7xdZ6DiHzIx43pCv3sBz05gwmw2-q7A9Vqwp2WMNNPaAZii-5v6z5nY-ucp87L3ZZt99qXG3pQltzbeLGGqhs7aujs/s1600/Jan+Josef+Horemans+the+Elder+-+Marriage+Contract.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLikOYDa_ayweiBwf_j84d_ak7QnVvXQGpwjUQMYOmpB4dsoWtew7xdZ6DiHzIx43pCv3sBz05gwmw2-q7A9Vqwp2WMNNPaAZii-5v6z5nY-ucp87L3ZZt99qXG3pQltzbeLGGqhs7aujs/s320/Jan+Josef+Horemans+the+Elder+-+Marriage+Contract.jpg" width="224" /></a>A wife can be acquired in one of three ways, and she acquires herself back in one of two ways.
<br />
<br />
She may be acquired through money, a document of betrothal, or cohabitation. Two witnesses are needed to testify in case of money and document. In case of acquisition by cohabitation (which is not encouraged), the witnesses testify to the declared intention and the seclusion.
<br />
<br />
She acquires herself back through a Get or through the death of her husband.
<br />
<br />
Passive use of “she is acquired” instead of “he acquires” teaches that a woman can only be acquired willingly, not against her will.
<br />
<br />
Art: Marriage Contract by Jan Josef Horemans the Elder

---

### content/kiddushin/20.txt
<a id="src-00327"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/20.txt`

Kiddushin 20 - Terms of Servitude
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgbmUfF6wIMhbAHkmQxN6MunTFmCX7uLiHLBPfPeQf1LsfSHx6n9LHwnByqyhaRFkpLbBmqqhaHVi74r2vPJaylJ9W1h4Ct4xuuXSE1i0_hPXGZjTOd6TQuI4DsBPsSg3btyaZBa-WPH_5S/s1600-h/Lucas+The+Younger+Cranach+-+The-Ill-Matched+Lovers.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5262275069457128882" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgbmUfF6wIMhbAHkmQxN6MunTFmCX7uLiHLBPfPeQf1LsfSHx6n9LHwnByqyhaRFkpLbBmqqhaHVi74r2vPJaylJ9W1h4Ct4xuuXSE1i0_hPXGZjTOd6TQuI4DsBPsSg3btyaZBa-WPH_5S/s320/Lucas+The+Younger+Cranach+-+The-Ill-Matched+Lovers.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 239px;" /></a>A father can sell his daughter as a Hebrew maidservant to his father (the girl's grandfather). Although the grandfather can not marry his granddaughter, he can designate her to marry his son, the girl's uncle, which the Torah allows.<br />
<br />
A master, who strikes a Canaanite slave and deprives him of his tooth or eye, must set him free. In contrast, a Hebrew servant receives payment but not freedom in this situation.<br />
<br />
If a servant has a wife or children when he begins his term of servitude, his master may give him a Canaanite slave-woman as a mate.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The-Ill-Matched Lovers by Lucas The Younger Cranach</div>

### content/kiddushin/21.txt
<a id="src-00328"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/21.txt`

Kiddushin 21 - Hebrew Servant Wants to be Free Again
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-zAfJT6P5nykldnB9svqCRYakdG0Z9wVOOb-pBZ4e_UmOg2fzIitAF0HjfGDA28mGfy_kuKnxz0CMk6MKP1wtF7bp-8-7Z4vMqPsqTFqOzr26NhzlS2OlJxgyL6ibCdgBmemlfga9NxJ1/s1600-h/Ludwig+Deutch+-+Leaving+the+Mosque.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5262692385052062386" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg-zAfJT6P5nykldnB9svqCRYakdG0Z9wVOOb-pBZ4e_UmOg2fzIitAF0HjfGDA28mGfy_kuKnxz0CMk6MKP1wtF7bp-8-7Z4vMqPsqTFqOzr26NhzlS2OlJxgyL6ibCdgBmemlfga9NxJ1/s320/Ludwig+Deutch+-+Leaving+the+Mosque.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 252px;" /></a><div>A Hebrew servant who has sold himself into servitude and wants to redeem himself early enjoys a special privilege: his redemption price is the lowest of his purchase price and the current service value for the remaining years.&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Through the sequence of Torah passages, we can deduce which transgressions caused him to become poor and sell himself. Still, now that he wants to become free again, he gets leniency.&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
He can reduce his remaining years of servitude with a partial payment, but this can result in either a gain or a loss if his price fluctuates.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Leaving the Mosque by Ludwig Deutch</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/22.txt
<a id="src-00329"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/22.txt`

Kiddushin 22 - Hebrew Servant Stays Forever Because Life is Good
<div style="margin-bottom: 0in;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiNV0ZzffOADFSvjZHCUwrPuAzGmSfn1OCIwHRs_ub5YdQuwoOYcLv8N7g-Nd74YUe-EzZO2XmJVlNqMavioOQSdn2aimC1IOse4I4aQgihFVC4rYlGdPqIcm1GcKJezPzqWAt7vI20qOzPC-sPspi8BnVdj2nQdxY6MPgy-kY82cp-hoip3eCTTCizem8C/s1476/Willem%20Claesz.%20Heda%20-%20Breakfast%20with%20a%20Crab.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1463" data-original-width="1476" height="317" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiNV0ZzffOADFSvjZHCUwrPuAzGmSfn1OCIwHRs_ub5YdQuwoOYcLv8N7g-Nd74YUe-EzZO2XmJVlNqMavioOQSdn2aimC1IOse4I4aQgihFVC4rYlGdPqIcm1GcKJezPzqWAt7vI20qOzPC-sPspi8BnVdj2nQdxY6MPgy-kY82cp-hoip3eCTTCizem8C/s320/Willem%20Claesz.%20Heda%20-%20Breakfast%20with%20a%20Crab.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>A Hebrew servant who likes life with his master and with his Canaanite slave-woman mate  may stay with his master "forever" if he insists on it, which practically means until the Jubilee year. In court, the master bores his ear against the door with an awl as an act of acquisition.</div><div style="margin-bottom: 0in;"><br />A Hebrew servant should be given food and wine better than his master's, and a better bed, because the Torah says, "It is good for him with you."  The master also supports the servant's wife and children that the servant had before his servitude.</div>
<div style="margin-bottom: 0in;">
<br /></div>
<div style="margin-bottom: 0in;">Art: Breakfast with a Crab by Willem Claesz. Heda</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/23.txt
<a id="src-00330"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/23.txt`

Kiddushin 23 - Can a Canaanite Slave-woman be Acquired through Anal Intercourse?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgye00IeZlYhJh_8DBu_goz8t7aU0amzQtpO1s9AuO5H7pv17qxt_SwQB4iCMquAC_FfN6xRSuibMcrVEEKFgj6JLVQX1P7CaHgYt5giC2WTou1zl_a6INfJebfrSVbTxvjN9j_7GSKtJz3/s1600-h/Interior+with+a+Sleeping+Maid+and+her+Mistress+.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5263414002033697826" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgye00IeZlYhJh_8DBu_goz8t7aU0amzQtpO1s9AuO5H7pv17qxt_SwQB4iCMquAC_FfN6xRSuibMcrVEEKFgj6JLVQX1P7CaHgYt5giC2WTou1zl_a6INfJebfrSVbTxvjN9j_7GSKtJz3/s320/Interior+with+a+Sleeping+Maid+and+her+Mistress+.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 241px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">A Canaanite slave may be acquired using money, a document, or a proprietary act of serving his new master, such as removing his master's shoe or lifting him.<br />
<br />
Can we derive from here that a Canaanite slave woman can be acquired by sexual intercourse because she is lifting her master? - No, this is not comparable to regular lifting, where the lifter gets no pleasure. How about anal intercourse where she is not getting pleasure? Who is to say that she is not getting any pleasure? - Disproved!  A slave woman can not be acquired in this way.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: The idle servant by Nicoleas Maes</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/24.txt
<a id="src-00331"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/24.txt`

Kiddushin 24 - How Can Canaanite Slave Become Free?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggnPFHT6d5R8ujX8jmVTq77GUaIt9CGIYTjJqd9fT27wO7rlk6s7nC3rw2WW-XI4IEZARd6uhToZiVGJbLS4KpXQAVo5H7DBYz-q5kDi-jpayT0Iw3U3reSsNkHhyphenhyphenSk5ufsQNys700ZByn/s1600-h/Marinus_Claesz._van_Reymerswaele_005.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5263924989433563042" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggnPFHT6d5R8ujX8jmVTq77GUaIt9CGIYTjJqd9fT27wO7rlk6s7nC3rw2WW-XI4IEZARd6uhToZiVGJbLS4KpXQAVo5H7DBYz-q5kDi-jpayT0Iw3U3reSsNkHhyphenhyphenSk5ufsQNys700ZByn/s320/Marinus_Claesz._van_Reymerswaele_005.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 238px;" /></a>A Canaanite slave goes free if someone gives money to his master on the condition that the slave should be free. Another way is to provide cash to the slave so that he can use it to free himself.<br />
<br />
Suppose a Canaanite slave was already circumcised and immersed in a Mikveh, and the master knocks out his tooth, takes out his eye, or inflicts damage on any of 22 other extremities. In that case, the slave goes free, and the courts force his master to write a document of emancipation for him.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Two tax collectors by MARINUS VAN REYMERSWAELE</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/25.txt
<a id="src-00332"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/25.txt`

Kiddushin 25 - Cold Fish
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhxhDggS6iYX7BfryyOhCaIjash3U5yeI6pCm3bO-FiSlkC8In5mD6AfhqMxiMGDw5EUji0AkMXaSQ0pK3u7G0LU7FD2t0A8RDWCRja9QA-QSvsDu2weE9HlKhPT8SKX6cfri8Vc_v2Jd1T/s1600-h/Quiringh+Gerritsz.+van+Brekelenkam+-+A+Fishmonger+-C.1667.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5264253785519986034" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhxhDggS6iYX7BfryyOhCaIjash3U5yeI6pCm3bO-FiSlkC8In5mD6AfhqMxiMGDw5EUji0AkMXaSQ0pK3u7G0LU7FD2t0A8RDWCRja9QA-QSvsDu2weE9HlKhPT8SKX6cfri8Vc_v2Jd1T/s320/Quiringh+Gerritsz.+van+Brekelenkam+-+A+Fishmonger+-C.1667.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 282px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">The elders of Nezonia did not attend Rav Chisda's lecture. He said to Rav Hamnuna, "Go place a ban on them."<br />
<br />
Rav Hamnuna went and asked them, "Why didn't you go to the lecture?" They said, "When we asked him a question, he did not resolve it." Rav Hamnuna said, "Ask me any question." They asked, "A slave whose master emasculated him in his testicles, is it treated as an exposed blemish, in which case the slave goes free, or not?"<br />
<br />
Rav Hamnuna did not know. So they said, "You are not Khamnuna (hot fish) but Karnuna (cold fish).</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">A Fishmonger by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Quiringh Gerritsz. van Brekelenkam</span></div>

### content/kiddushin/26.txt
<a id="src-00333"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/26.txt`

Kiddushin 26 - Methods of Acquisition
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhb8PBiDxzWhJi465-45GvfCChCdmLbT2GwNS6cun6vuMjkmDYVxRth5LJHoDsbB7wVD3DKTBL7cLm1HYsqL3L1M614eC5Z85YxymZ3udo16eGqOIA5Prih5x4Z2CmvRMVdjos_xbeIvKXj/s1600-h/Royal-Elephant-At-The-Gateway-To-The-Jami-Masjid-Mathura.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5264640391341420402" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhb8PBiDxzWhJi465-45GvfCChCdmLbT2GwNS6cun6vuMjkmDYVxRth5LJHoDsbB7wVD3DKTBL7cLm1HYsqL3L1M614eC5Z85YxymZ3udo16eGqOIA5Prih5x4Z2CmvRMVdjos_xbeIvKXj/s320/Royal-Elephant-At-The-Gateway-To-The-Jami-Masjid-Mathura.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 203px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">A large animal (cow or horse) is acquired by handing over its reins, and a small animal (sheep) by drawing it near.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon says that only lifting the animal acquires it. Then how does Rabbi Shimon acquire elephants? By having them step on bundles of vines.<br />
<br />
Real property may be acquired using money, a document, or a proprietary act such as locking the gate. Movable property may be acquired only by "drawing it near." To protect buyers, the Rabbis abrogated the power of money to acquire so that sellers would guard the sold goods after receiving the money.</span><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;Royal Elephant At The Gateway To The Jami Masjid Mathura by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Rudolf Ernst&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/27.txt
<a id="src-00334"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/27.txt`

Kiddushin 27 - Acquiring Movable Properties
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgULtUN0i6aKk7kK80Au29LI43rzBvoCN8Yq79Wg37D2huEjbehifrBxwGSUvajNyjGG3j97q_XGzqcoTeVHzC09RQcRRrJkZ4cyljzpYudiGg3tCKuG0HJhCXXNtJATp-4VCjLQPTcthPe/s1600-h/Pompeo+Massani+-+The+Money+Counter.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5264996265208652274" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgULtUN0i6aKk7kK80Au29LI43rzBvoCN8Yq79Wg37D2huEjbehifrBxwGSUvajNyjGG3j97q_XGzqcoTeVHzC09RQcRRrJkZ4cyljzpYudiGg3tCKuG0HJhCXXNtJATp-4VCjLQPTcthPe/s320/Pompeo+Massani+-+The+Money+Counter.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 258px;" /></a>While acquiring a field "by dint of," one may also specify the acquisition of movable properties, wherever they may be, in which case no additional act of acquisition is required.<br />
<br />
In the same way, one may combine the sale of land with the gifting of movables. The land may even be sold to one person, while the gift of movables goes to the other.<br />
<br />
In all these cases, complete money payment must be made before the movables are acquired.<br />
<br />
"Devolving of the oath" happens when the Torah requires an oath for one item and a related item requires an oath by devolving.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Money Counter by Pompeo Massani</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/28.txt
<a id="src-00335"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/28.txt`

Kiddushin 28 - Slander
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3L9I-5FDIqTU9SVNDyF5U6UBMB1tvgMgEdn4tZkEqLa6UKWlRXkvX86VO6XeVyfJZdYKyobMqv9zv8RvuAiCk9ihSbPOHrWc78ir6gFT_IJP8ZH_pabNeylSX0UXhczZ0nd5j1_PEzfgU/s1600-h/A-Prize-Fight,-From-the-National-Sports-Of-Great-Britain-1823.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5265260547108259010" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3L9I-5FDIqTU9SVNDyF5U6UBMB1tvgMgEdn4tZkEqLa6UKWlRXkvX86VO6XeVyfJZdYKyobMqv9zv8RvuAiCk9ihSbPOHrWc78ir6gFT_IJP8ZH_pabNeylSX0UXhczZ0nd5j1_PEzfgU/s320/A-Prize-Fight,-From-the-National-Sports-Of-Great-Britain-1823.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 210px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><br />
<div>
<div>
The courts once had this power that if one called another a slave, he would be put under a ban, and if he called him a "mamzer" (bastard), the courts could flog him.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If one calls another a bad person (Rasha), courts do not get involved, but the one slandered can compete with the offender in business, even unfairly. What about the law of not taking revenge? It does not apply if one is hurt or humiliated in public. However, since it is uncertain if the above ruling is accepted, one should refrain from revenge even in this situation.</div>
<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A Prize Fight, From the National Sports Of Great Britain</div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="color: #333333; font-family: Verdana; font-size: 11px; line-height: 17px;">

</span></div>
</div>

### content/kiddushin/29.txt
<a id="src-00336"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/29.txt`

Kiddushin 29 - Things that father has to do for his son
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFO6GYj875Uj29fNrRnp3GznCyE_1ZgF2YvQJYnTPOWz0W51yz2l5uN3W963m5lh_eL_3tCErfFPbuq-b4iNv2ho0Bszvu_yQIV_beUzSIE2vW6gvNGzBIwhRd5dt7KC5SMc3YHoep3teo/s1600-h/Ivan+Nikolaevich+Kramskoy+-+Insulted+Jewish+Boy.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5265764972885126578" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFO6GYj875Uj29fNrRnp3GznCyE_1ZgF2YvQJYnTPOWz0W51yz2l5uN3W963m5lh_eL_3tCErfFPbuq-b4iNv2ho0Bszvu_yQIV_beUzSIE2vW6gvNGzBIwhRd5dt7KC5SMc3YHoep3teo/s320/Ivan+Nikolaevich+Kramskoy+-+Insulted+Jewish+Boy.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 271px;" /></a>The father's obligations that involve his son are: to circumcise him, to redeem him if he is a firstborn (by paying fives coins to a Kohen), to teach him Torah, to take a wife for him (that is, to help him find a wife and assist him in preparations for marriage) and to teach him a craft. Some say the father must teach him to swim in the water.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehudah says, "Anyone who does not teach his son a craft has taught him banditry. Talmud: "Can you really think so? - Rather, as if the father taught him banditry."<div><br /></div><div>Art: Insulted Jewish Boy by Ivan Nikolaevich Kramskoy</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/3.txt
<a id="src-00337"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/3.txt`

Kiddushin 3 – Who searches for whom?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihEWgN87t6BcP7TVtey0bE0Iv5SnaSpGhjUanzudro0wPofbSnyHzRyJco-K6-RXu7UhCsCN60Wz48Ix9gY84nt3aWHCN-KCEgVEZ-v5GvQgXUNo01HeESs0ZKXuJuzfwHwKnb3njq4Rk6/s1600/Man+in+a+Smock+Gustave+Caillebotte.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihEWgN87t6BcP7TVtey0bE0Iv5SnaSpGhjUanzudro0wPofbSnyHzRyJco-K6-RXu7UhCsCN60Wz48Ix9gY84nt3aWHCN-KCEgVEZ-v5GvQgXUNo01HeESs0ZKXuJuzfwHwKnb3njq4Rk6/w264-h320/Man+in+a+Smock+Gustave+Caillebotte.jpg" width="264" /></a>It is the way of a man to search after a wife and not the other way around. This is similar to someone who lost a precious stone on a beach. Who searches after whom? Obviously, the one that lost his possession searches for it.
<br />
<br />
We mentioned that betrothal can be done with money. Why is that so? Furthermore, there is a related law that a father can give his daughter away in marriage when she is young; in that case, the money the groom pays goes to the father. 
<br />
<br />
Both questions have the same, if non-trivial, answer. This is derived from the law of a Jewish slave girl. The father can sell his daughter as a servant. In this case, it is understood that when she grows up, the buyer will take her as a wife or designate her for her son. She goes free if none of these happen, and the Torah adds, "No money!" We already know that "free" means "no money." So we understand that it is in this case that there is no money, but in another related case, there is money. And when is it? When a woman gets married, or when the father gives her away in marriage.
<br />
<br />
That is exactly what we wanted to demonstrate, that the betrothal which will lead to marriage (chuppah) can be done with money.
<br />
<br />
Today both events happen under the chuppah in close succession: first, the groom gives money (or a ring) to the bride, then the ceremony is concluded under the chuppah, which symbolizes the new home.
<br />
<br />
Art: Man in a Smock by Gustave Caillebotte

---

### content/kiddushin/30.txt
<a id="src-00338"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/30.txt`

Kiddushin 30 - Teaching Torah to one's Grandchildren
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivnOfksmTVJh-51uEYbDX64Uu6Du-MHkrH_eRJY7Uq7x5jdeL2k7CwulEueIPAy6wgLlXQfjUrylUEIB3qxS-uSLDyYq3QAjCT7fnc1RONgH-V4rQQW_ntnEmigB9CPZ6GFiNdtv5OaS_v/s1600-h/MosesOnMountSinai-Jean-LeonGerome-1895-1900.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5266002914738662834" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivnOfksmTVJh-51uEYbDX64Uu6Du-MHkrH_eRJY7Uq7x5jdeL2k7CwulEueIPAy6wgLlXQfjUrylUEIB3qxS-uSLDyYq3QAjCT7fnc1RONgH-V4rQQW_ntnEmigB9CPZ6GFiNdtv5OaS_v/s320/MosesOnMountSinai-Jean-LeonGerome-1895-1900.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 186px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Chiya bar Abba encountered Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi, who had hurriedly thrown a sheet upon his head and was bringing his grandchild to the synagogue for this Torah lesson. He asked, "What is all this rush about?"<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi replied, &nbsp;- is it a small thing to fulfill that which is written in the Shema prayer, "You shall make them known to your children and grandchildren," and next to this, "The day that you stood before Hashem your God at Chorev?" We see from here that teaching Torah to one's grandchild is tantamount to receiving Torah at Sinai.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Moses On Mount Sinai by Jean-Leon Gerome</span></div>

### content/kiddushin/31.txt

Kiddushin 31 - Honoring one's Parents
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEizIFTjmpPhpJDYld96tLuO_QTswaOoXK8WNWiqOkx5vZSFqotuoayCuLlKVtPubOY-QDp71ybSqY5VuvwhCzwOlqATaBcfoY3BdadkMVcJ6-V9dWHfVV2C69G7VazcET0hMLg-CtAuiuL0/s1600-h/Gerrit+Dou+-+Portret+van+Rembrandts+moeder.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5266500935654496258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEizIFTjmpPhpJDYld96tLuO_QTswaOoXK8WNWiqOkx5vZSFqotuoayCuLlKVtPubOY-QDp71ybSqY5VuvwhCzwOlqATaBcfoY3BdadkMVcJ6-V9dWHfVV2C69G7VazcET0hMLg-CtAuiuL0/s320/Gerrit+Dou+-+Portret+van+Rembrandts+moeder.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 244px;" /></a>Rabbi Tarfon had an elderly mother whom he treated with such respect that whenever she wanted to climb into bed, he would bend down, and she would climb on him into it; whenever she descended, she would descend on him to reach the floor.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Tarfon came and lauded his own performance of the mitzvah to his colleagues in the study hall. They told him: You have not yet reached half of the honor one can bestow upon his parents. Has your mother ever thrown a bag of money into the sea in your presence, and you did not shame her?<div><br /></div><div>Art: Portret van Rembrandts moeder by Gerrit Dou</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/32.txt
<a id="src-00340"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/32.txt`

Kiddushin 32 - Difference Between Honor and Reverence Towards one's Parents
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgsDI_9ipAr0w7jo8mMximfx85opf9hZlmYNoeMOk4pci8sRdn8ZeokgfkAjxC_bNPGld6oAWhdSKC96lIF-rSTLrWWJ4DMrf_YnDFGs7YzpOHTSEPEP5ByTWavcvQo7uqtxZROhs8UuLus/s1600-h/Cezanne+father.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5266870646183918050" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgsDI_9ipAr0w7jo8mMximfx85opf9hZlmYNoeMOk4pci8sRdn8ZeokgfkAjxC_bNPGld6oAWhdSKC96lIF-rSTLrWWJ4DMrf_YnDFGs7YzpOHTSEPEP5ByTWavcvQo7uqtxZROhs8UuLus/s320/Cezanne+father.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 190px;" /></a>What is proper reverence for one's parents, and what is adequate honor?<br />
<br />
Reverence means that the son may not sit in his father's place; he may not contradict his father in words in his presence – but he may offer challenges to his father's position until a conclusion is reached.<br />
<br />
Honor means that he must give his father food and drink, dress and cover him, bring him in, and take him out.<br />
<br />
The same applies to his mother.<br />
<br />
The son is not required to pay for his parents' needs out of his pocket but merely to expend the effort.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;The Artist's Father, Reading "L'Événement" by Louis-Auguste Cézanne</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/33.txt
<a id="src-00341"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/33.txt`

Kiddushin 33 - Standing Up in Front of a Sage
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhVDX-Yyr-Gdn_rEHbnq7EFUMfgXtTtVWj-NOCavV9sbskEGBEir1Z8apWJQIrRF0o7SFayfE3Hc5QQ5CYp_iIfG1S8L-xrJkKnNFRWmSo96V4kcyE-KODNlQO1Uu57pK8ge8tDvZ7xoiR5/s1600-h/Paying+Respects+to+His+High+Mightiness.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5267226220177676498" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhVDX-Yyr-Gdn_rEHbnq7EFUMfgXtTtVWj-NOCavV9sbskEGBEir1Z8apWJQIrRF0o7SFayfE3Hc5QQ5CYp_iIfG1S8L-xrJkKnNFRWmSo96V4kcyE-KODNlQO1Uu57pK8ge8tDvZ7xoiR5/s320/Paying+Respects+to+His+High+Mightiness.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 230px;" /></a>"Before an old man you shall rise" - refers to a sage of any age or any man or woman older than 70, but not to a wicked or ignorant person. The Torah continues, "Fear your God," meaning one should not avert his eyes pretending he did not see the sage.<br />
<br />
One is not obligated to suffer monetary loss by standing up in front of a sage; even so, one is obligated to stand up in front of a person bringing the first fruit to Jerusalem. Why is this? Because a mitzvah in its proper time is especially beloved.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Paying Respects to His High Mightiness</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/34.txt
<a id="src-00342"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/34.txt`

Kiddushin 34 - Women's Obligations to do Mitzvot
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh7c87KvmIHhoMCbBoJOEHWh-71uDEZLkabt72NH9FcL87lcca2oJRWLGEaJtJnsLpmZEEZ3O-mdBQ5E-4UfwuVhLK_eND0BLVezQxWslDUfQj1LFcZgjxo33ySPjrA9xegvxCQDPldVixZ/s1600-h/vermeer-milkmaid.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5267642551851728546" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh7c87KvmIHhoMCbBoJOEHWh-71uDEZLkabt72NH9FcL87lcca2oJRWLGEaJtJnsLpmZEEZ3O-mdBQ5E-4UfwuVhLK_eND0BLVezQxWslDUfQj1LFcZgjxo33ySPjrA9xegvxCQDPldVixZ/s200/vermeer-milkmaid.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 182px;" /></a>Women are not obligated to do mitzvot which are related to time, such as dwelling in a succah or hearing the shofar, although they observe these as a custom. They are also not obligated to learn those areas of the Torah which have no practical applicability nowadays.<br />
<br />
Women are obligated to affix mezuzot to their doorposts because the Torah promises long life for it, and women need long life just as men do.<br />
<br />
Women are obligated in all the negative commandments of Passover, such as not eating bread, and therefore all of the positive commandments of Passover, such as eating matzah.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Milkmaid by Vermeer</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/35.txt
<a id="src-00343"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/35.txt`

Kiddushin 35 - Women Are Obligated in Some Mitzvot but Exempt from Others
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjK8AxgGFBSdzhuAcJRl6pbwx5DwoCw700g-H7OgnzCW_vhdnJS3qrFuLA8rDhJKtIguRLTnngEhP5nL-oyvSDv1s2qwDVD2afHrlEMH2pMkKJXw8BRfha8VftT7qY6EhrM0C8OZE4nFF6k/s1600-h/John+James+Chalon+-+The+Cemetery+Of+Pere-+Lachaise+-1822.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5267973164040781938" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjK8AxgGFBSdzhuAcJRl6pbwx5DwoCw700g-H7OgnzCW_vhdnJS3qrFuLA8rDhJKtIguRLTnngEhP5nL-oyvSDv1s2qwDVD2afHrlEMH2pMkKJXw8BRfha8VftT7qY6EhrM0C8OZE4nFF6k/s200/John+James+Chalon+-+The+Cemetery+Of+Pere-+Lachaise+-1822.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 150px;" /></a>The negative commandments of the Torah apply equally to women and men. Even though the Torah says in many places, "Speak to the sons of Israel," the following phrase makes men and women equal: "When a man or a woman commits any sin that men commit."<br />
<br />
Another phrase, "These are the ordinances that you shall set before them," equates a woman to a man in all monetary payment laws.<br />
<br />
Women are exempt from the prohibition of cutting off peyot (corners of the hair on the head), and a daughter of a Kohen is allowed to visit a cemetery.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Cemetery Of Pere- Lachaise by John James Chalon</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/36.txt
<a id="src-00344"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/36.txt`

Kiddushin 36 - Mitzvot From Which Women are Exempt
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFdzaH43h3PiP4vielS_rXBW0E7xexWJfyZBOH6UFwY1AdcH6NbCzda7WXttptCi-GTmQ9CnaGYa9i-vUGN4j0x-vOnsZfS923bZnhk3kDmA7VeBkG-ppzdHDHBjP3wiQ0V51XzNvsHwCO/s1600-h/wall.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5268253741580955106" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFdzaH43h3PiP4vielS_rXBW0E7xexWJfyZBOH6UFwY1AdcH6NbCzda7WXttptCi-GTmQ9CnaGYa9i-vUGN4j0x-vOnsZfS923bZnhk3kDmA7VeBkG-ppzdHDHBjP3wiQ0V51XzNvsHwCO/s200/wall.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 149px;" /></a><div>Although a Jewish man is not allowed to make a bald spot "between the eyes" and anywhere on the head to signify mourning for the dead, a Jewish woman may. This is derived by comparison with the tefillin, worn "between the eyes" and which women are not obligated to wear.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Most elements of the priestly service in the Temple apply to men who are Kohanim but not to women who are daughters of Kohanim because of "speak to the sons of Aharon" - and not to the daughters of Aharon.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Solomon's Wall by Jean Leon Gerome</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/37.txt
<a id="src-00345"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/37.txt`

Kiddushin 37 - Mitzvot Done in the Land of Israel and Outside
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjW8azyoyXRH2XmyMn7RnGZ64LVfyxc4SiqBhrXgroEVoZrvCdcVE0fhNfF7zV6lCN7BMsWCZ5XMhUDGk1M7Jlpb1-KqQHCQMUmyqAJpBbzuftKWdi1FPUG1_Rhxh93Gb5EHyp04Kw6F2NjZ7PYWf0MDUMNjajS6vTjj8TWnqgJ_Vqu2KCI96Npo4y5xTGQ/s484/Homer%20Winslowapple%20-%20Apple%20Picking.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="400" data-original-width="484" height="264" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjW8azyoyXRH2XmyMn7RnGZ64LVfyxc4SiqBhrXgroEVoZrvCdcVE0fhNfF7zV6lCN7BMsWCZ5XMhUDGk1M7Jlpb1-KqQHCQMUmyqAJpBbzuftKWdi1FPUG1_Rhxh93Gb5EHyp04Kw6F2NjZ7PYWf0MDUMNjajS6vTjj8TWnqgJ_Vqu2KCI96Npo4y5xTGQ/s320/Homer%20Winslowapple%20-%20Apple%20Picking.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Every commandment that is dependent on the land applies only in the Land of Israel, and every commandment that is not dependent on the land applies both in the Land of Israel and outside the Land, except for the commandments of Orlah (prohibiting first 3 years of tree's fruit) and forbidden mixtures of planting.&nbsp;<div><br /></div><div>Then why, in connection with the Mitzva of Tefillin, does the Torah say, "And it will come to pass when God brings you to the Land of Canaanaties...?" - It means to say, "Perform this commandment, for on account of it you will merit to enter the Land."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Apple Picking by Homer Winslow</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/38.txt
<a id="src-00346"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/38.txt`

Kiddushin 38 - Moses, Manna, and the Land of Israel
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjwPPreTNPcYNtY20dGQhwjGVEt7Pp_bK43qSS1LFilEmD91mbWbGnvCIVlMYQ3jOyei_wbqisPYPVshdnPPhnZv_K7nW44O12z1VIfgsoJfFgJlpo8nJc9BomjgQ38nfRaoo4ZzeEV0Ayh/s1600-h/Moritz+Oppenheim+-+Moses.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5269125954362478130" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjwPPreTNPcYNtY20dGQhwjGVEt7Pp_bK43qSS1LFilEmD91mbWbGnvCIVlMYQ3jOyei_wbqisPYPVshdnPPhnZv_K7nW44O12z1VIfgsoJfFgJlpo8nJc9BomjgQ38nfRaoo4ZzeEV0Ayh/s200/Moritz+Oppenheim+-+Moses.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 160px;" /></a>Moses said, "I am one hundred and twenty years old today." The extra word "today" teaches that God completes the years of the righteous ones. Moses was born and died on the 7th of Adar.<br />
<br />
When Moses died, the manna ceased to descend from heaven, and the Jews subsisted on the manna, which was left in their vessels until the following Passover, thus making up 40 years of eating manna.<br />
<br />
From  "...and you shall proclaim liberty in the land," one might think it is only in Israel, but the extra "this is the Jubilee year" teaches that slaves are released everywhere.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Moses by Moritz Oppenheim</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/39.txt
<a id="src-00347"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/39.txt`

Kiddushin 39 - Reward for a Mitzvah is Another Mitzvah
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi0f-lRd9JCiLR__1YmxPX0O3YJ_qknY4Qyu517rsITzogKoB76Be0f3xknsQtaS6WNcLXEVzMS1m9PYoAG8vrO6Xorcz45r8uOS_RsCp-rvMSXpAdbfbgD1ElJWMPdm6aBzT61Gofd2tdQo5NBRvJzEsk7FD3U8uYFrgv7kHMsrGFA5wSJ10f9ibcVZT6t/s750/Vincent%20van%20Gogh%20-%20Still%20Life%20with%20Three%20Birds'%20Nests.jpeg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="574" data-original-width="750" height="245" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi0f-lRd9JCiLR__1YmxPX0O3YJ_qknY4Qyu517rsITzogKoB76Be0f3xknsQtaS6WNcLXEVzMS1m9PYoAG8vrO6Xorcz45r8uOS_RsCp-rvMSXpAdbfbgD1ElJWMPdm6aBzT61Gofd2tdQo5NBRvJzEsk7FD3U8uYFrgv7kHMsrGFA5wSJ10f9ibcVZT6t/s320/Vincent%20van%20Gogh%20-%20Still%20Life%20with%20Three%20Birds'%20Nests.jpeg" width="320" /></a></div>Orlah (prohibition of the first 3 years of a tree's fruit) reads as follows: in Israel, it is forbidden; if in doubt, it is also prohibited. Outside of Israel, one can go to the field where the Orlah tree grows and buy the fruit, provided that one does not see it being picked.<p></p><p>One who performs an extra mitzvah is getting the goodness of performing another mitzvah, and his life is extended to do it. Thus, the reward for a mitzvah is only another mitzvah, except for respect for the parents and sending away the mother bird, for which extended life is promised.</p><p>Art: Still Life with Three Birds' Nests&nbsp; by Vincent van Gogh</p>

---

### content/kiddushin/4.txt
<a id="src-00348"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/4.txt`

Kiddushin 4 – When a man takes a wife
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiUbQUSd74cHY8iEinazAdKOTdlb5XgdffMhEk4O-lnq1rO2jGa5M7FtpazpBBE5GLjDrBToBYKKHHUqrbQItbaVtcPrvri9B_1ToJUsIUQ97msSDQ3y9f3azjQa930Wwv0HRcFolEtjVwi/s1600/The+Innkeepers+Daughter+by+Charles+Cope+West.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiUbQUSd74cHY8iEinazAdKOTdlb5XgdffMhEk4O-lnq1rO2jGa5M7FtpazpBBE5GLjDrBToBYKKHHUqrbQItbaVtcPrvri9B_1ToJUsIUQ97msSDQ3y9f3azjQa930Wwv0HRcFolEtjVwi/s320/The+Innkeepers+Daughter+by+Charles+Cope+West.jpg" width="253" /></a></div>
<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2016/03/kiddushin-3-who-searches-for-whom.html">Earlier, we saw</a>&nbsp;one way to derive that marriage can be effected by giving the bride-to-be a ring or another object of value. However, it was based on taking the extra word "money" from a different place in the Torah and applying it to our context.
<br />
<br />
A more direct way is to take the phrase, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=24">When a man takes a woman and has relations with her... if later he does not like her, he can divorce</a>."" This clearly describes the situation of marriage and uses the word "take." The same word "<b>take</b>" is found when Abraham buys a field from Efron and says, "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=23#P585">I gave you the money for the field, <b>take</b> it from me.</a>" We thus see that "take" has a meaning of acquiring with money.
<br />
<br />
Now this calls for some logical acrobatics. Look at a Jewish female slave, who cannot be acquired by having relations with her and is acquired only with money; a wife, who is acquired by relations, is undoubtedly acquired with money! Therefore, we don't need the derivation above at all!!
<br />
<br />
No, because a Yebamah case disproves this. Look at Yebamah (one's dead brother's wife), whom the remaining brother has to marry. She is acquired by cohabitation – and nevertheless, she is not acquired with money. So the above logic breaks: someone acquired with relations is nevertheless not acquired with money.
<br />
<br />
However, we can deflect this attack: Yebamah has an inherent weakness in that she is not acquired with a document, whereas a wife <b>is</b> acquired with a document of intent to marry.<br />
<br />
Thus, we saw an attack, a deflection of this attack, and then a deflection of this deflection.  We see at least why the proof based on the word "take" helps.
<br />
<br />
Art: The Innkeepers Daughter by Charles Cope West

---

### content/kiddushin/40.txt
