**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/40.txt`

Kiddushin 40 - Importance of Mitzvot
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhwjUM1YMG3d0EoLluhcE2r4NgQfnssKfXmILA9zS7i5mHaU2kYh3MgzeQSb7uZJVRp_ywiv-aNb20knzUlBZ1XegkKdFxWos3spM3sCBkWLYURTpYpozQja8-CaGP7ixA5qd6hn6O95I2w/s1600-h/maria_de_medici.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5269734095116400002" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhwjUM1YMG3d0EoLluhcE2r4NgQfnssKfXmILA9zS7i5mHaU2kYh3MgzeQSb7uZJVRp_ywiv-aNb20knzUlBZ1XegkKdFxWos3spM3sCBkWLYURTpYpozQja8-CaGP7ixA5qd6hn6O95I2w/s200/maria_de_medici.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 154px;" /></a><div>A certain noblewoman propositioned Rabbi Tzadok. He told her, "My heart is weak, and I can not do it. Is there anything to eat?" She said to him: "There is some non-kosher meat." He told her: "What is to be deduced from this? That whoever performs this eats this."&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
She lit the oven and put the meat inside it. Rabbi Tsadok climbed up and sat inside the oven (he was allowed to sacrifice his life because of his great stature). She said to him: "Had I known that you regard the matter as so severe, I would not have bothered you."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Marie de Medici by Alessandro Allora</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/41.txt
<a id="src-00350"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/41.txt`

Kiddushin 41 - Marriage With the Help of an Agent
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1TX9t-G15i24yi4Hy18bm88AsUKFqpeFfHNKIf3KNrjEh6s8ylcdFPun-DeCJTM9KapdD73ao2eLFvDOyqrUJCCQE6_gR88HpH-Ot_YejTHZw5gsudfZ2BmTE2UjeDFTpwpM_AgUmEusm/s1600-h/Konstantin+Jegorowitsch+Makowski+-+The+Young+Bride.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5270074628314363954" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1TX9t-G15i24yi4Hy18bm88AsUKFqpeFfHNKIf3KNrjEh6s8ylcdFPun-DeCJTM9KapdD73ao2eLFvDOyqrUJCCQE6_gR88HpH-Ot_YejTHZw5gsudfZ2BmTE2UjeDFTpwpM_AgUmEusm/s200/Konstantin+Jegorowitsch+Makowski+-+The+Young+Bride.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 140px;" /></a>A man can betroth a woman either personally or through his agent. A woman can accept kiddushin and become betrothed personally or through her agent. A man may give his daughter in betrothal when she is a na'arah (under 12) either personally or through his agent. Performing betrothal, as well as any other mitzvah personally, is the preferred way.<br />
<br />
From where in the Torah do we derive the legal concept of agency? From its use of "and he sends her" instead of a more direct, "and he divorces," we learn that both man and woman can appoint an agent.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Young Bride by Konstantin Jegorowitsch Makowski</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/42.txt
<a id="src-00351"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/42.txt`

Kiddushin 42 - Division of an Inheritance
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiESTDCkvw5S69Xl2ZIDUCh7qzXdMkVzLlcROY1cyNe4_eH_YDrkKrYnKDUWcv8RVnVJO4yFHgLRSB4SZB_lv-tGFN7GeyURLh48hrUG869aEBA9YA-cHCZPeK2ev2nqAN_P3KAKZrGGVQJ/s1600-h/William+Bigg+-+The+Sailor%27s+Orphans.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5270581560710203298" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiESTDCkvw5S69Xl2ZIDUCh7qzXdMkVzLlcROY1cyNe4_eH_YDrkKrYnKDUWcv8RVnVJO4yFHgLRSB4SZB_lv-tGFN7GeyURLh48hrUG869aEBA9YA-cHCZPeK2ev2nqAN_P3KAKZrGGVQJ/s200/William+Bigg+-+The+Sailor%27s+Orphans.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 164px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 200px;" /></a>When orphans who are minors come before the court to divide the assets of their deceased father, the court appoints an administrator for each of them, just as leaders of the tribes who divided the land between the Jews entering Israel.<br />
<br />
When the orphans become adults, they cannot protest the settlement, for if they indeed had such a right, what worth is there in the power of the court?<br />
<br />
Brothers who divide an inheritance are like purchasers of their respective shares. Consequently, the transaction is void if they erred in estimating the value and the discrepancy is more than a sixth.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Sailor's Orphans by William Bigg</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/43.txt
<a id="src-00352"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/43.txt`

Kiddushin 43 - Is Killer for Hire Liable?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjcMYJCUQFDVbGSSsukzTSCK-quP6qGmpcVATu7pVkiDgbVi73UpirCWC5bIOdH2k0BAtQwudrCUQUzvjIFFzruRAQydAM5N0VEeAeDWg7JQSXI1HlSMUf8vlnQzcBX3m5NuMM1atfWKMBe/s1600-h/Cezanne+Storm.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5270821963064443650" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjcMYJCUQFDVbGSSsukzTSCK-quP6qGmpcVATu7pVkiDgbVi73UpirCWC5bIOdH2k0BAtQwudrCUQUzvjIFFzruRAQydAM5N0VEeAeDWg7JQSXI1HlSMUf8vlnQzcBX3m5NuMM1atfWKMBe/s200/Cezanne+Storm.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 144px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 200px;" /></a><div>The agency is inapplicable in matters of transgression because of the principle of "The words of the Master and the words of the disciple, whose words should you obey?"</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
The two exceptions are misappropriation of Temple property and stealing and selling of an animal, for which the sender is liable. </div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
If one says to his agent, "Go and kill a certain person," the agent is liable for the deed, while the one who sent him is exempt. Shammai says, "The one who sent him is liable" based on "...you have killed him with the sword of the Ammonites."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: A Murder by Cezanne</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/44.txt
<a id="src-00353"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/44.txt`

Kiddushin 44 - Marriage and Divorce of a Minor
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgstDzaKw_FNjte2rw3gpsius5G-6JfD1sH-VIq31lhzWM1jJNKH6kM3fg0mty9stHwpFM-nEKG_UKlSj3ACzzgdhi7im7zccJ8uLZiIelldlhPW_FTCwwsHRXK_oc1okOJnKmQgDaeFkr2/s1600-h/Gainsborough+-+Painters+daughters+with+a+cat.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5271198195245015090" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgstDzaKw_FNjte2rw3gpsius5G-6JfD1sH-VIq31lhzWM1jJNKH6kM3fg0mty9stHwpFM-nEKG_UKlSj3ACzzgdhi7im7zccJ8uLZiIelldlhPW_FTCwwsHRXK_oc1okOJnKmQgDaeFkr2/s200/Gainsborough+-+Painters+daughters+with+a+cat.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 162px;" /></a>We have learned that a man may betroth his daughter when she is a Naarah (between 12 and 12.5 years of age).<br />
<br />
Related teaching: a betrothed Naarah whose husband wishes to divorce her, either she or her father can receive her divorce bill (Get), and any girl unable to care for her Get cannot become divorced.<br />
<br />
However, regarding kiddushin, her father accepts the kiddushin, and she can not.<br />
<br />
Can a Naarah appoint an agent to accept her Get? - No - because she has less power than her father, who alone can appoint such an agent.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Painter's daughters with a cat by Gainsborough</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/45.txt
<a id="src-00354"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/45.txt`

Kiddushin 45 - Betrothal by a Minor without the Knowledge of Her Father
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLgGHNkN89OVOzLBUCZ7XNpqQ8zL-oQsHKrYsw0rEbgo-3qbTgPmZeYoRTOtwXfnXVoO2UpUb0m84AwqF8OAxzNEZBUTfLTaDcG1Vxvk9GofbiPWR2t3iYdz6Kqp19VoG4bve6FE2fKFTo/s1600-h/Van_Heussen_Marktst.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5271722612012397458" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLgGHNkN89OVOzLBUCZ7XNpqQ8zL-oQsHKrYsw0rEbgo-3qbTgPmZeYoRTOtwXfnXVoO2UpUb0m84AwqF8OAxzNEZBUTfLTaDcG1Vxvk9GofbiPWR2t3iYdz6Kqp19VoG4bve6FE2fKFTo/s200/Van_Heussen_Marktst.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 152px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 200px;" /></a>A minor who became betrothed without her father's knowledge requires a Get before she can marry another man, for the eventuality that her father has agreed to her betrothal and it became valid. She also requires "Refusal," a procedure where the minor says to her husband in court, "I do not want you anymore," in case her father has not agreed.<br />
<br />
A certain man betrothed a minor by giving her a bundle of vegetables in the marketplace. Here we are not concerned that the father may acquiesce because betrothal was not done honorably.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Fruit and Vegetable Seller by Frans Hals</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/46.txt
<a id="src-00355"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/46.txt`

Kiddushin 46 - A Woman who Ate her Betrothal Gift
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjK49IUPHysJr-d-SYor9F_XbX-LibT-6Wq_OXjJ1J1mz9f3EgnsAlKPOU0Iv-IQZucZ52ws1zAFfIuUIJWBJo4_6am516OOyhcroj1zxfiYQ4icdM6eiuhzQp8_dpLOQRDG7CuRLinSY3Y/s1600-h/Comiendo+fruta+%28Eating+fruit%29" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5272037418164849362" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjK49IUPHysJr-d-SYor9F_XbX-LibT-6Wq_OXjJ1J1mz9f3EgnsAlKPOU0Iv-IQZucZ52ws1zAFfIuUIJWBJo4_6am516OOyhcroj1zxfiYQ4icdM6eiuhzQp8_dpLOQRDG7CuRLinSY3Y/s200/Comiendo+fruta+%28Eating+fruit%29" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 163px;" /></a>If one says to a woman: "Become betrothed to me with this date," then again, "Become betrothed to me with this date"; if either one of these dates has the value of a prutah, she is betrothed, and if not, she is not betrothed.<br />
<br />
If he hands her the dates and says: "Become betrothed to me with this, with this, and with this," if there is the value of a prutah in all of them combined, she is betrothed.<br />
<br />
If she was eating the dates one by one, she was betrothed only if one of them had the value of a prutah.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Comiendo fruta by Pons Arnau Francisco&nbsp;</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/47.txt
<a id="src-00356"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/47.txt`

Kiddushin 47 - Betrothal with a Loan
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNVjlSldHhpzCDi-E9dApX7ugCPvKYqo46mBBiQKqFzqOEAppcOcclx9r2r-yWk-WiA9awiU9zvW0f_xSqF0naFys0ND5MP2oy8KeG0jMyfD1_uXXFynyzN-i-YBZIFz1ry0s_2KtIdLvl/s1600-h/Gabriel+Metsu,+Girl+Receiving+a+Letter,+1658.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5272414983226458738" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgNVjlSldHhpzCDi-E9dApX7ugCPvKYqo46mBBiQKqFzqOEAppcOcclx9r2r-yWk-WiA9awiU9zvW0f_xSqF0naFys0ND5MP2oy8KeG0jMyfD1_uXXFynyzN-i-YBZIFz1ry0s_2KtIdLvl/s200/Gabriel+Metsu,+Girl+Receiving+a+Letter,+1658.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 200px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 199px;" /></a>If one betroths a woman with a loan, she is not betrothed, for a loan is given to be spent. Thus, a man cannot say to a woman, "I forgive you the loan, and with that money become betrothed to me," because at this time the money is hers. Instead, he can forgive her the loan and betroth her with the benefit she receives from no longer having to repay him.<br />
<br />
If a man said to a woman, "Become betrothed to me with $100", but gave her only $1, she is betrothed, and the man must pay later.<br /><br />
<div>Art: Girl Receiving a Letter by Gabriel Metsu</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/48.txt
<a id="src-00357"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/48.txt`

Kiddushin 48 - Betrothal with Loan Collection Rights or with Labor
If a creditor sells a note of indebtedness to his fellow and afterward forgives the debt - it is indeed forgiven. Therefore, if one betroths a woman by giving her a loan document for collection, she may  fear that he will forgive the debt, and thus she does not wholeheartedly commit herself to the betrothal, which is therefore void.<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgZVtHHV-Sdo6KPPpjzlUWx4Gl4pMesnswcEhH5n9q0b_6aAi3AO6fc9Uvb-lgYw4dmKCWC8M9fE0FVBdB966EpyVYrz4-IxUg0L34nBM86Z51_OLHvPgTp10eDz2dNY7LpoSxYnNNRLUNE/s1600-h/Andries+Vermeulen+-+Still+Life+Jewellery+Casket.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5272816239931524994" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgZVtHHV-Sdo6KPPpjzlUWx4Gl4pMesnswcEhH5n9q0b_6aAi3AO6fc9Uvb-lgYw4dmKCWC8M9fE0FVBdB966EpyVYrz4-IxUg0L34nBM86Z51_OLHvPgTp10eDz2dNY7LpoSxYnNNRLUNE/s200/Andries+Vermeulen+-+Still+Life+Jewellery+Casket.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 117px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 200px;" /></a><br />
<br />
If a woman handed a piece of gold to a craftsman and said to him: "Fashion for me anklets, earrings, or rings, and in return for your labor, I will become betrothed to you," - it is betrothal with a loan, which is invalid.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Still Life Jewellery Casket by Andries Vermeulen</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/49.txt
<a id="src-00358"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/49.txt`

Kiddushin 49 - Betrothal with a Wrong Object
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgPPrB9sxPAzfWQvurGQ9e4C30gC_9FFuaxos4J7Ak8r5FxrxOA6PP3hVFcxpltSyGc5PqqMCHpBVIZlY3L4etafP4VnZMt40qv5I-dzy2FdVH21JLXcm2O_kckOfO9uoUFhWBuzpbZKk8X/s1600-h/Hans+van+Sant+-A+still+life+with+glass+of+wine,+tazza+and+a+pewter+plate.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5273161826928459618" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgPPrB9sxPAzfWQvurGQ9e4C30gC_9FFuaxos4J7Ak8r5FxrxOA6PP3hVFcxpltSyGc5PqqMCHpBVIZlY3L4etafP4VnZMt40qv5I-dzy2FdVH21JLXcm2O_kckOfO9uoUFhWBuzpbZKk8X/s320/Hans+van+Sant+-A+still+life+with+glass+of+wine,+tazza+and+a+pewter+plate.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 218px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If a man says to a woman: "Become betrothed to me with this cup of wine," and the cup was found to contain honey or the other way around - she is not betrothed. Some people prefer wine, and some prefer honey.<br />
<br />
Or, if a man asks a woman to become betrothed with a silver coin, and it was found to be made of gold, or the other way around - she is not betrothed. In some situations, she may need silver, and in some, gold. Rabbi Shimon says that if he promised a silver coin but gave a golden one, she is betrothed since he only mentioned silver "<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/02/bava-batra-165-three-daily.html">by way of example</a>."<br />
<br />
Ten measures of conversation descended to the world, and women took nine of them.</span><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">A still life with a glass of wine, tazza, and a pewter plate by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Hans van Sant</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/5.txt
<a id="src-00359"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/5.txt`

Kiddushin 5 - Terms of Endearment
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgYSxAVUo_tEionolRX6zv0BJAOSDCoJpuXV1XnTG8xAXtkMHD4xJxq6y5ly24yQVNem3Dj7wie1UtB2cbIh2ap8eDaW5Fev9F_9iZuuM1kr3biz2t7gtwAl71a0OLuLnqypTdQslQUXPqo/s1600-h/A-Young-Lady-And-A-Cavalier-Holding-A-Letter.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5257585379151596402" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgYSxAVUo_tEionolRX6zv0BJAOSDCoJpuXV1XnTG8xAXtkMHD4xJxq6y5ly24yQVNem3Dj7wie1UtB2cbIh2ap8eDaW5Fev9F_9iZuuM1kr3biz2t7gtwAl71a0OLuLnqypTdQslQUXPqo/s320/A-Young-Lady-And-A-Cavalier-Holding-A-Letter.jpg" style="float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>How is Kiddushin brought about through money? When a man gives a woman money or items worth money and says, "Behold, you are betrothed to me - Harei at mekudeshet li," and she agrees, she is betrothed.<br />
<br />
Anyone who does not know the laws of divorce documents and Kiddushin should have no dealings with them, for an unwitting error in the decision could prove intractable.<br />
<br />
A woman can not be betrothed by forgoing the repayment of a loan. The loan is given for expenses, with the obligation to repay. Thus, he is not giving her anything of value at this  moment.<div><br /></div><div><div>How about a document? A document is drafted by a man, and it states that a woman is hereby betrothed to him. The Kiddushin is effected when the man gives the document to the woman.</div><div><br /></div><div>Why does this work? Because “And she will leave the first husband's house, and she will go and be a wife unto another man.” Since “leave” can be effected through a document, so too “be” can be effected through a document.</div><div><br /></div><div>But if so, can divorce be effected by money? - No, because a defender cannot become an accuser. And while the documents would be different and distinct, money would be the same.</div></div><div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A Young Lady and a Cavalier by Frans Francken (III)</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/50.txt
<a id="src-00360"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/50.txt`

Kiddushin 50 - Betrothal by a Liar
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg99EWjS0mLPl56YQkXc5xDS0vyCmFZuw24NqkeVJmXsgP2rgCdq7dFInjnlyUWLzGS-oCELb0oWxO-JnEATGQUxZE6EJCUBQg2HxFcFH11f5W33GouCNgaQ0J4qceq7nFRWQJLdxnrGSG8/s1600-h/Tarbell,+Edmund+Charles+Three+Sisters+-+A+Study+in+June+Sunlight.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5273497301931994162" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg99EWjS0mLPl56YQkXc5xDS0vyCmFZuw24NqkeVJmXsgP2rgCdq7dFInjnlyUWLzGS-oCELb0oWxO-JnEATGQUxZE6EJCUBQg2HxFcFH11f5W33GouCNgaQ0J4qceq7nFRWQJLdxnrGSG8/s320/Tarbell,+Edmund+Charles+Three+Sisters+-+A+Study+in+June+Sunlight.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 282px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">If a man says to a woman, "Become betrothed to me on condition that I am a Kohen," but he is found to be a Levi or the reverse - even if the woman later says, "In my heart, I intended to become betrothed to him nevertheless," - she is not betrothed. Unexpressed intentions are not recognized in Jewish law.<br />
<br />
If one betroths a woman and her sister simultaneously, neither is betrothed.<br />
<br />
There were five women, two of whom were sisters, and a man collected a basket of their figs and said, "You are all betrothed to me with this basket" - the sisters were not betrothed.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Three Sisters - A Study in June Sunlight by Edmund Charles Tarbell</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/51.txt
<a id="src-00361"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/51.txt`

Kiddushin 51 - Betrothal That Does Not Permit Cohabitation
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgmZfH9GFho7anQ4HLe_ukdR5QTYnomkQzakZT9kQe12BBKv0UQX4FP3b1eAsNah6LV46zXE2cuD88LRMo2JdKEInTDaRnJvY1pHhAb2lkkgzEAhLiGY1tN5HkycGNnk0xHkm3PukrkGDWt/s1600-h/Family+Portrait+of+a+Boy+and+his+Two+Sisters,+1900" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5273849651865150306" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgmZfH9GFho7anQ4HLe_ukdR5QTYnomkQzakZT9kQe12BBKv0UQX4FP3b1eAsNah6LV46zXE2cuD88LRMo2JdKEInTDaRnJvY1pHhAb2lkkgzEAhLiGY1tN5HkycGNnk0xHkm3PukrkGDWt/s320/Family+Portrait+of+a+Boy+and+his+Two+Sisters,+1900" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 263px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">Concerning Kiddushin that does not allow legal cohabitation, Abaye said: It is a valid Kiddushin; Rava said: It is not a valid Kiddushin.<br />
<br />
Rava: "When a man shall take a wife and cohabit with her..." teaches my rule.<br />
<br />
Abaye: If a man betroths one of two sisters and does not know which, she is betrothed. However, since he does not know which of the two is his wife, he must give both a Get. According to Rava, Kiddushin should not even take effect!<br />
<br />
Rava answers: The man knew whom he betrothed. Thus, the Kiddushin took effect, and then they intermingled.<br />
<br />
This is the "K" in the six cases abbreviated <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/05/bava-metzia-21-lost-objects-that-finder.html">Y</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">A</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/04/eruvin-15-abaye-wins.html">L</a> <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-51-should-betrothal-allow.html">K</a> G <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">M</a>, where the law follows Abaye against Rava.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;Family Portrait of a Boy and His Two Sisters, by&nbsp;Francois Flameng</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/52.txt
<a id="src-00362"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/52.txt`

Kiddushin 52 - Betrothal with Stolen Goods
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1pTbt39jzdobVAPtOK7u7al4mTjpjve8E1pM_5uUndH_U_0yFxmbVxr3wa0xM9MDY5rs1h00AbiJiMQfjiOjQDKjyYgPXIdIKlbr6vKqQ9CxQyXBZkhcYWrxpeb_cQ_odRZVT4oDy7yqB/s1600-h/Frederic+Lord+Leighton+-+A+Girl+Carrying+a+Basket+of+Fruit+on+Her+Head.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5274298294877166450" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1pTbt39jzdobVAPtOK7u7al4mTjpjve8E1pM_5uUndH_U_0yFxmbVxr3wa0xM9MDY5rs1h00AbiJiMQfjiOjQDKjyYgPXIdIKlbr6vKqQ9CxQyXBZkhcYWrxpeb_cQ_odRZVT4oDy7yqB/s320/Frederic+Lord+Leighton+-+A+Girl+Carrying+a+Basket+of+Fruit+on+Her+Head.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 207px;" /></a>From the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-50-betrothal-by-liar.html">previous teaching</a> about a man who betrothed five women with a basket of figs collected in the Sabbatical year and belonging to the women, we can draw three conclusions:<br />
<br />
- One can betroth with the produce of the Sabbatical year, even though it is ownerless while it grows because collecting this produce is allowed;<div><br />
- If one betroths with stolen goods, even if they are the bride's, the betrothal is invalid;</div><div><br />
- A woman can become an agent of betrothal for another woman, even where she also becomes a rival wife.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Girl Carrying a Basket of Fruit on Her Head by Frederic Lord Leighton</div></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/53.txt
<a id="src-00363"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/53.txt`

Kiddushin 53 - Betrothal with a Priest's Portion of Sacrifices
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEib6OGjYQPSbESPFy9k1VapWyu39X8ungKWW7TA7jTWfDw8dCUZ0Ccu4jKA72q3vfMTDBQorWSCXGcpU74Rr0Ut7epbJIeDTwymojs3NHrRqBu0mx3WFkGxRVWXbCOkBRYxS2AdJnAs6L5u/s1600-h/Sir+Thomas+Francis+Dicksee+-+The++offering.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5274698766499141090" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEib6OGjYQPSbESPFy9k1VapWyu39X8ungKWW7TA7jTWfDw8dCUZ0Ccu4jKA72q3vfMTDBQorWSCXGcpU74Rr0Ut7epbJIeDTwymojs3NHrRqBu0mx3WFkGxRVWXbCOkBRYxS2AdJnAs6L5u/s320/Sir+Thomas+Francis+Dicksee+-+The++offering.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 233px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If  a priest betroths a woman with his portion of the sacrificial offering, whether most holy (such as burnt-offering and sin-offering) or an offering of lesser holiness (such as peace and thanks-offering), she is not betrothed. The portions allotted to the priest and the owner of the offering are not theirs but rather Divine property, which they are merely permitted to eat.<br />
<br />
But it may be asked, how can a woman come into the Inner Temple courtyard to accept Kiddushin? Her father can accept her Kiddushin, she can appoint an agent, or she can force her way in!<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Offering by Sir Thomas Francis Dicksee&nbsp;</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/54.txt
<a id="src-00364"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/54.txt`

Kiddushin 54 - Misappropriation
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikJhpFRm2ZxVKZfPzuY-QJbRqgFLC2veWOKM4nF6zYTbU4faYXSwbRkUQf34tAsL3Lf9kyCLf1gssiIR5ezM-dTbGMxMEAg6nal3R0S73wC8uN4Vqt2c0AtmpGVav6aQ2j-4Z79UKKAhOO/s1600-h/Gerard+Ter+Borg+-+The+Dancing+Couple.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5275040976885516210" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikJhpFRm2ZxVKZfPzuY-QJbRqgFLC2veWOKM4nF6zYTbU4faYXSwbRkUQf34tAsL3Lf9kyCLf1gssiIR5ezM-dTbGMxMEAg6nal3R0S73wC8uN4Vqt2c0AtmpGVav6aQ2j-4Z79UKKAhOO/s320/Gerard+Ter+Borg+-+The+Dancing+Couple.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 288px;" /></a>If one betroths a woman with a second tithe (produce separated from the crops which must be brought to Jerusalem and eaten there), he has not betrothed her because the second tithe is not his but Divine property (accepted ruling of Rabbi Meir).<br />
<br />
If one betroths a woman with property belonging to the Temple treasury, then, if he did this by mistake, the property first became his, and even though he committed misappropriation, the betrothal took effect. If, on the other hand, he did it knowingly, then the property remained consecrated, not his, and the betrothal did not work (accepted ruling of Rabbi Yehudah).<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Dancing Couple by Gerard Ter Borg</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/55.txt
<a id="src-00365"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/55.txt`

Kiddushin 55 - Animal Lost near Jerusalem
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjxOVpHfYjaW8JVJF0RT6tNIkuKQNiOQ2zQ0nxeNGIkgnIYe1lGvmyZ5WwKUK_rVdsxe4vA5270phR13KbHpNeFyBlDXgUAzWwddZRzveUt-T81F3kubJoS0h271xNkzDeARU9gpTazzIMq/s1600-h/Henriette+Ronner-Knip+-+A+Goat+In+A+Meadow.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5275372779121190114" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjxOVpHfYjaW8JVJF0RT6tNIkuKQNiOQ2zQ0nxeNGIkgnIYe1lGvmyZ5WwKUK_rVdsxe4vA5270phR13KbHpNeFyBlDXgUAzWwddZRzveUt-T81F3kubJoS0h271xNkzDeARU9gpTazzIMq/s320/Henriette+Ronner-Knip+-+A+Goat+In+A+Meadow.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 267px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If an animal suitable for an offering was found between Jerusalem and Migdal Eder or at a similar distance (4 miles) from Jerusalem, males are treated as burnt offerings, and females are treated as peace offerings.<br />
<br />
But males can also be peace offerings! - We treat them with the stringencies of both; thus, if someone steps forward and voluntarily obligates himself to the monetary value of the lost animal to redeem it, he needs to consecrate the value of both (Rabbi Meir).<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yochanan: But redemption, though effective, is not allowed! - He waits for the animal to get a blemish and be redeemed.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Goat In A Meadow by Henriette Ronner-Knip</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/56.txt
<a id="src-00366"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/56.txt`

Kiddushin 56 - Betrothal with Items Forbidden For Benefit
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilaZQUpT_-k2HYIg-eBc2oStRNN1tv5SuKdO4C8AB5hbmjj5tWHsiZtAuFyowJ4OnpnAGkvaL0nopMwy5tCejEzSeQ1G7Gh1LqzwKdp3fXlzdX3UDwI3Zhyphenhyphen_d8X71GgVXPTX_tVaaz83rJ/s1600-h/kiddushin56.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5275790731404657410" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilaZQUpT_-k2HYIg-eBc2oStRNN1tv5SuKdO4C8AB5hbmjj5tWHsiZtAuFyowJ4OnpnAGkvaL0nopMwy5tCejEzSeQ1G7Gh1LqzwKdp3fXlzdX3UDwI3Zhyphenhyphen_d8X71GgVXPTX_tVaaz83rJ/s320/kiddushin56.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 240px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If one betroths a woman with the fruits of the tree's first three years, with grains planted in a vineyard, with an ox that was condemned to be stoned, with a decapitated calf, with birds of a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tzaraath">metzora</a>, with hair of a Nazirite, with a firstborn male of a donkey, with a mixture of meat cooked with milk, with an unconsecrated animal slaughtered in the Temple Courtyard, she is not betrothed.<br />
<br />
However, she is betrothed if he transgressed and sold any of these items and betrothed her with their payment.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Burns and Highland Mary by Thomas Faed&nbsp;</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/57.txt
<a id="src-00367"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/57.txt`

Kiddushin 57 - Sources for Benefit Prohibitions
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9INOkRO19KVoul7iqryU6z2L0HaoI_ow4O2foh2-0zlPtsLvkzLQy97y-JSMWK1tmz5119GdVzcOChBBWhaiIp8VT28cgwbQrC8V2urqb2R5joJlHzvDB9W2c1r-A3Eatw3SSGeUxhtxC/s1600-h/Peter+Paul+Rubens+-+Boy+with+Bird.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5276187044482451122" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9INOkRO19KVoul7iqryU6z2L0HaoI_ow4O2foh2-0zlPtsLvkzLQy97y-JSMWK1tmz5119GdVzcOChBBWhaiIp8VT28cgwbQrC8V2urqb2R5joJlHzvDB9W2c1r-A3Eatw3SSGeUxhtxC/s320/Peter+Paul+Rubens+-+Boy+with+Bird.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 265px;" /></a>Decapitated calf, used as atonement for murder, is forbidden for benefit and can not be used to betroth a woman - because it is compared to sacrifices, which are forbidden for benefit.<br />
<br />
Why are the birds of a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tzaraath">metsora</a> forbidden for benefit? The procedure requires slaughtering one of them, then dipping the other one into the blood and letting it go free. It is performed outside the city but is compared to sacrifices inside the Temple, which are prohibited for benefit. The bird which is let free is afterward not prohibited for benefit, for the Torah would not create a stumbling block.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Boy with Bird by Peter Paul Rubens</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/58.txt
<a id="src-00368"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/58.txt`

Kiddushin 58 - Money from the Sale of Forbidden Objects
Money from the sale of <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/12/kiddushin-21-hebrew-servant-wants-to-be.html">forbidden objects listed previously</a> is permitted for use, and betrothal with it is valid. Why?<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhGa5IhSUQW-Yw1L4msvFcigY_XhDamEBp2L_bYY8JA1SQIb6kLDyQlAzP8wK2iERFz3pvMEjroKuADmV7B_gqDfhUrGUYKFNj1XvawrBdYJmMn-gG1rkUPxoU9UL0AlgDvE6sotRWZtqNA/s1600-h/Terracotta-Idols-Of-Tabasco,-From-The-Ancient-Cities-Of-New-Mexico,-By-Claude-Joseph-Desire-Charnay,-Pub.-1887.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5276925720755697202" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhGa5IhSUQW-Yw1L4msvFcigY_XhDamEBp2L_bYY8JA1SQIb6kLDyQlAzP8wK2iERFz3pvMEjroKuADmV7B_gqDfhUrGUYKFNj1XvawrBdYJmMn-gG1rkUPxoU9UL0AlgDvE6sotRWZtqNA/s320/Terracotta-Idols-Of-Tabasco,-From-The-Ancient-Cities-Of-New-Mexico,-By-Claude-Joseph-Desire-Charnay,-Pub.-1887.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 319px;" /></a><br />
<br />
Regarding idolatry, it says, "You shall not bring it into your house and become banned like it," which means that whatever you generate from the sale of idols is forbidden, but other money is permitted. But this may teach the rule, not an exception. - No, because there is another exception where money is forbidden: the fruit of the seventh year. Money from the sale of other items is permitted.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Terracotta Idols Of Tabasco, From The Ancient Cities Of New Mexico, by Claude Joseph Desire Charnay</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/59.txt
<a id="src-00369"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/59.txt`

Kiddushin 59 - Stealing the Bride
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLhhe61cQWM5jG3pzpS9PCICNtQr1F3w5k5gBP5ap0fgFmgZpyiTDaJhlkN4jWn4-_T-jwMw7sRbY0RxONdYm-gm8mWCIhGFgmyJqytGCgpekNGe6P8JUCJdxGRozadVXBQaLCXqi4oFgy/s1600-h/Vicente+de+Parades+:+A+Flirtation" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5276934614050826978" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLhhe61cQWM5jG3pzpS9PCICNtQr1F3w5k5gBP5ap0fgFmgZpyiTDaJhlkN4jWn4-_T-jwMw7sRbY0RxONdYm-gm8mWCIhGFgmyJqytGCgpekNGe6P8JUCJdxGRozadVXBQaLCXqi4oFgy/s320/Vicente+de+Parades+:+A+Flirtation" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 220px;" /></a>If one says to his fellow: "Go and betroth so-and-so to me," and the fellow went and betrothed her to himself, she is betrothed to this second person, though he has acted deceitfully.<br />
<br />
Rav Gidel was negotiating to buy a piece of land, but Rav Abba bought it first. He  wanted to give the land when informed, but Rav Gidel would not accept presents. The land was left for students' use and acquired the name "The Land of the Rabbis."<br />
<br />
If one says to a woman, "Behold, you are betrothed to me after thirty days" (valid), and another man comes and betrothed her in the meantime, she is betrothed to the second man.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Flirtation by Vicente de Parades</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/6.txt
<a id="src-00370"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/6.txt`

Kiddushin 6 - Say what you mean
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSWaEp27NXt2e8e0MtHG8K1a-ArRGQxIPKijVW8C06ba1cAiQCd6KlAXsSA_3SUliCQLIvkgZJLpgeBUtN24uGYbFF4uLI3NNwINGprD0JkzcU4e_8ByfkfpRRmk_TBXooYCWy1Csmu30DUpcUeT6VjfZmRGgFKKSZdSqpLZfRHxQLAsxX6vmcCIqHN-I_/s1200/Jacobus_Buys_(1724-1801)_-_The_Betrothal_-_1298226_-_National_Trust.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1200" data-original-width="852" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSWaEp27NXt2e8e0MtHG8K1a-ArRGQxIPKijVW8C06ba1cAiQCd6KlAXsSA_3SUliCQLIvkgZJLpgeBUtN24uGYbFF4uLI3NNwINGprD0JkzcU4e_8ByfkfpRRmk_TBXooYCWy1Csmu30DUpcUeT6VjfZmRGgFKKSZdSqpLZfRHxQLAsxX6vmcCIqHN-I_/s320/Jacobus_Buys_(1724-1801)_-_The_Betrothal_-_1298226_-_National_Trust.jpg" width="227" /></a></div>The standard procedure of getting married is a man saying to a woman, "Behold, you are betrothed to me." But if he uses a different unequivocal formula, it also works. For example, "Behold, you are my wife," "You are my betrothed," and "You are acquired to me" are all valid declarations of kiddushin.<p></p><p>What if he uses expressions that hint at the language of the Torah but can be interpreted otherwise? For example, "You are singled out for me," "You are my helpmate," "My <i>taken</i> one?" The Talmud resolves at least the last question positively because the Torah said, "When a man shall <i>take</i> a woman."</p><p>Let's return to the "You are singled out for me" question. What are the exact circumstances here? If they are talking in general about the subject of marriage, and then he gives her the money, even if he does not say anything else, she is betrothed. And if they were not talking about marriage, what is she agreeing to? The answer is that if he is silent, she is indeed betrothed. It is when he adds these words, does he maybe mean to hire her for work? And here, the Talmud does not have an answer.</p><p>Art: The Betrothal by Jacobus Buys</p><p><br /></p>

---

### content/kiddushin/60.txt
<a id="src-00371"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/60.txt`

Kiddushin 60 - Betrothal with Delayed Payment
<div class="separator"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEghJwP3o3RFwy85Js5MIDWBPoB9dQh4GrxdXEL6Q5s_Q_vIJyfJWl4m9sCX8YhyBV5rL4WjQfoXTrP4az9NrhxyNieJNo6YR4nybtlsEpL6S1STn3kZwMoI6LCU1CiM_jpdguT5EnAYditJ/s1600-h/Quinten+Metsys+-+The+Moneylender+And+His+Wife.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5277240909757340402" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEghJwP3o3RFwy85Js5MIDWBPoB9dQh4GrxdXEL6Q5s_Q_vIJyfJWl4m9sCX8YhyBV5rL4WjQfoXTrP4az9NrhxyNieJNo6YR4nybtlsEpL6S1STn3kZwMoI6LCU1CiM_jpdguT5EnAYditJ/s320/Quinten+Metsys+-+The+Moneylender+And+His+Wife.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 249px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a></div>A man said to a woman: "Become betrothed to me after thirty days," and someone betrothed her in the interim. When the thirtieth day arrives, the second betrothal remains effective and thus prevents the first one from going into effect.<br />
<br />
If one says to a woman, “You are betrothed to me on condition that I will give you two hundred silver coins (about $10,000) – she is betrothed to him, provided that he pays. When he pays, she is betrothed to him retroactively from the first day. Therefore, if she accepted a betrothal from someone else in the interim, it is void.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Moneylender And His Wife (detail) by Quinten Metsys</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/61.txt
<a id="src-00372"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/61.txt`

Kiddushin 61 - Conditions
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjVUAeDeVVceWHwEGn-FW0fMpDbMlteN4FIlFQi2U7z3Wd24jaQWkckFLM8KCs7lzoX3yRQhLPv0sEXSi307raqBPdg88mGKjhWDM_NFWtqqPKGzxeQBMzr_GmSRLtHtKpetujFHr4fv7i/s1600-h/Artur+Markowicz+:+Torah+Scribe" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5277614266322847954" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhjVUAeDeVVceWHwEGn-FW0fMpDbMlteN4FIlFQi2U7z3Wd24jaQWkckFLM8KCs7lzoX3yRQhLPv0sEXSi307raqBPdg88mGKjhWDM_NFWtqqPKGzxeQBMzr_GmSRLtHtKpetujFHr4fv7i/s320/Artur+Markowicz+:+Torah+Scribe" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 232px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>All stipulations (such as "I will marry you if you do this") must observe the following rules:<br />
<br />
* They must be doubled, such as if yes, then.. and if no, then ...<br />
* The stipulation must precede the act, that is, "If you do this, I will marry you..."<br />
* The positive must precede the negative<br />
<br />
This is learned from the conditions that Moshe set, "If the children of Gad and the children of Reuven will cross..." and "But if they will not cross..."<br />
<br />
If these rules are not adhered to, the conditions are void. However, there are other opinions, and one better be careful.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Torah Scribe by Artur Markowicz</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/62.txt
<a id="src-00373"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/62.txt`

Kiddushin 62 - Mistaken But Valid Betrothals And Those That Can't Happen Yet
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhkOHXtPw3mu15YLvXYSJx_8a_PVc1xWlFSpqKmA9h5Wzp5C3TwKBDpYJWU-0mnITiEyI6rSt8qsY2PUlbgR1zeeIVuaF4VwkDm4xCrbDwLsd5hQvYKEH5ZucwEVLaf1CVxJG91FW0e7fGp/s1600-h/Hugues+Merle+-+A+Beggar+Woman.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5277966989444665266" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhkOHXtPw3mu15YLvXYSJx_8a_PVc1xWlFSpqKmA9h5Wzp5C3TwKBDpYJWU-0mnITiEyI6rSt8qsY2PUlbgR1zeeIVuaF4VwkDm4xCrbDwLsd5hQvYKEH5ZucwEVLaf1CVxJG91FW0e7fGp/s320/Hugues+Merle+-+A+Beggar+Woman.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 230px;" /></a>If one betrothed a woman and subsequently said, "I thought that she was the daughter of a Kohen, but in fact, she is the daughter of a Levi," or vice versa, "I thought that she was poor, but in fact, she is rich," or vice versa - the woman is betrothed, because she did not mislead him.<br />
<br />
Suppose one performs an act of betrothal and tells a woman, "Become betrothed to me after I convert to Judaism," or "after your husband dies," or "After your sister (my current wife) dies." In all these cases, she is not betrothed even after the specified event takes place.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Beggar Woman by Hugues Merle</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/63.txt
<a id="src-00374"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/63.txt`

Kiddushin 63 - The Father of the Bride Has a Say
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSBKe62_HK299QrD_g-3UHOfRy9ayOoEj_9GdtW3CfjGSoU602FcMBRu4WwoVSG0LunoTLlFIEiPBPZzbIC8BL5PRjNsR6YjwCxbE9BjQJEuVZ9Xpb5cdbewJUdB4eyPGq5rTqBIom9oSv/s1600-h/Charles+Henry+Tenre+:+The+Surprise.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5278367261191866226" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSBKe62_HK299QrD_g-3UHOfRy9ayOoEj_9GdtW3CfjGSoU602FcMBRu4WwoVSG0LunoTLlFIEiPBPZzbIC8BL5PRjNsR6YjwCxbE9BjQJEuVZ9Xpb5cdbewJUdB4eyPGq5rTqBIom9oSv/s320/Charles+Henry+Tenre+:+The+Surprise.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 247px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If a man says to a woman: "Become betrothed to me on condition that my father does not protest," and the father dies without protesting, the woman is betrothed. If the son dies, the father should protest retroactively so that the woman avoids levirate marriage.<br />
<br />
If the father of a girl declared: "I gave my daughter in betrothal, but I do not know to whom," and a man  came and said, ""I am the one," he is believed. If two men came, both of them should give a Get. If they wish, one gives a Get, and the other marries her.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Surprise by Charles Henry Tenre</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/64.txt
<a id="src-00375"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/64.txt`

Kiddushin 64 - Older Daughters and Younger Daughters
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivFECCb2meTrIfNqdmtaJpsEKETFGL096nt-IKdEzUPMvlAFJPOK2nzGidXahsW1WcB-ddiSJf0HJPz9_s24sfPQqsfovH1lXtiX_WPbmg4KpQpEaV0qI-F0sNz70M1EMTTIE37GRu7V0L/s1600-h/Paul+Sandby+:+Daughters+of+the+Earl+Waldegrave.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5278759995355717874" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEivFECCb2meTrIfNqdmtaJpsEKETFGL096nt-IKdEzUPMvlAFJPOK2nzGidXahsW1WcB-ddiSJf0HJPz9_s24sfPQqsfovH1lXtiX_WPbmg4KpQpEaV0qI-F0sNz70M1EMTTIE37GRu7V0L/s320/Paul+Sandby+:+Daughters+of+the+Earl+Waldegrave.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 231px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If one has two groups of daughters from two wives, and he says: “I gave my eldest daughter in betrothal to a man, but I do not know if it was the eldest daughter of the older ones, or the eldest of the younger ones, or the youngest of the older ones - they are all prohibited from marrying other men, except for the youngest daughter of the younger ones – says Rabbi Meir.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yosi says they are all permitted to marry other men, except for the eldest of the older ones, for a man would not voluntarily put himself in a position of doubtful outcome.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Daughters of the Earl Waldegrave by Paul Sandby</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/65.txt
<a id="src-00376"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/65.txt`

Kiddushin 65 - Disagreement about Who Betrothed Whom
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiLCcncSUF-Qj5CGhICuCj3mcsO7LjQ3-zaAXSuKzN47gEm90tgTaQLWd1s0uqH-lwz1myaREfDRwEAE7jk7m6-q1aumVQF6FQdNs_9wH1dbKPRB2GWrfJR5sz-dpHkFUxfEDXT3lPU93hL/s1600-h/Faustine+-+Maxwell+Armfield.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5278988348692947826" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiLCcncSUF-Qj5CGhICuCj3mcsO7LjQ3-zaAXSuKzN47gEm90tgTaQLWd1s0uqH-lwz1myaREfDRwEAE7jk7m6-q1aumVQF6FQdNs_9wH1dbKPRB2GWrfJR5sz-dpHkFUxfEDXT3lPU93hL/s320/Faustine+-+Maxwell+Armfield.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 258px;" /></a>If a man says to a woman: "I betrothed you," and she says: "You did not betroth me," - he is forbidden to marry her relatives (mother, sister, etc.), but she is permitted to marry his relatives.<br />
<br />
If he says: "I betrothed you," and she says: "You did not betroth me, but rather you betrothed my daughter," - he is forbidden to marry the relatives of the mother, and the mother is permitted to marry his relatives; he is allowed to marry the relatives of the daughter, and the daughter is permitted to marry his relatives.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Faustine by Maxwell Armfield</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/66.txt
<a id="src-00377"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/66.txt`

Kiddushin 66 - Credibility of Witnesses
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2Udv65USfsSMXzS84Ce6jrMmxmCUrhAPdnMCxw6lBSLxx6g9GDddYI0eIuTxXXT1e2Y0UxsS0dMaUHcvtYY_7ZL9BzMD4XKOclrjn74Ibs1N8_yNIyWx6Mcsjznc3WYEFIr3KKnaVNrEo/s1600-h/Jacob+Jordaens+-+Two+Standing+Oxen.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5279506491650419074" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh2Udv65USfsSMXzS84Ce6jrMmxmCUrhAPdnMCxw6lBSLxx6g9GDddYI0eIuTxXXT1e2Y0UxsS0dMaUHcvtYY_7ZL9BzMD4XKOclrjn74Ibs1N8_yNIyWx6Mcsjznc3WYEFIr3KKnaVNrEo/s320/Jacob+Jordaens+-+Two+Standing+Oxen.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 269px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">If a single witness says to a person, "Your ox was sodomized," and it is, therefore, unfit to be a sacrifice, and that person remains silent, the witness is believed.<br />
<br />
King Yannai was incited by Elazar Ben Po'ira against the sages of Israel. Yannai wore the golden plate of the High Priest, and one Sage protested that Yannai was an unfit Kohen. Elazar suggested killing all Sages. But what of the Torah? - Here it is in the corner; anybody who wants can learn! Yannai executed the Sages. And why was Yannai fit? The witnesses to his unfitness were later established as false witnesses.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Two Standing Oxen by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jacob Jordaens</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/67.txt
<a id="src-00378"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/67.txt`

Kiddushin 67 - Offspring
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiEvd6-WbVY5ibjwiCB_iSLuwF_LY9GJUvM707fFaR1DQGWuSQFSbfDp77hPU8c7YiUdJakL40qxd9R3nIu1WHQO1ojjjbHt9q2iAmE_Jbpvm01_dZr8wypMuMFpjQ6HBWsP69YfDrqEy3L/s1600-h/Josef+Johann+Suss+-+Jewish+Scholars+Debating.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5280510977378577122" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiEvd6-WbVY5ibjwiCB_iSLuwF_LY9GJUvM707fFaR1DQGWuSQFSbfDp77hPU8c7YiUdJakL40qxd9R3nIu1WHQO1ojjjbHt9q2iAmE_Jbpvm01_dZr8wypMuMFpjQ6HBWsP69YfDrqEy3L/s320/Josef+Johann+Suss+-+Jewish+Scholars+Debating.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 250px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>In every case where betrothal takes effect, and the Torah did not prohibit marriage, the offspring follows the male. If a Jewish woman was married to a Kohen, Levi, or Yisrael, the son is like the father.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
In every case where betrothal takes effect, even though the marriage is prohibited, the offspring follows the blemished party. A woman mamzer married to a Jew or a Jewess married to a mamzer - the child is a mamzer.</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
In every case where marrying is prohibited to the degree that betrothal does not even take effect, the offspring is a mamzer. Thus, mamzer (literally, "defective seed") is an offspring from any one of the forbidden relations in the Torah, such as a married woman with another man (married or unmarried). Mamzer is forbidden to marry anyone but a convert, and his or her child remains a mamzer.</div><div><br /></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Jewish Scholars Debating by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Josef Johann Suss</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/68.txt
<a id="src-00379"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/68.txt`

Kiddushin 68 - Marriage with Gentiles
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQoxSd3biGqG93QhyphenhyphenJGbP8WJR8SBKJp_KiXU9Z6AB2eLFeNdrz2dmJg_0hGowTp-ldhNn-yWWJ6Ql89PxAGPBCGlTSCLrv4-WwCE28DWgBGoqJRhUaQghqlqkt0P56wnxGSZiLgXl6U5gc/s1600-h/Louis+Henry+Charles+Moeller++-Grandfather%27s+Pleasure.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5280616190638223154" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQoxSd3biGqG93QhyphenhyphenJGbP8WJR8SBKJp_KiXU9Z6AB2eLFeNdrz2dmJg_0hGowTp-ldhNn-yWWJ6Ql89PxAGPBCGlTSCLrv4-WwCE28DWgBGoqJRhUaQghqlqkt0P56wnxGSZiLgXl6U5gc/s320/Louis+Henry+Charles+Moeller++-Grandfather%27s+Pleasure.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 238px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>From where do we know that Kiddushin does not take effect with a gentile? - "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/7-3.htm">You shall not make marriages with them</a>."<br />
<br />
From where do we know that her offspring is non-Jewish like her? - "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/7-4.htm">For he will turn your son away from Me, and they will serve other gods.</a>"  Thus your grandson who comes from your Jewish daughter is called your son, but your grandson who comes from a heathen woman is not called your son; instead, he is considered her son.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Grandfather's Pleasure by Louis Henry Charles Moeller</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/69.txt
<a id="src-00380"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/69.txt`

Kiddushin 69 - Ten Genealogical Classes
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgWkjuYp_5nZgLKXOTGsfsVNq-bt33taSv7MU6EFdJrsv29-zJlr3rBk5Iu4Rw3rV3lcUqbhlcmuYx0ygPgte3n5lYxFEycuMYrA-v544azYzKME-r8YIy1g4b5gm8ew8fUtZxPbiwGfHZA/s1600-h/A+Children%27s+Party+-+Walter+Frederick+Osborne.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5280625366039251986" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgWkjuYp_5nZgLKXOTGsfsVNq-bt33taSv7MU6EFdJrsv29-zJlr3rBk5Iu4Rw3rV3lcUqbhlcmuYx0ygPgte3n5lYxFEycuMYrA-v544azYzKME-r8YIy1g4b5gm8ew8fUtZxPbiwGfHZA/s320/A+Children%27s+Party+-+Walter+Frederick+Osborne.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 257px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>According to Rabbi Tarfon, a mamzer can marry a slave woman, have children with her who get her status of slaves, then free them, and they become free Jews and not mamzerim. However, Rabbi Eliezer says that the children are still mamzerim.<br />
<br />
Ten genealogical classes went up from Babylonia to Israel: Kohanim, Leviim, Israelim, Chalalim (disqualified Kohanim), converts, freed Canaanite slaves, mamzerim (illegitimate), Netinim (Gibeonites),  Shetukim (whose mother silences him about the father) and Asufim (foundlings, or ones gathered in).<br />
<br />
Kohanim, Levvim, and Yisraelim are permitted to marry each other. Leviim, Israelim, chalalim, converts, and freed slaves are allowed to marry each other.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A Children's Party by Walter Frederick Osborne</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/7.txt
<a id="src-00381"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/7.txt`

Kiddushin 7 - Cash Flow
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg6usU0eXa-AgvGr9i7WGKPY3yXLLj4eLzC8LXVsU1HqyC6J_CjORZWzk-Y0uc6ab9ErzTw_KenmIU9nBt2UXJRa7ZHpFQB33TXYFd8v-nn0_VP4wvS3SoZt454TARD9OSw2ScgcqoLn-iP/s1600-h/Antonio+Maria+Fabres+y+Costa+-+The+Gift+for+the+Favorite.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5257586471704629298" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg6usU0eXa-AgvGr9i7WGKPY3yXLLj4eLzC8LXVsU1HqyC6J_CjORZWzk-Y0uc6ab9ErzTw_KenmIU9nBt2UXJRa7ZHpFQB33TXYFd8v-nn0_VP4wvS3SoZt454TARD9OSw2ScgcqoLn-iP/s320/Antonio+Maria+Fabres+y+Costa+-+The+Gift+for+the+Favorite.jpg" style="float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a>If a woman suggests to a man, “Give money to so-and-so and I will thereby become betrothed to you,” and the man gives the money as specified and says the formula, the woman becomes betrothed, through the principle of a guarantor. A loan guarantor, even though he does not personally receive the benefit, still binds himself to repay. So too, she commits herself in return for the money based on her say-so.<br />
<br />An extraordinary man who never accepts gifts (none such today) can marry a woman by giving her the pleasure of taking her gift.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Gift for the Favorite by Antonio Maria Fabres y Costa</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/70.txt
<a id="src-00382"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/70.txt`

Kiddushin 70 - Whoever Calls Others Unfit is Himself Unfit
<div class="separator"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhb1Bv93ko-tjqw64iOgoDw1Xe1oLEtrk08E1jFOJ_KZQw53U6GX9llkLBf59VhxMBuN9ZX7sC_pZ2WB7BJ-tB-YXTYqmiCF8zny-enfcpt-TDU4X2Bbw362_30xN9U63UInyzm3dRa9Ae_/s1600-h/Karoly+Ferenczy+-+Joseph+Sold+Into+Slavery+By+His+Brothers.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5280981909882236658" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhb1Bv93ko-tjqw64iOgoDw1Xe1oLEtrk08E1jFOJ_KZQw53U6GX9llkLBf59VhxMBuN9ZX7sC_pZ2WB7BJ-tB-YXTYqmiCF8zny-enfcpt-TDU4X2Bbw362_30xN9U63UInyzm3dRa9Ae_/s320/Karoly+Ferenczy+-+Joseph+Sold+Into+Slavery+By+His+Brothers.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 274px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Whoever declares others to be genealogically unfit is himself genealogically unfit, never speaks in praise of others, and declares them unfit with his own blemish.<br />
<br />
A man in Pumbedita offended Rav Yehuda. The man used to call other people slaves. Rav Yehuda excommunicated him and pronounced him a slave. In the court of Rav Nachman, Rav Yehudah explained that he pronounced the man slave because he called others slaves. Usually, this only allows one to suspect, but on that day, Rav Matna, who had not visited Pumbedita for 13 years, came and confirmed that the man was  a slave, and more blemishes were discovered.<br />
<br />
Art: Karoly Ferenczy - Joseph Sold Into Slavery By His Brothers</span>

---

### content/kiddushin/71.txt

Kiddushin 71 - Family Conflict
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiyN3XZwOPv5rl9XRqD2a0IRYFYYg5psqs_rGbU9jDhMJ0i5LsZaPfHz-pMgyGf135YgU6HBFuhSU64SAoNpQSLCkBaSixIBajRacW5KnX0PLkFBobp7TZjxfHpXecM4LcBJ9e3tuNKbmQR/s1600-h/A+Peaceful+Moment+-+Charles+Baugniet.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5281313648741313618" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiyN3XZwOPv5rl9XRqD2a0IRYFYYg5psqs_rGbU9jDhMJ0i5LsZaPfHz-pMgyGf135YgU6HBFuhSU64SAoNpQSLCkBaSixIBajRacW5KnX0PLkFBobp7TZjxfHpXecM4LcBJ9e3tuNKbmQR/s320/A+Peaceful+Moment+-+Charles+Baugniet.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 254px;" /></a>Rav Yehudah needed help finding a genealogically fit wife for his son. Ulla asked him, - do we know from where we come?  We might be descended from those "...<a href="http://scripturetext.com/amos/6-4.htm">who lie upon beds of ivory and defile their couches</a>." Instead, go after silence, that is, find a family whose members are quiet and peaceable.<br />
<br />
If you see two families in conflict with one another, you can assume that there is some genealogical flaw in one of them, and because of that flaw, Heaven will not allow one of them to cleave to the other.<div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A Peaceful Moment by Charles Baugniet</div>

---

Kiddushin 72 - Generations
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgPTC6tNgZ7je3NgcmM8-SrSQR2kebYLCRkSKgHbxbD2n8K5UEEL-flDFWShUF9zwFTKUKUcvKKriJ-oJ0pwuJt99omYgBjhoFbk5qLTkczZvOQogrXVoiwYSHvIGSdDcSRrZGngen_qKrM/s1600-h/Alexandre+Evariste+Fragonard+-+Cardinal+Mazarin+at+the+Deathbed+of+Eustache+Le+Sueur.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5281615827280458642" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgPTC6tNgZ7je3NgcmM8-SrSQR2kebYLCRkSKgHbxbD2n8K5UEEL-flDFWShUF9zwFTKUKUcvKKriJ-oJ0pwuJt99omYgBjhoFbk5qLTkczZvOQogrXVoiwYSHvIGSdDcSRrZGngen_qKrM/s320/Alexandre+Evariste+Fragonard+-+Cardinal+Mazarin+at+the+Deathbed+of+Eustache+Le+Sueur.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 262px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div>When R' Akiva died, Rebbi was born. When Rabbi died, Rav Yehudah was born. When Rav Yehudah died, Rava was born. When Rava died, Rav Ashi was born. This teaches you that a righteous person does not depart from the world until another righteous person like him is born, as it is said, "<a href="http://bible.cc/ecclesiastes/1-5.htm">And the sun rises, and the sun sets...</a>"&nbsp;</div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
Mamzerim will be genealogically pure in the Messianic Era because "<a href="http://bible.cc/ezekiel/36-25.htm">I will cast pure water on you, and you will be purified from all your impurities, and from all your defilements, I will purify you</a>."</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Cardinal Mazarin at the Deathbed of Eustache Le Sueur by Alexandre Evariste Fragonard</div>
