### content/kiddushin/73.txt
<a id="src-00385"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/73.txt`

Kiddushin 73 - Whom Can a Convert Marry?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjb5v45Gczj3Yx0xbKugp-zikA8HW0G_-eoGkpYolX2Ia33A0NtKW_QGYaEWA_xZScCEHkwDAKOJ_5RzligaoClFRt90qaItbT8zGpZk_WEfcnBTWWOOI4DqGvKlLLjQjkwGZDYPqQgEFHl/s1600-h/Edwin+Lord+Weeks+-++The+Silk+Merchants.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5282120677921087426" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjb5v45Gczj3Yx0xbKugp-zikA8HW0G_-eoGkpYolX2Ia33A0NtKW_QGYaEWA_xZScCEHkwDAKOJ_5RzligaoClFRt90qaItbT8zGpZk_WEfcnBTWWOOI4DqGvKlLLjQjkwGZDYPqQgEFHl/s320/Edwin+Lord+Weeks+-++The+Silk+Merchants.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 221px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">Rava lectured in Mechuza: "A convert is permitted to marry a daughter of a Kohen." The people of Mechuza loaded him with fine silks. He then taught them: "A convert is permitted to marry a woman who is a mamzer." They told him, "You have ruined the effect of the first statement you made."<br />
<br />
Shetuki (his unmarried mother silences him when asked about the identity of his father) should not marry an Israelite of unblemished lineage. Even though he is Kosher, since most of the men who might have been his father are Kosher, this is an additional measure to protect genealogical purity.<br />
<br />
Art: Edwin Lord Weeks -  The Silk Merchants</span>

---

### content/kiddushin/74.txt
<a id="src-00386"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/74.txt`

Kiddushin 74 - Who Is To Be Believed
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBIm9Vra6aJA8ApDHQFk5COIrj4B3z6wGw7UU0IDiIM8T84IOxZM91-7faaFWMOml44Wg_-pky3kiHzg6maNeZa4-wS6POMhlXhYg7amL03yuZmUoeXq7YZznE_OUbXJWvAJ5dwdcTx7Ss/s1600-h/Pieter+de+Hooch+-+A+Woman+with+her+Baby+in+her+Lap.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5282469022957247122" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBIm9Vra6aJA8ApDHQFk5COIrj4B3z6wGw7UU0IDiIM8T84IOxZM91-7faaFWMOml44Wg_-pky3kiHzg6maNeZa4-wS6POMhlXhYg7amL03yuZmUoeXq7YZznE_OUbXJWvAJ5dwdcTx7Ss/s320/Pieter+de+Hooch+-+A+Woman+with+her+Baby+in+her+Lap.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 240px;" /></a>The seller is believed when he states, "I sold the item to this person, and the other person gave me the money against my will" - all the time that the merchandise is still in his possession.<br />
<br />A midwife is believed to tell us who is the firstborn – but only immediately after birth; his mother is believed for the first seven days of his life; his father is always believed because of “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/21-17.htm">...shall recognize the firstborn</a>.”<br />
<br />
A mother of a child born out of wedlock is believed if she says that she cohabited with a person who is genealogically fit.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Woman with her Baby in her Lap by Pieter de Hooch</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/75.txt
<a id="src-00387"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/75.txt`

Kiddushin 75 - Those Whose Prohibitions are Uncertain
<div class="separator"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjx-N_guiDq30yOV1mgoGn9Mdg75ZBUU6zJX1559U753u13dxHyaBFyxA_P6Vb9tTN9fUNoSVasmViOSRf4I-9rVrdt-VP-_LtyLsF1lBkTZDJFs6Zk0-ddo1ZXflfzHsLYT7uXMWvlnbbn/s1600-h/Paul+Rose+-+TheLions.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5282788731337051442" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjx-N_guiDq30yOV1mgoGn9Mdg75ZBUU6zJX1559U753u13dxHyaBFyxA_P6Vb9tTN9fUNoSVasmViOSRf4I-9rVrdt-VP-_LtyLsF1lBkTZDJFs6Zk0-ddo1ZXflfzHsLYT7uXMWvlnbbn/s320/Paul+Rose+-+TheLions.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 196px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a></div>Rabbi Eliezer says: “Those whose prohibitions are uncertain, such as children born out-of-wedlock from unknown father and foundlings, can not marry each other or those whose prohibitions are certain.” However, the law is not like this but is like the Mishna, which states that they are allowed to marry each other.<br />
<br />
Two opinions about Cutheans (dwellers of Shomron): that they were insincere converts driven by fear of lions, and the special Kohamin who mixed with them were unfit, or that they were sincere converts and the special Kohanim among them were the best.<div><br /></div><div>Art: The Lions by Paul Rose</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/76.txt
<a id="src-00388"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/76.txt`

Kiddushin 76 - Checking the Family Line
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEica0hZKNRkyQb9aU6IBc9BWbo4StqeeqSd0AMAufI1ssXmyOC2buyko4wgFmOdAxM0W5SMyA60A-x_g9Igvos_cdTnru8gjR95rkVe-AV3djug_3e7J5nawJxyqGg_gfwDm0anYOloxYhE/s1600-h/Charles+Cotteto+-+Four+Breton+Women+At+The+Seashore.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5283168004758659954" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEica0hZKNRkyQb9aU6IBc9BWbo4StqeeqSd0AMAufI1ssXmyOC2buyko4wgFmOdAxM0W5SMyA60A-x_g9Igvos_cdTnru8gjR95rkVe-AV3djug_3e7J5nawJxyqGg_gfwDm0anYOloxYhE/s320/Charles+Cotteto+-+Four+Breton+Women+At+The+Seashore.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 191px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>A Kohen who wishes to marry a daughter of a Kohen must examine the status of her ancestors: her mother and the mother of her mother, the mother of her mother's father and  <span style="font-style: italic;">her</span> mother, the mother of her father and <span style="font-style: italic;">her</span> mother, the mother of her father's father and <span style="font-style: italic;">her</span> mother - but only if there is some evidence of a blemish.<br />
<br />
If in that line he finds a Kohen who served at the Altar, or a member of the Sanhedrin, or a public official, or a charity collector, the investigation stops. The latter two are often involved in quarrels, so any blemish in their genealogy is already known.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Four Breton Women At The Seashore by Charles Cotteto</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/77.txt
<a id="src-00389"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/77.txt`

Kiddushin 77 - Kosher Kohen
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSlaHc74JKfkr2nA10VPvMVHgRXwmW_ig9AoYlQaprL2OkXL0hcO48VljlgAxsVtzluvZBZVCU4tuNAxRztzbmlHWuS7kSdNM_yRjZxE8F_37TGJdDVfDKfN2yTx6HsJlHznr3fWHskDD-bNqevDgJKL09ULVHHrkBT40fOMcdYOgO2oq_xeERUSnfDWhj/s1000/800px-Conversation_Piece_MET_DT4335.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1000" data-original-width="800" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgSlaHc74JKfkr2nA10VPvMVHgRXwmW_ig9AoYlQaprL2OkXL0hcO48VljlgAxsVtzluvZBZVCU4tuNAxRztzbmlHWuS7kSdNM_yRjZxE8F_37TGJdDVfDKfN2yTx6HsJlHznr3fWHskDD-bNqevDgJKL09ULVHHrkBT40fOMcdYOgO2oq_xeERUSnfDWhj/s320/800px-Conversation_Piece_MET_DT4335.jpg" width="256" /></a></div>A child born from a union between a Kohen and a woman who is forbidden to him due to his status as a Kohen is not imbued with Kohanic sanctity. He may not perform the Temple service and is not subject to the prohibition against going to the cemetery.<br />
<br />
Women prohibited to a Kohen include a divorcee, a convert, and a woman who cohabited with any man whom she is Biblically forbidden to marry.<br />
<br />
If a male convert marries a female convert, their daughter is allowed to marry a Kohen.<div><br /></div><div>Art: A Conversation Piece by&nbsp;<span style="background-color: white; color: #202122; font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px;">Lilly Martin Spencer</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/78.txt
<a id="src-00390"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/78.txt`

Kiddushin 78 - Parents Testify About Children
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtknJKnFavO1xR28bih6ken7rdz6fKiJl_UGR8libjohpP4-bWxEMwe3kZwxXZcVp2VdNh04PuCnSV1h1MOgd-bnS8ApNj-XA75-bE67ObhzWkvKAjoImP96IdXLgXKcRlHkJF8lYTIZT5/s1600-h/Mary+Cassatt+-+Child+Drinking+Milk.jpeg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5283960207793992834" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtknJKnFavO1xR28bih6ken7rdz6fKiJl_UGR8libjohpP4-bWxEMwe3kZwxXZcVp2VdNh04PuCnSV1h1MOgd-bnS8ApNj-XA75-bE67ObhzWkvKAjoImP96IdXLgXKcRlHkJF8lYTIZT5/s320/Mary+Cassatt+-+Child+Drinking+Milk.jpeg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 274px;" /></a>If a Kohen cohabits with his sister, he renders her  a zonah (someone who engaged in an illicit relationship that is forbidden to her), but he does not render her a chalalah (someone whose child loses Kohanic sanctity). However, if he cohabits with her again, he renders her a chalalah.<br />
<br />
If one testifies that his son is a mamzer, and even if both parents say this about a fetus, they are not believed because a man can not testify against himself. But Rabbi Yehudah says that they are believed because a man is believed to say, “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/21-17.htm">This is my first-born son</a>,” and so also about a mamzer.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Child Drinking Milk by Mary Cassatt</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/79.txt
<a id="src-00391"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/79.txt`

Kiddushin 79 -  Agent and Father Find Husband for Daughter
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhwzfIcaUW_OTTg-9LmgP0S_C2BlVzByRQbLa1SZ0RSp5EbM-k4WxgNobeA4WBzbuTQNRF33Wx5NDMkDMqfE0gnLy62XaiMEHQCRzaB_f7QeQUqT6jbG3DUdI3GgFonLEP3JTqK0PZEkHO3/s1600-h/Eug%C3%A8ne+Carri%C3%A8re+-+Alphonse+Daudet+%26+his+Daughter.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5284234302486522322" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhwzfIcaUW_OTTg-9LmgP0S_C2BlVzByRQbLa1SZ0RSp5EbM-k4WxgNobeA4WBzbuTQNRF33Wx5NDMkDMqfE0gnLy62XaiMEHQCRzaB_f7QeQUqT6jbG3DUdI3GgFonLEP3JTqK0PZEkHO3/s320/Eug%C3%A8ne+Carri%C3%A8re+-+Alphonse+Daudet+%26+his+Daughter.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 246px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a>If a minor girl's father commissioned an agent to find a husband for her and accept the betrothal money, and the father himself then went and betrothed her to someone, then if the father's betrothal occurred first, it is valid. If the agent's betrothal occurred first, then it is the one that is valid.<br />
<br />
If it is unknown whose betrothal occurred first, she can only marry another man if both give her  a Get. And if they want, one can give her a Get, and the other can marry her.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Alphonse Daudet &amp; his Daughter by Eugene Carriere</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/8.txt
<a id="src-00392"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/8.txt`

Kiddushin 8 - Betrothal with Valuables
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiuTxdEGqdn1zDhhsuBbqhwjqLy6OvURxXuyiOh75ow77n6KSeMTm_qzugoeMt36RpxOlkZiHm_FOROIJMWFIfX9eyiPPZb7F2dV5bsx-0IfUSGYl4455VkueCXM4GmBu9r0wYMtFOiOb7F/s1600-h/Silks-and-Satins-1900-Posters.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5257941658694177810" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiuTxdEGqdn1zDhhsuBbqhwjqLy6OvURxXuyiOh75ow77n6KSeMTm_qzugoeMt36RpxOlkZiHm_FOROIJMWFIfX9eyiPPZb7F2dV5bsx-0IfUSGYl4455VkueCXM4GmBu9r0wYMtFOiOb7F/s320/Silks-and-Satins-1900-Posters.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">A man betrothed a woman by giving her a quantity of silk. He said, “Become betrothed to me with $2,000, and here is this silk as payment.” The silk was indeed worth $2,000. Does the woman, who is not an appraisal expert, rely on his words and wholeheartedly commit herself to marriage? The prevailing ruling is that she does.<br />
<br />
If a man said to a woman, “Become betrothed to me with $100,” but instead gave her an item as collateral, she is not betrothed. She did not receive the promised money, nor was collateral given as a gift.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;Silks and Satins,&nbsp; 1900 Posters</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/80.txt
<a id="src-00393"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/80.txt`

Kiddushin 80 - Seclusion with a Woman
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1Nu2WcXP5jK1OrOCqpce2ZS6HnIMCGjwX29arMvLaA6ChaVSnK0N99-MhdKfnoBw6MFfz0nY_CXSelHw1gIbWAJ9-yHY7yB9cg3IA1oH7pUFkbS2B0dCrqenAsW1s1Q9Y8Yf1g2CL4tnJ/s1600-h/Titian+-+Portrait+of+Caterina+Cornaro+Wife+of+King+James+II+of+Cyprus.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5284698251752043858" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg1Nu2WcXP5jK1OrOCqpce2ZS6HnIMCGjwX29arMvLaA6ChaVSnK0N99-MhdKfnoBw6MFfz0nY_CXSelHw1gIbWAJ9-yHY7yB9cg3IA1oH7pUFkbS2B0dCrqenAsW1s1Q9Y8Yf1g2CL4tnJ/s320/Titian+-+Portrait+of+Caterina+Cornaro+Wife+of+King+James+II+of+Cyprus.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 240px;" /></a>A man may not be secluded even with two women (and certainly not with one) because a woman may hope that her female companion can be convinced to duplicate her act - following the teaching that women's minds are easily swayed.<br />
<br />
One may be secluded with two women if his wife is present, and he may even sleep in the same room as them in an inn.<br />
<br />
A woman may be secluded with two men if they are of high moral character, but if they aren't, then even with  a group of ten, it is not permitted.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Portrait of Caterina Cornaro, Wife of King James II of Cyprus by Titian</div>

---

### content/kiddushin/81.txt
<a id="src-00394"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/81.txt`

Kiddushin 81 - Don't Scoff at Sinners
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhlZ0BYRbSKiRS2DS3t7mEPWilcHwI2VO1G4ycdND4P7kKd2k54g1EOCV5tBKgPZ9REfI9U0M3HcLEDwp5OEVhHFWmEY23gZw2G4zIF6SVDUEV3_bsNa6f6J3lWmTjQXASuL8OxW9weYxuj/s1600-h/Ridolfo+Ghirlandaio+-+Adoration+Of+The+Shepherds+-+detail-1510.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5285063209894281554" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhlZ0BYRbSKiRS2DS3t7mEPWilcHwI2VO1G4ycdND4P7kKd2k54g1EOCV5tBKgPZ9REfI9U0M3HcLEDwp5OEVhHFWmEY23gZw2G4zIF6SVDUEV3_bsNa6f6J3lWmTjQXASuL8OxW9weYxuj/s320/Ridolfo+Ghirlandaio+-+Adoration+Of+The+Shepherds+-+detail-1510.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 254px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Akiva was accustomed to scoffing at sinners because he felt it was simple to overcome the temptations of the Evil Inclination if only one desired to do so.<br />
<br />
One day Satan appeared to him disguised as a woman, perched atop a palm tree. Rabbi Akiva began to climb to meet "her." When he reached the middle, Satan released him from his grip and said: "Had they not proclaimed in Heaven - 'Be cautious of Rabbi Akiva and his Torah,' - I would have made your life worthless."<br />
<br />
Students of Shmuel were careful not to be alone with an animal, but this is usually not required.</span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;Ridolfo Ghirlandaio - Adoration Of The Shepherds</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/82.txt
<a id="src-00395"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/82.txt`

Kiddushin 82 - Conclusion
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiMOIHERA3Q1hJUVkhOjHxOJ7IiFE1PAdgLp2Bx8mo4fewOj4pTkCH0QFJzoHxhIiceoXQfsc7ZL8hG4uhErJg8l3b91P7kDNVq1gd_VeXioXucghSZ1YHIiEvlQJmnkdgLd_FYmfrd4rFi/s1600-h/Jan+Georg+van+Vliet+-+Bricklayers,-From-A-Series-Depicting-Trades-And-Professions.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5285302574492145218" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiMOIHERA3Q1hJUVkhOjHxOJ7IiFE1PAdgLp2Bx8mo4fewOj4pTkCH0QFJzoHxhIiceoXQfsc7ZL8hG4uhErJg8l3b91P7kDNVq1gd_VeXioXucghSZ1YHIiEvlQJmnkdgLd_FYmfrd4rFi/s320/Jan+Georg+van+Vliet+-+Bricklayers,-From-A-Series-Depicting-Trades-And-Professions.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 253px;" /></a><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Meir says: "One should always teach his son a clean and easy trade, and he should pray to He to Whom all wealth and possessions belong because there is no trade that does not include indigence and wealth. For poverty is not the result of a trade, nor is wealth the result of a trade; rather, all is per one's merit."<br />
<br />
Rabbi Nehorai says: "I put aside every trade in the world, and I teach my son only Torah, for a man benefits from its reward in this world, and the principal remains for him in the World to Come."<br />
<br /><span style="font-style: italic;">The mystical meaning of Kiddushin</span><br />
<br />
The bride is symbolic of Tzedek - righteousness and also of being poor. When given a coin - a prutah - the minimum amount for giving, she symbolizes Tzedakah, charity. She then turns her face to the groom, and this face-to-face meeting, symbolic of God talking to Moses, prepares them for the honor of Chupah.<br /></span><div><span style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: medium;">Art: Bricklayers, From A Series Depicting Trades And Professions by Jan Georg van Vliet</span></div>

---

### content/kiddushin/9.txt
<a id="src-00396"></a>

**Source file:** `content/kiddushin/9.txt`

Kiddushin 9 – Betrothal in earnest
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQapRRiWM2DCkzsnWJc7sZbwGgk4vBJgGxFSriQc2PK6sQrQe16yTTNrvqi8Mjv-V14C8iJLHxsAc5uj_hvPdsPAiD0ZteiXBQZh6AkgcC7Icutoz6IcvPGzwNk3qNfS_qC1KG5cKy1EjR/s1600/Woman+Drinking+with+Sleeping+Soldier+by+Gerard+Ter+Borch.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiQapRRiWM2DCkzsnWJc7sZbwGgk4vBJgGxFSriQc2PK6sQrQe16yTTNrvqi8Mjv-V14C8iJLHxsAc5uj_hvPdsPAiD0ZteiXBQZh6AkgcC7Icutoz6IcvPGzwNk3qNfS_qC1KG5cKy1EjR/s320/Woman+Drinking+with+Sleeping+Soldier+by+Gerard+Ter+Borch.jpg" width="281" /></a>To become betrothed (which is considered like complete marriage, except that a chuppah is needed before the couple begins to live together), the woman has to accept a valuable proffered by the groom and tell him that with this, she agrees to become his bride. Let us look at some marginal cases.
<br />
<br />
If a woman on a cruise takes the betrothal money (a hundred zuz, about $5,000) from the man but immediately throws it overboard the ship, she is not betrothed. But we just said it!? – You might think that – since she would be obligated to return the money if she does not get married – she actually means to accept but tests the husband in his anger management. So the teacher had to tell us that she was not betrothed because she did not voice an agreement.
<br />
<br />
Another example: a man was drinking in a bar, and a woman came over and said, "Give me a drink." He said, "If I do, will you become betrothed to me?" She replied, "Do pour a drink!" – Here, too, she is not betrothed since she agreed to the drink, not the marriage.
<br />
<br />
In addition to money or valuables, a man can betroth a woman with a document, where he writes, "With this document, you become betrothed to me." This is derived from other sales laws, and it applies even if the paper on which it is written is not worth anything. Just like a bill of divorce, this document must be written with her in mind. 
<br />
<br />
Finally, one can engage a woman by having relations with her – provided that he announces to the witnesses that this is his intent and then secludes himself with her. This is derived from the words "<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=22#P5487">who cohabited with her husband</a>."<br />
<br />
Art: Woman Drinking with Sleeping Soldier by Gerard Ter Borch

---

### content/makkot/10.txt
<a id="src-00397"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/10.txt`

Makkot 10 – Arrangements for the Unintentional Killer
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjPwhR9dC3qDHKc6qXGjye9b7gZFVnKN2KCKXSqctAP34h7Kctaen-xedsAec0SAUGpx1tIv0Zs7wnjOcLVCIlSQCeP48nT1FFG3OOIgJIbiHFcUaiXfs_twgMWvaFCPzFgNzIVzlw5gBw/s1600/Isaac+Snowman+-+Three+Rabbis+Of+Jerusalem.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjPwhR9dC3qDHKc6qXGjye9b7gZFVnKN2KCKXSqctAP34h7Kctaen-xedsAec0SAUGpx1tIv0Zs7wnjOcLVCIlSQCeP48nT1FFG3OOIgJIbiHFcUaiXfs_twgMWvaFCPzFgNzIVzlw5gBw/s320/Isaac+Snowman+-+Three+Rabbis+Of+Jerusalem.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The phrase "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/4-42.htm">and he shall flee to one of those cities and live</a>" teaches that we must provide him with arrangements to enable him to live. If he is a student of Torah, we exile his teacher with him, because a student cannot survive without the one who teaches him Torah. From here, we see that  a person should not teach a disciple who is not of good character. Furthermore, if the teacher is exiled, his academy is exiled with him.<br />
<br />
Rav Chama used to say, "If <a href="http://bible.cc/psalms/25-8.htm">God guides sinners on the way</a>,&nbsp; He surely guides the righteous."<br />
<br />
Resh Lakish used to explain the phrase "<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/21-13.htm">but God caused it to come to his hand</a>" with this example. Two people killed a person, one inadvertently, and one intentionally, but there were no witnesses against both. God causes one to sit under a ladder while the other one descends, falls on him, and kills him, this time with witnesses. One is thus executed, and the other is exiled.<br />
<br />
Art: Three Rabbis Of Jerusalem by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Isaac Snowman</span>

---

### content/makkot/11.txt
<a id="src-00398"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/11.txt`

Makkot 11 – Unintentional Killer and the High Priest
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiL0MYcYyVu30yOjaB0oZFKsHn36yV2qqNff4ZknHsEq6kB1EnFjzLWAFXu86btvagsaK863Mx1ClEynZz-QtxvN9xVXuoryIbjo-LQe7n0QCQ7Yf7nBIxIpeJma-lTbr08uB28WGEwTWM/s1600/John+Opie+-+The+Murder+of+Rizzio.JPG" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiL0MYcYyVu30yOjaB0oZFKsHn36yV2qqNff4ZknHsEq6kB1EnFjzLWAFXu86btvagsaK863Mx1ClEynZz-QtxvN9xVXuoryIbjo-LQe7n0QCQ7Yf7nBIxIpeJma-lTbr08uB28WGEwTWM/s320/John+Opie+-+The+Murder+of+Rizzio.JPG" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">An unintentional killer who is exiled to a city of refuge can leave the city and go home upon the High Priest's death. This includes any High Priest: one who was anointed with oil or by wearing special garments, and even one who served temporarily. Rabbi Yehudah says, “Even the High Priest who is anointed for war.” Therefore, the mothers of High Priests would supply the exiles with food and clothing, so that they would not pray for their sons to die.<br />
<br />
One whose sentence was finalized when there was no High Priest, one who accidentally kills a High Priest, or a High Priest who killed – these never leave the city of refuge. <br />
<br />
One may not leave the city of refuge for testimony regarding a mitzvah, a monetary dispute, or capital punishment. Even if all Israel needs him, and he is like the general Yoav, the son of Zeruyah, he never leaves.<br />
<br />
If a killer left the boundary of the city of refuge and the redeemer of the blood found him, Rabbi Yose HaGligli says that it is a mitzvah for the redeemer to kill him. Everybody else is allowed to do so, but Rabbi Akiva says that it is permissible for the redeemer, and everybody else is liable to death for killing him.<br />
<br />
Art: The Murder of Rizzio by John Opie<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/makkot/12.txt
<a id="src-00399"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/12.txt`

Makkot 12 – Life in the City of Refuge
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3Ic7y_-aW8RXu2Bp8gzGjhIWEXngjSObg-3ATBME5i99IOJJgrOgUPOu3FkEPxLwhmz8pOAVvAFnfvBPbN19neXYoZy1vSCUBUcDsAnhWBI9DYjWAjMWw1W55uvw1fMH2FyvPonoyAuQ/s1600/Berthe+Morisot+-+Orange+Tree+Branches.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg3Ic7y_-aW8RXu2Bp8gzGjhIWEXngjSObg-3ATBME5i99IOJJgrOgUPOu3FkEPxLwhmz8pOAVvAFnfvBPbN19neXYoZy1vSCUBUcDsAnhWBI9DYjWAjMWw1W55uvw1fMH2FyvPonoyAuQ/s320/Berthe+Morisot+-+Orange+Tree+Branches.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a tree stands inside a city of refuge, but its branches lean outside, and the killer is clinging to the trunk, the redeemer of the blood may still kill him, because we consider only the branches. Rav Ashi says, "Also the branches," which changes the ruling to say just the opposite: the killer is protected if the tree is inside and he is under the leaves outside.<br />
<br />
If an exiled killer inadvertently killed someone else in that city of refuge where he resides, he is exiled from his neighborhood to a different neighborhood. If a Levite inadvertently killed someone in his home city, he is exiled from his city to another city.<br />
<br />
If a killer was exiled to a city of refuge and the townspeople wanted to honor him, he must tell them, "I am a killer." If they wanted to do it anyway, they were allowed to do so. In the six designated cities of refuge, the killer does not have to pay rent. The other forty-two cities of the Levites also serve as cities of refuge, but the killer who resides there has to pay rent. <br />
<br />
After the killer returns home, Rabbi Meir says that he returns to the position of authority he had occupied previously, but Rabbi Yehudah says that he does not.<br />
<br />
Art: Orange Tree Branches by Berthe Morisot
</span>

---

### content/makkot/13.txt
<a id="src-00400"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/13.txt`

Makkot 13 – When is the Penalty of Lashes Deserved
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEitZy6mn513ujE9-bOb7uH6hnc3mjuWAlUBxPGbAdno9OZIQqKYLreFfoMa0LN6GwOVvQP_N5orL27RJ87RC3OC3QDMoT_Wb3JA_sm20QfEWf7T_7wLRPWO77RBvr19YBi0aZ9T2rxhWX4/s1600/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Two+Rats.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEitZy6mn513ujE9-bOb7uH6hnc3mjuWAlUBxPGbAdno9OZIQqKYLreFfoMa0LN6GwOVvQP_N5orL27RJ87RC3OC3QDMoT_Wb3JA_sm20QfEWf7T_7wLRPWO77RBvr19YBi0aZ9T2rxhWX4/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Two+Rats.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In general, a person is liable to lashes if he transgresses a negative commandment, is warned a short time before his transgression, and verbally accepts the consequences of his actions on himself. The total number of such prohibitions is 207. The following list contains novelty points, for example, even though the ones in the first group carry the penalty of being cut off from the people, and lashes still apply:<br />
<br />
One who cohabits with his sister, aunt, his wife's sister, or a woman who did not immerse herself in a mikveh. A High Priest who cohabits with a widow, or an ordinary kohen who cohabits with a divorcee. A ritually unclean person who eats sacrifices, or one who enters the Temple while unclean. One who eats chametz on Passover, or one who works on Yom Kippur. One who eats meat of any animal that was not slaughtered properly, and one who eats unkosher fish, birds, insects, reptiles, and rodents.<br />
<br />
Art: Two Rats by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Vincent Van Gogh</span>

---

### content/makkot/14.txt
<a id="src-00401"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/14.txt`

Makkot 14 – No Double Punishment for the Same Offense
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9SlD151dO2FuHDSgm2NDpaFPje6xlaLVEGNy3Ln5_vW25drtNs7ratonDBcMg1tQJ3VuWx5QTifTXVBwkHLvZvjE5xrqiTcqlrbikAzITisqKMmtko-whw2a1St9wWQWzGX64T-LHiPs/s1600/John+Singer+Sargent+-+The+Daughters+Of+Edward+Darley+Boit.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9SlD151dO2FuHDSgm2NDpaFPje6xlaLVEGNy3Ln5_vW25drtNs7ratonDBcMg1tQJ3VuWx5QTifTXVBwkHLvZvjE5xrqiTcqlrbikAzITisqKMmtko-whw2a1St9wWQWzGX64T-LHiPs/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+The+Daughters+Of+Edward+Darley+Boit.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Usually, two punishments cannot be administered for one transgression because one is punished "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/25-2.htm">corresponding to his wickedness</a>," but not more. However, Rabbi Yishmael allows both lashes and the death penalty because it is all "one long death."<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yitzchak says that one is cut off for relations with his sister, but does not get lashes. Talking about the laws of incest, the Torah <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/20-17.htm">repeated the prohibition one's sister</a>. There is a rule: "The exception proves the rule." In our case, when incest with one's sister is prohibited yet again, on the pain of being cut off, this teaches that being cut off is the only punishment for it, and one does not get lashes. It also teaches that one does not get lashes for all other similar transgressions.<br />
<br />
The Sages, who disagree with Rabbi Yitzchak, say that the Torah here speaks about someone who fathered two girls with his mother, then a son with one of the girls, and his son then had relations with the other girl, who is the now his sisterfather's's sister, anmother's's sister – such a person gets three sets of lashes.<br />
<br />
Art: The Daughters Of Edward Darley Boit by John Singer Sargent
</span>

---

### content/makkot/15.txt
<a id="src-00402"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/15.txt`

Makkot 15 – Uncertain Warning
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgGMUE4py9d0tI0etVar6JRQeYBja7cp6fhlDbLUuMj4I5DGomC6EVizfUt3Tkr6MNVLM6vATWhOcEr4lsgZAohs-4HbUIhhGtkTQRdX9Xb25EPnaOslXBU8xwKQeo1dliF_eOfXEM9SpE/s1600/Jacobus+Vrel+-+Street+Scene+with+Bakery.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgGMUE4py9d0tI0etVar6JRQeYBja7cp6fhlDbLUuMj4I5DGomC6EVizfUt3Tkr6MNVLM6vATWhOcEr4lsgZAohs-4HbUIhhGtkTQRdX9Xb25EPnaOslXBU8xwKQeo1dliF_eOfXEM9SpE/s320/Jacobus+Vrel+-+Street+Scene+with+Bakery.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">For lashes to be administered, the transgressor must be warned shortly before. In the cases where such a warning cannot be stated with certainty, is the court still allowed to administer lashes?<br />
<br />
For example, one proclaims, "An oath that I will eat this loaf today!" If he is warned in the morning that he had better eat the loaf, or else he will receive lashes, this is an uncertain warning, because he may still eat the loaf later on. This applies throughout the day: he cannot be told with certainty that if he does not eat the loaf now, he will incur lashes, since he can eat it a while later. He could potentially be warned on the very last moment of the day, but it is practically impossible. In this situation, Rabbi Yochanan says that an uncertain warning is legal; however, he does not receive lashes because he does not act. On the contrary, Resh Lakish does allow lashes even for no action, but Resh Lakish considers an uncertain warning invalid. Thus, according to both, he does not receive lashes, but for different reasons.<br />
<br />Art: Street Scene with Bakery by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jacobus Vrel</span>

---

### content/makkot/16.txt
<a id="src-00403"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/16.txt`

Makkot 16 – Remedy for  Transgression
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBimFcyOjbKEb98uj3CEFz9pS7-vUYADHQBYt9uKSy16XZjAQ9jxtd_frTiHy_3TghsS6yMpFVdYlfJ99cVl6ZPcSQS0HihQeOWt_ZJFL_qpzw2m6vKjEp9v5BNeUwoc1eH4Ju5qXKEs0/s1600/J.+Stewart+-+Study+of+different+bees.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiBimFcyOjbKEb98uj3CEFz9pS7-vUYADHQBYt9uKSy16XZjAQ9jxtd_frTiHy_3TghsS6yMpFVdYlfJ99cVl6ZPcSQS0HihQeOWt_ZJFL_qpzw2m6vKjEp9v5BNeUwoc1eH4Ju5qXKEs0/s320/J.+Stewart+-+Study+of+different+bees.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">“<a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/12-10.htm">You shall not leave from the Passover offering until morning, and whatever is left until morning you shall burn with fire</a>” - is an example of a remedy for one's transgression. In this case one is not punished with lashes. Rabbi Yochanan learns from here that had the Torah not provided the remedy,  he would be punished, even though this is an example of an uncertain warning. Thus, one can get lashes with uncertain warning. Resh Lakish learns that had the Torah not provided the remedy, he would be punished, even though the transgression of leaving over involves no action. Thus, one can incur lashes for the prohibition that does not involve action.<br />
<br />
If one ate an ant, he is liable to five separate sets of lashes – two for eating creeping things, and three for land varieties. For a hornet, he is liable to an additional set for creeping things that fly. If one mashed nine ants and then added another live one, and the live one completed the volume of an olive, he is liable to six sets, the last one for an olive's volume of non-kosher meat.<br />
<br />
The same law would apply for mashing one ant the size of an olive, but such ants are rare.<br />
<br />
Art: J. Stewart - Study of different bees<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/makkot/17.txt
<a id="src-00404"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/17.txt`

Makkot 17 – Rava's Adoration of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgDC8PmzBCDOWfKuscR8VjT0W_Flmb8zYIAXiB8zbKsx-N9Gsu9TLNLzpzVxx9om-0ovon9X7mpa8vyKLLprPH1JI6ddG8V08_HSwDFQjwojm6SgPkaVUwP5A35vPd2Mu3nskdMO81j6Yg/s1600/Pieter+the+Elder+Bruegel+-+The+Peasant+and+the+Birdnester.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgDC8PmzBCDOWfKuscR8VjT0W_Flmb8zYIAXiB8zbKsx-N9Gsu9TLNLzpzVxx9om-0ovon9X7mpa8vyKLLprPH1JI6ddG8V08_HSwDFQjwojm6SgPkaVUwP5A35vPd2Mu3nskdMO81j6Yg/s320/Pieter+the+Elder+Bruegel+-+The+Peasant+and+the+Birdnester.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The following also incur lashes: one who <a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/26-1.htm">eats first fruit before its owner recites over them the verses prescribed by the Torah</a>; one who eats the holy offerings outside the Temple, and one who eats less holy offerings outside Jerusalem; and one who breaks a bone of a Passover lamb if it is ritually pure.<br />
<br />
About one who takes a mother bird with her young: Rabbi Yehudah says that he incurs lashes and does not need to send the bird away, but the Sages say that he must send the bird away, and does not incur lashes.<br />
<br /><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">Rabbi Shimon derives through logic the prohibition of eating the first fruit mentioned above by comparing it to&nbsp;<a href="" target="_blank">the first tithe</a>.&nbsp;On this, Rava comments, "A woman who is giving birth to him should pray that she should give birth to one like Rabbi Shimon," and proceeds to refute his logic.</span>&nbsp;If so, why the praise? Because Rabbi Shimon knows how to change the order of words to arrive at what the Torah really meant.<br />
<br />
Art: The Peasant and the Birdnester by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Pieter Brueghel the Elder&nbsp;</span>

---

### content/makkot/18.txt
<a id="src-00405"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/18.txt`

Makkot 18 – Having Capacity is Greater than Doing
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFrJ-FRAa_yr1g1-o8I_qDp6FicPjPFZ6zTGRmuCJ9lUSFLgrdjv0yIPM34dujHTyQ5iUqMrp3eZhbwkZOpOiVUmfZEQzybOZB57p9PqeqcUS4OFupzyhW_Xw9HtjCf1ff6rMYsCgRGWo/s1600/Ignace+Henri+Jean+Fantin-Latour+-+Fruits+and+Flowers+1866.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgFrJ-FRAa_yr1g1-o8I_qDp6FicPjPFZ6zTGRmuCJ9lUSFLgrdjv0yIPM34dujHTyQ5iUqMrp3eZhbwkZOpOiVUmfZEQzybOZB57p9PqeqcUS4OFupzyhW_Xw9HtjCf1ff6rMYsCgRGWo/s320/Ignace+Henri+Jean+Fantin-Latour+-+Fruits+and+Flowers+1866.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Elazar says: "The step of placing the first fruit before the Altar is an essential one, and without it the ritual is not complete and the fruit cannot be eaten. In contrast, reading the verses is not essential and does not invalidate the ritual."<br />
<br />
But did Rabbi Elazar really say this? Didn't he say the opposite in the following ruling: "If one separated first fruit before Sukkot, and Sukkot has passed, and he didn't bring the first fruit, they must be left to rot." Why is this? Isn't it because the owner can no longer say the verses over them? This proves that Rabbi Elazar considers the verses essential!<br />
<br />
The answer is similar to Rabbi Zeira's principle. Rabbi Zeira has said that flour offerings must be mixed, and even if they are not mixed in practice, this does not matter as long as the volume allows it to be mixed. However, if the volume is too large for mixing, the offering is invalid. By the same token, one must be able to say the verses. Not saying them is acceptable, but not being able to say them invalidates the ritual.<br />
<br />
Art: Fruits and Flowers by Ignace Henri Jean Fantin-Latour
</span>

---

### content/makkot/19.txt
<a id="src-00406"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/19.txt`

Makkot 19 – Can One Fulfill the Law of Second Tithe Nowadays?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYhK6qHq2X0Dbwqz1H19SEATxW_QMEM0OSS4VGVW6ZaH4Uv5nBFR__HhYH_TbC2StnVCww7jdKWRYaUZFDYqPBwwBM38p-L717pOtIIxZYb3m6j9ZmowH7MBgnUh5pUrMJLuZDLpfcUVI/s1600/Eug%C3%A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+Sheep+Returning+From+Pasture.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhYhK6qHq2X0Dbwqz1H19SEATxW_QMEM0OSS4VGVW6ZaH4Uv5nBFR__HhYH_TbC2StnVCww7jdKWRYaUZFDYqPBwwBM38p-L717pOtIIxZYb3m6j9ZmowH7MBgnUh5pUrMJLuZDLpfcUVI/s320/Eug%C3%A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+Sheep+Returning+From+Pasture.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Since the Torah directs us to separate the second tithe and eat it in Jerusalem, one might have considered fulfilling this mitzvah even today. <br />
<br />
However, this notion is refuted by comparison with the firstborn animal. The second tithe and the firstborn animals had to be brought to Jerusalem and eaten there. And, just as the firstborn animal can only be offered at the time when the Temple stands – because it needs to be sacrificed at the Altar – so too the second tithe can be eaten in Jerusalem when the Temple stands. <br />
<br />
This argument, however, has an internal weakness: firstborn requires that its blood be placed on the Altar, which is a stringency that the second tithe does not have. Then, how do we know not to bring the second tithe today? Only from the verse, “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/14-23.htm">In the place where He will choose to rest His name – there you will eat second tithe and the firstborn animals</a>.” Since they are placed next to each other in the same verse, they have the same law.<br />
<br />
Art: Sheep Returning From Pasture by Eugene Verboeckhoven -&nbsp;</span>

---

### content/makkot/2.txt
<a id="src-00407"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/2.txt`

Makkot 2 – Marital Disqualifications
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg46C4_DxpTiSzO0EGD9i4hVOhsWhU4pv-10UzKwASs0Q4MsKfKRzi6usL_ZvlxOS3-e5sovXAAeEeCvt5PpqKE4Hyb5r2l814YSexeZ7eLfmrYxfaWqq3IkQ0s3vS7k9zR-JEk8VWnBAE/s1600/Diego+Rodriguez+de+Silva+y+Velazquez+-+Three+Men+at+a+Table.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg46C4_DxpTiSzO0EGD9i4hVOhsWhU4pv-10UzKwASs0Q4MsKfKRzi6usL_ZvlxOS3-e5sovXAAeEeCvt5PpqKE4Hyb5r2l814YSexeZ7eLfmrYxfaWqq3IkQ0s3vS7k9zR-JEk8VWnBAE/s320/Diego+Rodriguez+de+Silva+y+Velazquez+-+Three+Men+at+a+Table.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Two people want to disqualify a Kohen by testifying about the marital status of his parents. They come to court and state the following: "We testify about a certain man (who until now was presumed to be a qualified Kohen), that he is a son of a divorced woman. Later, they are found to be plotting witnesses: two other witnesses came and asked them, "How can you say that you saw this woman being divorced when on that day you were with us in a different place?"<br />
<br />
It is impossible to apply to them what they wanted to inflict on the defendant, even if they are Kohanim. If we disqualify the children of the witnesses, we will violate the commandment of "do to them (but not to their children) what they wanted to do to him." And if we do not disqualify their children, this is not right either because they did want to disqualify the defendant's children. Therefore, they get the punishment of forty lashes instead.<br />
<br />
Art: Three Men at a Table by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Diego Rodriguez de Silva y Velazquez</span>

---

### content/makkot/20.txt
<a id="src-00408"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/20.txt`

Makkot 20 – Other Prohibitions Punishable by Lashes – Cuts for the Dead
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpFGOSkbI7utgGJxt7ewvECYcmC2J2xXMtaVUyFe2CR9YeoAkIsyjBh7QjAEY7bLfaGabE4k9B4kNIbnAWNAKoOmvTWy5ddU-EfWqg_bDWPPyd9LlCbE0BZEldaept08XMx8G6lbnwQSg/s1600/Peter+Paul+Rubens+-+Head+Of+A+Bearded+Man.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjpFGOSkbI7utgGJxt7ewvECYcmC2J2xXMtaVUyFe2CR9YeoAkIsyjBh7QjAEY7bLfaGabE4k9B4kNIbnAWNAKoOmvTWy5ddU-EfWqg_bDWPPyd9LlCbE0BZEldaept08XMx8G6lbnwQSg/s320/Peter+Paul+Rubens+-+Head+Of+A+Bearded+Man.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">These prohibitions include: one who makes a bald spot on his head in mourning for a dead person; one who rounds (shaves off) the corner of his head; one who destroy the corner of his beard with a razor; one who in anguish makes a single cut in his flesh over a deceased person.<br />
<br />
One who makes a single cut  over five dead people, or one who makes five cuts over one dead person, is liable for lashes for each dead person and for each cut.<br />
<br />For rounding the corners of the head, one gets two sets of lashes, one for one side and one for the other.<br />
<br />
For destroying the five corners of the beard, a person is liable to five sets of lashes. Rabbi Eliezer says that if he cut them as one, he deserves only one set. One is not liable unless he shaves his beard with a razor, but Rabbi Eliezer makes him liable even for shaving with planes.<br />
<br />
Art: Head Of A Bearded Man by Peter Paul Rubens<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/makkot/21.txt
<a id="src-00409"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/21.txt`

Makkot 21 – Tattoo; Nazir Who Drinks Wine All Day
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSnk0pk7RU0t8A4imLeDgh2n-RS1RIKnQpK5bWncxaUGMmicKxNwImmlek84og_MUY9ac3M4_eLjHmk5LvrgAY4Xka-tz6dinzg3Is3jL8YilIA7WDZuqBavLhxTU1Wbmx2tYxwas65yo/s1600/Karel+van+III+Mander+-+A+young+man+drinking+from+a+silver+tankard.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSnk0pk7RU0t8A4imLeDgh2n-RS1RIKnQpK5bWncxaUGMmicKxNwImmlek84og_MUY9ac3M4_eLjHmk5LvrgAY4Xka-tz6dinzg3Is3jL8YilIA7WDZuqBavLhxTU1Wbmx2tYxwas65yo/s320/Karel+van+III+Mander+-+A+young+man+drinking+from+a+silver+tankard.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">To be liable for lashes for making a tattoo, one has to perform both steps: puncturing the skin and filling the holes with ink. Rabbi Shimon's opinion is that one is only liable if he tattoos the name of an idol.<br />
<br />
If a nazir was drinking wine all day, he receives only one set of lashes, following the first warning in the morning. If they kept warning him, and he kept drinking, he is liable for each warning. Similarly, if he was in the cemetery all day, he receives one set of lashes, but if they warned him against every entry, he is liable every time. If he was shaving his head all day, he is liable once, but if they warned him about every hair, he is liable every time.<br />
<br />
There is a case where one plows a single furrow and is liable for eight prohibitions: if he plows with an ox and a donkey, and they are consecrated, and he covers mixed species in a vineyard, and he does so on a Sabbatical years and on a Yom Tov; and he is both a Kohen and a nazir, plowing in a cemetery.<br />
<br />
Art: A young man drinking from a silver tankard by Karel van Mander III<br />
<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/makkot/22.txt
<a id="src-00410"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/22.txt`

Makkot 22 – How Are Lashes Administered
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjNwWuNmsiiK_DirPeExpm-bc-GdcFh4xMJYzqj4qa5Pm9r8hG1-sOUf-i9qikFR2ZuDyZjOQCfpHsv3E8uLpWPIZJXnQggJwY59fCMABup3Hn0bQ3NLC-NZu9dCQ5dQxBvSQrnqPnKWrI/s1600/Bartholomeus+Molenaer+-+A+Wife+Beating+her+Husband.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjNwWuNmsiiK_DirPeExpm-bc-GdcFh4xMJYzqj4qa5Pm9r8hG1-sOUf-i9qikFR2ZuDyZjOQCfpHsv3E8uLpWPIZJXnQggJwY59fCMABup3Hn0bQ3NLC-NZu9dCQ5dQxBvSQrnqPnKWrI/s320/Bartholomeus+Molenaer+-+A+Wife+Beating+her+Husband.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The maximum number of lashes that can be given is thirty-nine, because it says "in the number of forty." Rabbi Yehudah says that this means exactly forty. The court assesses how many lashes the transgressor can stand, and chooses a number divisible by three. If in the middle of giving him lashes, he appears weak, they stop the lashes, and he does not have to endure more.<br />
<br />
The attendant of the court binds his hands on either side of the post, grasps his garments, and pulls them away from the area to be lashed, and if they tear, they tear. A stone is placed behind the one being lashed, and the attendant stands on it with the strap in his hand. The whip is made of two calfskin straps with additional straps of donkey hide; the whip's handle is one handbreadth, and the length of it is such that its tip should reach the beginning of the stomach when he is lashed across his back.<br />
<br />
The reader reads appropriate verses to him. If he died as a result of lashing, the attendant  is not liable, but if the attendant gave an extra blow and he died, the attendant goes into exile like all who kill by mistake. If the lashed one lost control of his bodily functions and soiled himself, he is exempt from any further lashes.<br />
<br />
Art: A Wife Beating her Husband by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Bartholomeus Molenaer</span>

---

### content/makkot/23.txt
<a id="src-00411"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/23.txt`

Makkot 23 – The Positive Value of Lashes
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi9Bedg8lRi0CYlqJy3NDpluEjCjwlGb5CYaU2phueerBHFFzihdxzgcMQ800DMxUMl-NzzLo86ZsUkTJsYLoO6vn8mzEmL8zLNzrm1AbLmkGTLPrK9zaoBIp-EB5lD6tLH-Y79EpMTuQc/s1600/David+The+Younger+Teniers+-+The+Happy+Soldier.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi9Bedg8lRi0CYlqJy3NDpluEjCjwlGb5CYaU2phueerBHFFzihdxzgcMQ800DMxUMl-NzzLo86ZsUkTJsYLoO6vn8mzEmL8zLNzrm1AbLmkGTLPrK9zaoBIp-EB5lD6tLH-Y79EpMTuQc/s320/David+The+Younger+Teniers+-+The+Happy+Soldier.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one who is liable to excision (karet) is lashed, he becomes exempt from his excision, following the verse in the Torah, "and your brother will be demeaned before your eyes" - after he has been lashed, he is again like your brother – these are the words of Rabbi Chananyah ben Gamliel.<br />
<br />
Excision (karet) is also translated as being cut off. One opinion is that it entails both the premature death of the sinner and the loss of his future generations. "Premature death" is death at the ages of fifty through fifty-nine, or even at the ages of sixty through seventy-nine if the death is sudden.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Chananya ben Gamliel also said, "If a person who commits a single transgression punishable by being cut off forfeits his life, then if he performs a single mitzvah, how much more so should his life be given to him."<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon says that you can derive this better. The verses say, "My laws by which you shall live... The souls that do incest will be cut off." We see from here that whoever desists and does not do a transgression is given a reward of the one who performs a mitzvah.<br />
<br />
Art: The Happy Soldier by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">David Teniers the Younger</span>

---

### content/makkot/24.txt
<a id="src-00412"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/24.txt`

Makkot 24 – God Created Many Mitzvot in Order to Provide Merit for the Jewish People
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMzpS96nsDWE_hzNne55HtU_Pa7pEYsW9YqNsgZxnHh1pYV4-7T3vtGtwcfvxO45FhyyAbzhFfGysrj1rdWFVD3VfxKMZnWLV9NSV4mDNkBbYZ6gKpcs9IqgU399iG3ksu6XlwT4ju6nM/s1600/John+Everett+Millais+-+North-West+Passage.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMzpS96nsDWE_hzNne55HtU_Pa7pEYsW9YqNsgZxnHh1pYV4-7T3vtGtwcfvxO45FhyyAbzhFfGysrj1rdWFVD3VfxKMZnWLV9NSV4mDNkBbYZ6gKpcs9IqgU399iG3ksu6XlwT4ju6nM/s320/John+Everett+Millais+-+North-West+Passage.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The total number of commandments in the Torah is 613. This can also be seen from the verse “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/33-4.htm">Moses commanded us the Torah as inheritance</a>”. The numerical value of the word Torah is 611, plus the two commandments pronounced by God  Himself make up 613.<br />
<br />
King David established <a href="http://bible.cc/psalms/15-1.htm">11 ethical and moral requirements</a> on which to base the 613. <br />
<br />
Isaiah came and <a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/33-15.htm">established them on six</a>: “Walk with righteousness, speak with fairness, spurn extortionate profit, avoid suspicions of taking a bribe, seal the ears from hearing of bloodshed, and shut the eyes from seeing evil.”<br />
<br />
Michah established them <a href="http://bible.cc/micah/6-8.htm">on three</a>: do justice, love kindness, and walk humbly with your God. <br />
<br />
Habakkuk established them on one: "<a href="http://bible.cc/habakkuk/2-4.htm">The righteous person shall live through his faith</a>".<br />
<br />
Art: North-West Passage by John Everett Millais</span>

---

### content/makkot/3.txt
<a id="src-00413"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/3.txt`

Makkot 3 – False Witnesses About a Divorce
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAo0hnMDJ3TNoCA5cJiSP3z8Mtegk_8Bgqt1Sr4HmGCmPHmw0zDRLEJquaiTUyrRE9WV5TzRwfBJAbX69DYN3_czW9HV-l8pLdEBtdFRdVEdVHGQGJ9-iA_8cGPHRngR7hCVk9xFgoeo8/s1600/French+Unknown+Masters+-+Portrait+of+a+Couple.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAo0hnMDJ3TNoCA5cJiSP3z8Mtegk_8Bgqt1Sr4HmGCmPHmw0zDRLEJquaiTUyrRE9WV5TzRwfBJAbX69DYN3_czW9HV-l8pLdEBtdFRdVEdVHGQGJ9-iA_8cGPHRngR7hCVk9xFgoeo8/s320/French+Unknown+Masters+-+Portrait+of+a+Couple.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Two witnesses said, "We testify about this man that he divorced his wife (that is, gave her a Get) but has not paid her the Ketubah." Later, they were found to be false plotting witnesses.<br />
<br />
In this case, they cannot be made to pay the full value of the Ketubah, which they wanted the husband to lose, because he may have to pay her the Ketubah anyway if he divorces her or dies. Instead, the court estimates the trade value of the Ketubah, that is, how much someone would be willing to pay for that woman's Ketubah, on the understanding that he may not get the payment at all and the false witnesses pay this amount to the husband.<br />
<br />In a similar case, two witnesses said, "This man borrowed money and needs to repay it within thirty days," whereas in reality, the loan term was ten years. If they are found to be false witnesses, they  pay the amount that a person is willing to pay for having the loan in his possession for the extra time, and this is not prohibited interest.<br />
<br />
Art: Portrait of a Couple by French Unknown Masters</span>

---

### content/makkot/4.txt
<a id="src-00414"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/4.txt`

Makkot 4 – The Basic Case of Plotting Witnesses
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjKBQij6KurXBxXbgqVqF8-SzOWJTtnQdvwiAjdhTUMxdrrqCqoyVKWHw2YAtj99Gpx790pFZwtmQ2-OxGrJH44FwVNjzV_aZiFECUiPRIgXt9StZGC59sEfT_N_Fr4wnPAqMw_dRIzbik/s1600/Jean+Charles+Meissonier-+Two+Men+Talking+in+a+Tavern.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjKBQij6KurXBxXbgqVqF8-SzOWJTtnQdvwiAjdhTUMxdrrqCqoyVKWHw2YAtj99Gpx790pFZwtmQ2-OxGrJH44FwVNjzV_aZiFECUiPRIgXt9StZGC59sEfT_N_Fr4wnPAqMw_dRIzbik/s320/Jean+Charles+Meissonier-+Two+Men+Talking+in+a+Tavern.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If two witnesses said, "We testify about this person that he owes his fellow two hundred zuz," and they are found to be false plotting witnesses, they receive lashes for false testimony. They pay their victim the amount they intended to make him lose since lashes and repayment come from different places in the Torah – this is the opinion of Rabbi Meir. The Sages, however, say that whoever pays does not receive lashes since a person cannot be liable for both lashes and monetary payment for the same crime.<br />
<br />
If they said, "We testify about this person that he is liable to forty lashes," and they are found to be false plotting witnesses, they receive eighty lashes – these are the words of Rabbi Meir, but the Sages make them liable to only forty.<br />
<br />
Art: Two Men Talking in a Tavern by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jean Charles Meissonier</span>

---

### content/makkot/5.txt
<a id="src-00415"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/5.txt`

Makkot 5 – The Form of Testimony that Establishes Witnesses as False
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEheifNbl3KL47mCcitw3CaLuO6_iaSyFyw3tvBH0apIFx2qLL3XvqWbitEDGffecirqy5ZPtQxMwv4tmd5C5KRJrCxu3HcN4n6s0PQjUEDlf-TyQNPKQPN-et7YWYim9xOiTnaqnZ0Fkr4/s1600/Egbert+van+Heemskerck+-+Peasants+in+a+Tavern.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEheifNbl3KL47mCcitw3CaLuO6_iaSyFyw3tvBH0apIFx2qLL3XvqWbitEDGffecirqy5ZPtQxMwv4tmd5C5KRJrCxu3HcN4n6s0PQjUEDlf-TyQNPKQPN-et7YWYim9xOiTnaqnZ0Fkr4/s320/Egbert+van+Heemskerck+-+Peasants+in+a+Tavern.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Witnesses do not become plotting false witnesses unless other witnesses discredit them personally. If they said, "How can you testify about a murder when this murder victim, or this alleged murderer, was with us in a different place on that day?" they have attacked the testimony but not the witnesses themselves. However, if the new witnesses said, "How can you testify about this event when you were with us on that day in a different place?" the first witnesses do become plotting false witnesses and are executed on the words of the second set of witnesses.<br />
<br />
Suppose the witnesses are convicted as plotting false witnesses. In that case, they divide the monetary compensation they must pay to the intended victim, but if they are liable to lashes, they each receive their lashes. That is because lashes are comparable to capital punishment, and since there is no execution in half, there are also no lashes in half.<br />
<br />
Art: Peasants in a Tavern by Egbert van Heemskerck
</span>

---

### content/makkot/6.txt
<a id="src-00416"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/6.txt`

Makkot 6 – No Logic Allowed to Derive Capital Punishments
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtHBMpsqhqSdZ-yXkACND6w_7u-LGrsDc6o0hLlk2Qtzh_dGiU6Nm6bfIEn39uL1qk6jSu7T0LAn88DzAdc36l9gaFayedabRz7Q-vk0mb_T98bSN0tpjd4my22E46vHCKdeXeYqndGZ4/s1600/Bernhard+Gutmann+-+Heads+of+Three+Men+and+a+Boy.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhtHBMpsqhqSdZ-yXkACND6w_7u-LGrsDc6o0hLlk2Qtzh_dGiU6Nm6bfIEn39uL1qk6jSu7T0LAn88DzAdc36l9gaFayedabRz7Q-vk0mb_T98bSN0tpjd4my22E46vHCKdeXeYqndGZ4/s320/Bernhard+Gutmann+-+Heads+of+Three+Men+and+a+Boy.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">False plotting witnesses are liable only if the judgment has been pronounced, but the victim has not been executed since the law is "<a href="" target="_blank">do to them as they plotted to do to their brother</a>" and not as they actually did to him.</span>&nbsp;Logic would dictate that if the defendant has been executed, all the more so, the false witnesses should be executed now that they have caused an actual loss of  life. However, there is an overriding rule that one cannot derive capital punishments by logic – only those that are explicitly mentioned in the Torah are to be followed.<br />
<br />
What does the phrase "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-6.htm">by the word of two witnesses or three witnesses shall the one who is to die be put to death</a>" teach? That the law of three witnesses is the same as that of two witnesses: to be established as false plotting witnesses, all three have to be established thus.<br />
<br />
Art: Heads of Three Men and a Boy by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Bernhard Gutmann</span>

---

### content/makkot/7.txt
<a id="src-00417"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/7.txt`

Makkot 7 – Capital Punishment was Infrequent, Laws of Inadvertent Killing
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj7aYOhBPaMRNMF9Q8SYxXBinhsaPjCaV5LnvoWrlmYH9FiFq0mgSZt3HaWVOnNH68_wLrCWbD69aYjWtNJBziZSwLuwfdKwa066rrV2HlR8v9gOGPyl62opYO5ls15ZWNXpzoWf-KQYMo/s1600/Arnold+B%C3%B6cklin+-+The+Isle+of+the+Dead.JPG" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj7aYOhBPaMRNMF9Q8SYxXBinhsaPjCaV5LnvoWrlmYH9FiFq0mgSZt3HaWVOnNH68_wLrCWbD69aYjWtNJBziZSwLuwfdKwa066rrV2HlR8v9gOGPyl62opYO5ls15ZWNXpzoWf-KQYMo/s320/Arnold+B%C3%B6cklin+-+The+Isle+of+the+Dead.JPG" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The phrase "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/17-6.htm">By the word of two witnesses</a>" additionally teaches that the judges must understand the language spoken by witnesses.<br />
<br />
If two witnesses testify that a person was sentenced as a murderer by a particular court and name the time, place, and witnesses in the case, that person is executed based on their words.<br />
<br />
A Sanhedrin that executes once in seven years is called a destroyer. Rabbi Eliezer ben Azariah says, "Once is seventy years." Rabbi Tarfon and Rabbi Akiva say, "Had we been on the Sanhedrin at the time when they still performed executions, no person would ever been executed." Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel says, "They would just increase the number of murderers in Israel" because they would have eliminated the criminals' fear of retribution.<br />
<br />
One who kills a person inadvertently is exiled into a city of refuge. If one was lowering a cask from a roof with the rope and it fell on a bystander and killed him, the killer is exiled, but if he was raising a cask and the cask fell and killed, the killer is not exiled.<br />
<br />
Art: The Isle of the Dead by Arnold Bocklin<br />
<br />
</span>

---

### content/makkot/8.txt
<a id="src-00418"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/8.txt`

Makkot 8 – Negligent, Inadvertent , and Grossly Negligent Killing
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEixaDJHcKOaurlmxbnzHrx7FauWfSQY1CEDDQ0y6jwTSPLrGg__QvbXBN5uUuxhOEahVDt58Jlv5XbgZbvCD0-_gVAjbbiEYngwh7gl74MaWG5shc2kU5U2FvrRVt_fcyezHUiRk33OSRQ/s1600/Childe+Hassam+-+Woodchopper,+1902.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEixaDJHcKOaurlmxbnzHrx7FauWfSQY1CEDDQ0y6jwTSPLrGg__QvbXBN5uUuxhOEahVDt58Jlv5XbgZbvCD0-_gVAjbbiEYngwh7gl74MaWG5shc2kU5U2FvrRVt_fcyezHUiRk33OSRQ/s320/Childe+Hassam+-+Woodchopper,+1902.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A negligent killer runs away to one of the cities of refuge, where he lives in exile until the death of the High Priest. In the city, he is safe, but once outside, the avenger of blood - a close relative of the victim - is allowed to kill him. If the killing was a complete accident, the killer is not punishable at all, but if it was gross negligence, then the city of refuge does not protect him.<br />
<br /><span style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">When one is killed by the "<a href="" target="_blank">wood of the ax</a>", Rabbi Yehudah the Prince understands it as a wood chip, but the Sages say that it means that an axe head slipped off the wooden handle.</span>&nbsp;Therefore, if the victim was killed by the axe-head, Rabbi Yehudah classifies this as gross negligence, when the killer does not go into exile, because it does not help him, but the Sages say that this is precisely the case of the exile. If the death was caused by a woodchip from the tree that is being chopped, then according to Rabbi Yehudah, the killer is exiled, but according to the Sages, he is free from punishment, because the killing was inadvertent.<br />
<br />
Art: Woodchopper by Childe Hassam</span>

---

### content/makkot/9.txt
<a id="src-00419"></a>

**Source file:** `content/makkot/9.txt`

Makkot 9 – Exile for Inadvertent Killing
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhyZ1TPB2C2ixJAtEXuKi74oyIHN7dpX-cYaAX73BHOgyqJg7E1xqNMkzGqkECapxruGlPWTYyP1zodiQO1rnYG38AlhFbEGx-aWogdy_WzX93xdmpzi7j-PZCl8bVi7MhVMexq2bhorlM/s1600/Pieter+the+Elder+Bruegel+-+The+Parable+of+the+Blind+Leading+the+Blind+1568.jsp" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhyZ1TPB2C2ixJAtEXuKi74oyIHN7dpX-cYaAX73BHOgyqJg7E1xqNMkzGqkECapxruGlPWTYyP1zodiQO1rnYG38AlhFbEGx-aWogdy_WzX93xdmpzi7j-PZCl8bVi7MhVMexq2bhorlM/s320/Pieter+the+Elder+Bruegel+-+The+Parable+of+the+Blind+Leading+the+Blind+1568.jsp" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A blind person who killed inadvertently is not exiled, since "<a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/35-23.htm">without seeing</a>"&nbsp;excludes him from responsibility, says Rabbi Yehudah. However, Rabbi Meir says there is another exclusion, "<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/19-4.htm">without awareness</a>," and the double negative becomes affirmative, so a blind inadvertent killer is exiled.<br />
<br />
An "enemy" is one who deliberately avoids speaking to the victim of an "accidental" killing for three days. An "enemy" is not exiled, because he can't claim accidental killing. Rabbi Yose says an "enemy" is considered forewarned and therefore is executed. Rabbi Shimon looks at the circumstances of the case.<br />
<br />
There were three cities of refuge in Transjordan, and three in the land of Canaan. Direct roads were constructed to facilitate getting to a city of refuge. The court would provide the accidental killer with two Torah scholars, and they would try to dissuade the avenging relative from wishing to attack.  Then the court would bring him from the city of refuge and determine the degree of his responsibility.<br />
<br />
Art: The Parable of the Blind Leading the Blind by Pieter Brueghel the Elder&nbsp;</span>

---

### content/megillah/10.txt
<a id="src-00420"></a>

**Source file:** `content/megillah/10.txt`

Megillah 10 - Can one build a private altar and bring sacrifices?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhWtT7hRGuVeKROdt9JgiO1fqnSu0uxkLUw_-eedSvLQoe4_WZNVnLGmugbSmbLvflRQNDaITABmEOeyiSZzXl71HfKHpVU4VjsALXZLYUEdCCqW-nisXapk35xC1BFarRI1lbr9wYByRZkc6LeUMx57d-Q7rpTLForeCS2PQCg499Yyucjje5Dpxwguw=s930" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="709" data-original-width="930" height="244" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhWtT7hRGuVeKROdt9JgiO1fqnSu0uxkLUw_-eedSvLQoe4_WZNVnLGmugbSmbLvflRQNDaITABmEOeyiSZzXl71HfKHpVU4VjsALXZLYUEdCCqW-nisXapk35xC1BFarRI1lbr9wYByRZkc6LeUMx57d-Q7rpTLForeCS2PQCg499Yyucjje5Dpxwguw=s320" width="320" /></a></div>During some periods of Jewish history, one was allowed to build his personal altar and bring sacrifices on it. At other times, personal altars were forbidden.<p></p><p>During the forty years of travel in the wilderness, the Tabernacle had its Altar, and the sacrifices could be brought only on it and not on personal ones. Then, during the fourteen years of conquering Israel, the Tabernacle was in Gilgal. It was temporary, and although sacrifices continued there, personal altars were also allowed. This situation changed a few times until the Temple was built in Jerusalem. After that, personal altars became forbidden for all times.&nbsp;</p><p>In the Temple, they have placed the Ark that was initially constructed under the direction of Moses. That Ark had no physical dimensions. If one measured from one side of the Ark to the wall of the Holy of Holies, he got ten amot. If he measured from the other side of the Ark to the opposite wall, he also got ten amot. And yet, the distance between the opposing walls of the Holy of Holies was only twenty amot total. That proves that the Ark itself miraculously took no space.</p><p>Art: The Israelites Gathering Manna in the Wilderness by Jacob Willemsz. de Wet</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/megillah/11.txt
<a id="src-00421"></a>

**Source file:** `content/megillah/11.txt`

Megillah 11 - Computational mistake
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjFuRZ5lpLC9WhBJ13m8HM9GVcIMAFKEO4qErbnYPUkFAbond3QbPNanB04aEBEkdf4ALic0RUG0yjt-Y3YtVcyLhSQaXqKgTjSmSAQ5wXJAkzhlJe8unquVW-jvwTYKkwJ26pF0xXVLgfiovpp-gk-JubmCW1uiE5olN9fpFO9kj1xw1tZcdNPKQJcjg=s563" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="434" data-original-width="563" height="247" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjFuRZ5lpLC9WhBJ13m8HM9GVcIMAFKEO4qErbnYPUkFAbond3QbPNanB04aEBEkdf4ALic0RUG0yjt-Y3YtVcyLhSQaXqKgTjSmSAQ5wXJAkzhlJe8unquVW-jvwTYKkwJ26pF0xXVLgfiovpp-gk-JubmCW1uiE5olN9fpFO9kj1xw1tZcdNPKQJcjg=s320" width="320" /></a></div>The Megillah starts with a description of a <a href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt3301.htm" target="_blank">great feast thrown by King Ahashverosh</a>. What exactly was celebrated? - that God has abandoned the Jews and will no longer redeem them.<div><br /></div><div>As predicted by Jeremiah, <a href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt1129.htm" target="_blank">Jews would be redeemed from Babylon and returned to Israel after seventy years</a>. Now, Ahashverosh made this claim: "My predecessor, Belshazzar, made the calculation but made a mistake; however, I will not make a mistake." The Talmud describes Belshazzar's calculation, how he celebrated, and how he got punished.</div><div><br /></div><div>Ahashverosh sought to correct the previous mistake, and based on the analysis of the writing, he started counting seventy years from a different historical event. However, he celebrated in the same manner by using the Jerusalem Temple's vessels at the banquet. This started the chain of events that the Megillah describes, including the killing of Ahashverosh's wife, Vashti, who was the daughter of Belshazzar.</div><div><br /></div><div>But Ahashveroshes's calculations seemed correct!? - He should have started from the year of the destruction of the Temple.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Frans Francken Belshazzar Feast<br /><div><br /></div><div><br /></div></div>

---

### content/megillah/12.txt
<a id="src-00422"></a>

**Source file:** `content/megillah/12.txt`

Megillah 12 – Explanation of the Megillah
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRT0LsifTr3HiDKk5gso1d-5xlOH3L5VJA3JMhtxYzCRagGesBgqYKtfmc7h6gAUGIKEDUKmn_S7BOqy23U62xqIlsO_2JY_aWeQrl7oZwDSeypP7S1czP7ECvBSJ3aZNVyDMyKSpqBE9C/s1600/The+Arrival+Of+The+Guests+by+Georges+Jules+Victor+Clairin.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="198" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjRT0LsifTr3HiDKk5gso1d-5xlOH3L5VJA3JMhtxYzCRagGesBgqYKtfmc7h6gAUGIKEDUKmn_S7BOqy23U62xqIlsO_2JY_aWeQrl7oZwDSeypP7S1czP7ECvBSJ3aZNVyDMyKSpqBE9C/s1600/The+Arrival+Of+The+Guests+by+Georges+Jules+Victor+Clairin.jpg" width="320" /></a>What does it mean that king Ahashverosh displayed "<a href="http://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt3301.htm">the riches of his glorious kingdom</a>?" – that he put on the garments of the High Priest, about which it also says "glory."
<br />
<br />
Why did Ahashverosh invite the subjects from distant lands first? Some say that he was clever – the people of his own capital city Shushan he could appease any time. Others say that he was stupid: he should have invited his closest people first, and they would have protected him in case of rebellion.
<br />
<br />
The students of Rabbi Shimon ben Yochai asked him, "Why were the 'enemies of Israel' (euphemism for the Jewish people) on the brink of extinction?"  He said, "You say the reason." They answered, "Because they ate at the feast of Ahashverosh." He questioned, "If so, only the people in Shushan should have been punished." They then asked, "And what is your reason?" Rabbi Shimon told them, "Because they bowed down to an idol." The students then asked, "If so, they should not avoid punishment!" He told them, "They did not mean it and lacked conviction. So too, God did not mean it and only scared them."
<br />
<br />
What does it mean, "On the seventh day, the king's heart was merry with wine." And before it was not? – However, this was Shabbat, when people relaxed. When the Sages relax, they discuss knowledge and praise God. But his guests, when relaxed, started discussing which women, Persian or Midian, were the most beautiful. This led the king to tell them that his wife Vashti was from the nation of Chaldeans and was the most beautiful. They asked to see her in the crown but nothing else, but she would not come. Why would not she? Because the angel Gavriel came and made her grow a tail.
<br />
<br />
Art: The Arrival Of The Guests by Georges Jules Victor Clairin

---

### content/megillah/13.txt
<a id="src-00423"></a>

**Source file:** `content/megillah/13.txt`

Megillah 13 - What's in a name?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh1wvlwd6yBZQZG5BbJfu_pK4uqy4PkZu8TEIa5n4RsK9jrui-cYo3x02Z9njjg81EEWbLt7u1VOyO8g7PxWrp_6Y1y-KRwgFMMV-2Oe5lb-uEBkwCuqup9VVq_gW1zg2C0c9dqQc1t05QoZKXjecLCfFYcAH6-dHTV-bnAd1Z-3ZnVS492EfdrsqQhgQ=s914" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="914" data-original-width="800" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh1wvlwd6yBZQZG5BbJfu_pK4uqy4PkZu8TEIa5n4RsK9jrui-cYo3x02Z9njjg81EEWbLt7u1VOyO8g7PxWrp_6Y1y-KRwgFMMV-2Oe5lb-uEBkwCuqup9VVq_gW1zg2C0c9dqQc1t05QoZKXjecLCfFYcAH6-dHTV-bnAd1Z-3ZnVS492EfdrsqQhgQ=s320" width="280" /></a></div>The names influence their bearer. Esther had another name, Hadassah (myrtle), because she was righteous. Righteous are compared to myrtle. "Esther" means "to hide" because she did not tell anybody of her Jewish origins, as Mordechai had instructed her.<p></p><p>Esther was a complete orphan. Her father died before her birth, and her mother died while giving birth. Mordechai, her uncle, raised her as his daughter. The word "bat" - "daughter" hints at "bait" - "house." When Esther grew up, Mordechai took her as his wife, usually referred to as house.&nbsp;</p><p>Esther knew the rule that idleness acts negatively on the person's psyche. She was industrious on weekdays and did not work on Shabbat. Esther had seven maids. Since the maids would come for only one day a week, they did not notice that her behavior on Shabbat was different from weekdays and did not figure out that she was Jewish.</p><p>"<a href="https://mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt3302.htm" target="_blank">And the king loved Esther more than all the women, and she won more grace than all the other virgins</a>." This tells us that the king experienced the taste of a virgin in Esther. He could also experience the taste of a non-virgin, at will.</p><p>Two servants of Achashverosh - Bigtan and Teresh - complained between themselves. "Since the day that woman came, we never had a good night's sleep."&nbsp; They had to bring drinks to the king all night long. They decided to poison the king. They spoke a rare language of <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=10#C117" target="_blank">Tarshish</a> between themselves. However, they did not know that Mordechai knew that language. In fact, as a member of the Sanhedrin, he had to be fluent in seventy languages. Mordechai reported the plot to Esther. In this way, he saved the king.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;Mistress and Maid&nbsp; by Johannes Vermeer</p>
